Julia Child - French collection

July 28, 2025

acme_bread_couronne.txt - Acme Bread Couronne

Objectives

  • Learn to make a sourdough couronne using the Acme Bakery method
  • Understand the importance of using stages and starters for sourdough bread
  • Master the techniques of shaping and decorating a couronne

Ingredients

  • 1 small piece of old dough (about the size of a walnut)
  • Less than 1/4 cup of warm water (blood temperature)
  • Less than 1 cup of all-purpose flour (unbleached)
  • 1/4 cup of warm water
  • A little over 3 ounces of all-purpose flour
  • Just under 1/2 teaspoon of yeast
  • 1 pound of all-purpose flour
  • Just under 3 teaspoons of salt (1 tablespoon)
  • 5 ounces of dough (for decoration)
  • 12 ounces of water (about 1 1/2 cups)
  • A little bit of neutral oil (light olive oil or cottonseed oil)
  • A small container of rice flour (white or brown)
  • A dowel

Instructions

  1. Chop the old dough into small pieces, about the size of a small walnut.
  2. Add just under a quarter cup of warm water to the dough and mix well.
  3. Gradually add less than a cup of all-purpose flour, mixing until a stiff ball of dough forms.
  4. Let the dough ferment for about eight hours at a slightly warmer temperature than room temperature.
  5. After eight hours, add a full quarter cup of water to the dough and mix well.
  6. Gradually add a little over 3 ounces of all-purpose flour, mixing until the dough is smooth.
  7. Let the dough ferment for about four hours.
  8. In a separate bowl, combine a full quarter cup of water, just under half a teaspoon of yeast, and the starter dough.
  9. Gradually add 1 pound of all-purpose flour, mixing until the dough is well incorporated.
  10. Add just under 3 teaspoons of salt (1 tablespoon) to the dough and mix until the salt is dissolved.
  11. Allow the dough to rise for about an hour and a half in a warm place (80-85 degrees Fahrenheit).
  12. Gently fold the dough over on itself about four times to redistribute the yeast.
  13. Allow the dough to rise for another 45 minutes.
  14. Separate a 5-ounce piece of dough for decoration.
  15. Stretch the decoration dough into a long string, similar to making a baguette.
  16. Form the remaining dough into a loose round, turning the outside edge into the center until a ball is formed.
  17. Use your elbow to create a hole in the center of the dough, forming a doughnut shape.
  18. Let the dough rest for 10-15 minutes.
  19. Stretch the dough out to its full length.
  20. Let the dough rest for 3-4 minutes.
  21. Pinch the decoration dough into small pearls, working from one end to the other.
  22. Place the couronne dough in a floured basket.
  23. Arrange the pearls around the outside of the couronne dough.
  24. Allow the couronne to rise for about an hour and a half.
  25. Preheat the oven to 450 degrees Fahrenheit.
  26. Place the wheat stalk dough on a tray lined with cloth, seam side up.
  27. Form a slight pleat in the dough to keep it in shape.
  28. Allow the dough to rise for its final rising before baking.
  29. Place the pain fendu dough on a tray, seam side down.
  30. Roll the pain fendu dough in rice flour.
  31. Flip the dough over, seam side up.
  32. Using a dowel, press rice flour into the sections of the dough that will be against each other.
  33. Split the dough with the dowel, pressing more rice flour into the sections as you split.
  34. Turn the dough over, seam side down.
  35. Allow the pain fendu to rise for about an hour and a half.
  36. Once the dough has risen, place it on a peel dusted with rice flour.
  37. Carefully flip the dough onto a hot baking stone or sheet pan.
  38. Bake the bread for 20 minutes at 450 degrees Fahrenheit.
  39. After 20 minutes, turn the oven down to 425 degrees Fahrenheit and continue baking until the bread is golden brown.
  40. Enjoy your freshly baked Acme Bread Couronne!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-tHcxF9QvlU

apple_charlotte.txt - Charlotte aux Pommes

Objectives

  • Learn to make a French apple charlotte dessert.
  • Understand the importance of using crisp, flavorful apples.
  • Master the art of unmolding a charlotte.

Ingredients

  • 5-6 quarts apples (Red Gravensteins recommended)
  • 2 tablespoons lemon juice
  • 3-4 tablespoons sugar
  • 1/2 cup apricot preserves
  • 1 cup sugar
  • 1/4 cup dark Jamaican rum
  • 2 teaspoons vanilla extract
  • 3 tablespoons butter
  • White bread (thin-sliced sandwich bread)
  • Clarified butter

Instructions

  1. Slice 5-6 quarts of apples and toss with 2 tablespoons of lemon juice and 3-4 tablespoons of sugar.
  2. Cook apples in a heavy pot over moderate heat for 10-15 minutes until soft, stirring occasionally.
  3. Push apricot preserves through a sieve to remove any pieces of peel.
  4. Add the apricot preserves, 1 cup of sugar, 1/4 cup of rum, 2 teaspoons of vanilla extract, and 3 tablespoons of melted butter to the cooked apples.
  5. Cook the apple mixture for 30-40 minutes until it becomes a thick marmalade, stirring occasionally.
  6. Cut the crusts off of the white bread and line the bottom of a 6-cup baking dish with bread strips.
  7. Sauté the bread strips in clarified butter until lightly browned.
  8. Dip additional bread strips in melted clarified butter and arrange them around the sides of the baking dish, slightly overlapping.
  9. Fill the baking dish with the apple marmalade, pushing the bread against the sides to ensure it's full.
  10. Add a few more bread strips about a third of the way up the mold.
  11. Top with additional bread strips to create a base.
  12. Brush the sides of the mold with melted clarified butter.
  13. Bake in a preheated 425-degree oven for 30-40 minutes, placing a baking pan on the rack below to catch any butter drippings.
  14. Let the charlotte rest for at least 30 minutes to allow the apple puree to settle.
  15. Run a knife around the sides of the mold to loosen the bread strips.
  16. Invert the charlotte onto a plate and carefully lift the mold.
  17. Glaze the charlotte with sieved apricot preserves boiled down with 2 tablespoons of sugar.
  18. Serve warm or cold with cream, custard sauce, champagne, Sauternes, or coffee.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yqwn-ArodFU

apple_pie.txt - American Apple Pie

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic American apple pie with a flaky crust.
  • Understand the importance of using cold butter and water for the crust.
  • Discover the secrets to a perfect apple pie filling.

Ingredients

Crust - 2 1/2 cups all-purpose flour - 1 teaspoon sugar - 1/4 teaspoon salt - 2 sticks (1/2 pound) cold unsalted butter, cut into small cubes - 6 tablespoons cold water

Filling - 6 Empire apples, peeled, cored, and cut into 1/3-inch chunks - 1/2 cup sugar - 1 teaspoon ground cinnamon - 1 pinch allspice - 2 tablespoons tapioca flour - 1 beaten egg white - 2 tablespoons butter - 1 teaspoon sugar

Instructions

  1. In a large bowl, combine 2 1/2 cups of all-purpose flour, 1 teaspoon of sugar, and 1/4 teaspoon of salt.
  2. Cut the cold unsalted butter into small cubes and toss with the flour mixture to coat.
  3. Roll the butter and flour mixture with a rolling pin until the butter is evenly distributed in sheets.
  4. Add 6 tablespoons of cold water to the bowl and mix with a bench scraper, turning the dough over to ensure all the liquid is absorbed.
  5. Roll the dough on a floured surface, folding it over several times, until it is smooth and pliable.
  6. Refrigerate the dough for 10-15 minutes until it firms up.
  7. Cut the dough in half and shape each half into a circle.
  8. Roll out one half of the dough to about 1/8-inch thickness and place it in a pie pan.
  9. Prepare the apple filling by combining 1/2 cup of sugar, 1 teaspoon of ground cinnamon, 1 pinch of allspice, and 2 tablespoons of tapioca flour in a bowl.
  10. Add the prepared apple chunks to the bowl and toss to coat.
  11. Pour the apple filling into the pie pan.
  12. Brush the edge of the bottom crust with beaten egg white.
  13. Roll out the second half of the dough and place it on top of the apple filling.
  14. Trim the edges of the crust and fold the overhang over the lip of the pie pan.
  15. Flute the edges of the crust using your thumb and index finger.
  16. Brush the top crust with beaten egg white and sprinkle with 1 teaspoon of sugar.
  17. Cut 4 slits in the top crust to allow steam to escape.
  18. Bake the pie in a preheated 425° oven for 10 minutes.
  19. Reduce the oven temperature to 375° and continue baking for another 50 minutes.
  20. Let the pie cool for 1 hour before slicing and serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TMgPghHQvPE

apples_alaska_spaghetti_marco_polo.txt - Apples Alaska and Spaghetti Marco Polo

Objectives

  • Learn to make Apples Alaska with a flamed meringue
  • Prepare a unique, uncooked spaghetti sauce with walnuts, olives, and pimientos
  • Learn how to cook spaghetti al dente

Ingredients

Apples Alaska - 4 Golden Delicious apples - Lemon juice - 1/2 cup vermouth or dry white wine - 1/3 cup sugar - 1 teaspoon butter per apple - Nesselrode (glacéed fruits, sugar syrup, rum, marron) - 2 egg whites - 1/3 cup sugar - 1/4 teaspoon vanilla - Pound cake or croutons of white bread - Clarified butter - Strained apricot jam

Spaghetti Marco Polo - 1 pound spaghetti - Salt - Olive oil - Garlic - 2/3 cup chopped walnuts - 1/2 cup chopped black olives - 1/2 cup chopped red pimientos - 1/3 cup chopped parsley - 1 teaspoon fresh basil - Salt and pepper - Parmesan cheese

Instructions

  1. Core the apples by aiming the corer directly from one end to the other.
  2. Peel the apples and rub them with lemon juice to prevent darkening.
  3. Squeeze lemon juice down through the core of each apple.
  4. Place the apples in a heavily buttered dish.
  5. Cut thin slices of apple peel and add them to the dish.
  6. Fill the apples with Nesselrode.
  7. Add 1/2 cup of vermouth or dry white wine, 1/3 cup of sugar, and 1 teaspoon of butter to the dish.
  8. Bake the apples in a 350-degree oven for 30-40 minutes, basting with the buttery juices every 15 minutes.
  9. Test the apples with a knife to ensure they are tender but not overcooked.
  10. While the apples are baking, toast pound cake or sauté croutons in clarified butter.
  11. Spread a thin layer of strained apricot jam on the toasted pound cake or croutons.
  12. Beat 2 egg whites until stiff peaks form.
  13. Gradually beat in 1/3 cup of sugar and 1/4 teaspoon of vanilla.
  14. Place the apples on the prepared pound cake or croutons.
  15. Top the apples with the meringue, leaving a small space around the opening.
  16. Bake the apples in a 500-degree oven for 2 minutes, or until lightly browned.
  17. While the apples are baking, prepare the sauce by combining the apple juices with the apricot jam.
  18. Bring the sauce to a boil, stirring until well combined.
  19. Taste the sauce and adjust seasonings as needed.
  20. Cook the spaghetti in boiling salted water until al dente.
  21. Drain the spaghetti and toss it with olive oil and garlic.
  22. Season the spaghetti with salt and pepper.
  23. Combine the chopped walnuts, black olives, red pimientos, parsley, basil, salt, and pepper to make the spaghetti sauce.
  24. Serve the spaghetti on a platter, tossing it with the sauce.
  25. Garnish with Parmesan cheese.
  26. Flame the Apples Alaska with bourbon whiskey and serve with the sauce.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=btnNyq6AM4c

artichoke_lobster_duck.txt - Artichokes, Lobster & Designer Duck

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare artichokes for a first course.
  • Master the art of separating and cooking duck breast and legs.
  • Create a delicious duck mousse and learn how to cook duck burgers.
  • Discover the secrets of making a lemon-flavored pastry cream and meringue.
  • Explore the world of wine pairing with a renowned winemaker.

Ingredients

Artichokes

  • Artichokes
  • Lemon
  • Flour
  • Water
  • Lemon juice
  • Salt

Lobster

  • Lobster tails
  • Vinaigrette
  • Shallots
  • Mustard
  • Olive oil
  • Salt
  • Pepper

Duck

  • Duck
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Powdered allspice
  • Thyme
  • Heavy cream
  • Cooked minced onions

Dessert

  • Lemon
  • Sugar
  • Egg yolks
  • Flour
  • Milk
  • Vanilla
  • Strawberries
  • Egg whites
  • Cream of tartar

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Artichokes
  2. Cut the stem of the artichoke close to the bottom.
  3. Remove any leaves on the bottom.
  4. Bend back and pull off each leaf to remove the edible portion.
  5. Cut off the top cone of leaves.
  6. Remove the choke from the center.
  7. Rub the artichoke with lemon frequently to prevent discoloration.
  8. Carefully cut down the green part until you reach the tender, yellow part.
  9. Place the prepared artichoke bottoms in a "blanc" solution of flour, water, lemon juice, and salt.
  10. Simmer for 30 minutes until tender.
  11. Remove the choke with a teaspoon.
  12. Wash the artichoke bottom again to remove any fuzz.
  13. Slice the artichoke bottom on the diagonal with a thin knife.

  14. Marinate the slices in a lemon-based vinaigrette for 10-15 minutes.

  15. Prepare the Lobster

  16. Twist the lobster tail to separate it from the body.
  17. Break off the feelers.
  18. Push the meat out of the tail with your finger.
  19. Remove the small end of the tail.

  20. Slice the tail meat into thin medallions.

  21. Prepare the Duck

  22. Slit the duck skin down the back from neck to tail.
  23. Remove the wings close to the breast.
  24. Cut the legs down to the backbone and up, slitting the skin.
  25. Bend the legs back to break open the joints.
  26. Cut off any extra skin on the breast.
  27. Remove the wishbone.
  28. Lift the skin up off the breast on either side.
  29. Season the breast with salt, pepper, allspice, and thyme.
  30. Fold the skin back over the breast.
  31. Remove the skin and bones from the legs and wings.
  32. Combine the duck meat from the legs and wings with any other duck meat.
  33. Blend the duck meat with heavy cream, salt, allspice, thyme, and pepper in a food processor.
  34. Add half a cup of cooked minced onions to the mixture.

  35. Shape the duck mixture into small burger-like drumsticks.

  36. Cook the Duck

  37. Preheat oven to 425 degrees Fahrenheit.
  38. Roast the duck breasts for 20 minutes until rare.
  39. Let the breasts cool slightly.
  40. Slice the breast meat off and lay it in a buttered pan with shallots.
  41. Dice the duck skin and place it in a roasting pan.
  42. Roast the skin in a 250-degree oven for 1 1/2 hours to make cracklings.
  43. Sauté the duck burgers over low heat for 20 minutes, 10 minutes per side.
  44. Reheat the duck breast meat in a pan with port or Madeira wine, duck stock, salt, and pepper.
  45. Reduce the cooking liquid from the breast meat to a syrup.
  46. Drizzle the sauce over the duck breast meat.

  47. Serve the duck breast meat with cracklings and fresh vegetables.

  48. Prepare the Dessert

  49. Grate the zest of a lemon.
  50. Juice the lemon.
  51. Beat together 6 tablespoons of sugar and 3 egg yolks until they form a ribbon.
  52. Add 3 tablespoons of flour to the egg yolk mixture and mix well.
  53. Bring milk to a boil and add vanilla.
  54. Add a small amount of hot milk to the egg yolk mixture to loosen it.
  55. Pour the egg yolk mixture into the boiling milk and cook until thickened.
  56. Add the lemon zest and juice to the pastry cream and cook until thickened.
  57. Transfer the pastry cream to a bowl and set it in a bowl of ice water to cool.
  58. Blend together 3 cups of strawberries and 3/4 cup of sugar until smooth.
  59. Beat 6 egg whites with a pinch of salt until frothy.
  60. Add cream of tartar to the egg whites and beat until stiff peaks form.
  61. Gradually add 9 tablespoons of sugar to the egg whites and beat until shiny.
  62. Fold some of the meringue into the pastry cream to loosen it.
  63. Fold the pastry cream mixture back into the bowl of meringue.
  64. Stuff the crepe with the meringue mixture.
  65. Fold the crepe in half.

  66. Bake the crepe at 500 degrees Fahrenheit for 6-7 minutes.

  67. Wine Pairing

  68. Pair the hors d'oeuvres with a white zinfandel.
  69. Pair the artichokes and lobster with a light vintage Paso Robles zinfandel.
  70. Pair the duck with a Monte Bello cabernet sauvignon.
  71. Pair the dessert with a sweet, naturally sweet zinfandel.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2iwc_RZGZ8I

artichoke_prep.txt - Artichokes: From Top to Bottom

Objectives

  • Learn how to properly prepare and cook whole artichokes.
  • Discover the different edible parts of an artichoke.
  • Explore various ways to serve and eat artichokes, including as a first course or side dish.

Ingredients

  • 1 artichoke (4.5 inches in diameter)
  • 1.5 tablespoons salt
  • 1 piece of cheesecloth
  • 1 lemon
  • 2 cups water
  • 1.5 tablespoons flour
  • 1 tablespoon lemon juice
  • 3/4 teaspoon salt
  • 1 poached egg
  • 1/4 cup sauce Mornay (cream sauce with cheese)
  • 1/4 cup mayonnaise
  • Parsley (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Wash the artichoke under running water, gently spreading the leaves apart.
  2. Break off the stem, as fibers between the stem and heart might go up through the heart.
  3. Shave the bottom of the artichoke to make it sit nicely when served.
  4. Break off any old, cracked, or small bottom leaves.
  5. Even off the bottom of the artichoke with a knife.
  6. Cut off the pointed and prickly ends of the leaves with shears.
  7. Rub the cut portions of the artichoke with lemon to prevent discoloration.
  8. Fill a large pot with boiling water and add 1.5 tablespoons of salt per quart of water.
  9. Place the artichoke in the boiling water, ensuring the water covers it.
  10. Drape a damp piece of cheesecloth over the artichoke to siphon water up over the top.
  11. Boil the artichoke uncovered for about 30 minutes (or 20-25 minutes for smaller ones).
  12. Check for doneness by poking a sharp knife into the bottom; if it goes in easily, it's done.
  13. Serve the artichoke hot, cold, or warm.
  14. To remove the choke (the hairy part in the center), gently spread the leaves apart after cooking.
  15. Remove the choke with a spoon, being careful not to overcook the artichoke.
  16. Push the leaves back together and add sauce to the heart if desired.
  17. To prepare artichoke bottoms, break off the stem and leaves to about halfway up.
  18. Cut off the bottom of the artichoke heart where the choke begins.
  19. Rub the cut portions with lemon to prevent darkening.
  20. Shave off any green parts on the artichoke heart to ensure it's edible.
  21. Drop the artichoke hearts into acidulated water (1 quart water, 2 tablespoons lemon juice) as they're done.
  22. Cook the artichoke hearts in a white (blanc) - a mixture of flour, water, lemon juice, and salt.
  23. Simmer the artichoke hearts in the blanc for 20-30 minutes, uncovered.
  24. Remove the choke from the cooked artichoke heart with a spoon or grapefruit knife.
  25. Rinse the artichoke heart to remove any flour.
  26. To reheat the artichoke heart, place it upside down in a buttered baking dish, salt and pepper it, cover with wax paper, and bake at 325 degrees Fahrenheit for 5-10 minutes.
  27. To serve the artichoke heart, fill it with sauce (such as béarnaise) and top with a poached egg.
  28. Garnish with parsley.
  29. To eat an artichoke, remove each leaf, dip it in butter or vinaigrette, and eat the bottom part.
  30. Continue eating the leaves, placing them on the side of your plate.
  31. When you reach the heart, push through the cone of leaves with a fork and pull it off.
  32. Dip the edible part of the cone in sauce and eat it.
  33. Remove the remaining tiny cone of leaves covering the choke.
  34. Cut the bottom of the artichoke in half, then in half again, and remove the choke.
  35. Enjoy the edible bottom of the artichoke.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Le-5_bP5HM8

artichoke_recipe.txt - Artichokes: From Top to Bottom

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare and cook whole artichokes
  • Understand the different edible parts of an artichoke
  • Explore various ways to serve and eat artichokes

Ingredients

  • 1 artichoke
  • 1 tablespoon of salt
  • 1 tablespoon and a half of salt (for boiling water)
  • 1 piece of lemon
  • 1 piece of cheesecloth
  • 2 cups of water
  • 1 tablespoon and a half of flour
  • 1 tablespoon of lemon juice
  • 3/4 teaspoon of salt
  • 1 poached egg
  • 1/4 cup of sauce Mornay
  • 1/4 cup of mayonnaise
  • 1/4 cup of béarnaise sauce (optional)
  • 1/4 cup of creamed seafood (optional)
  • 1/4 cup of French dressing (optional)
  • 1/4 cup of hot sauce (optional)
  • 1/4 cup of butter (optional)
  • 1/4 cup of melted butter or vinaigrette (for dipping)
  • Parsley (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Wash the artichoke under running water, spreading the leaves apart gently.
  2. Break off the stem, as fibers between the stem and heart can affect the taste.
  3. Shave the bottom of the artichoke to create a flat surface for serving.
  4. Break off any old, cracked, or small leaves.
  5. Even off the bottom of the artichoke with a knife.
  6. Cut off the pointed ends of the leaves with shears to prevent pricking.
  7. Rub the cut portions of the artichoke with lemon to prevent discoloration.
  8. Bring a large pot of water to a boil and add 1 tablespoon and a half of salt per quart of water.
  9. Add the artichoke to the boiling water, ensuring the water covers the top.
  10. Drape a piece of damp cheesecloth over the artichoke to keep the water circulating and maintain even color.
  11. Boil the artichoke for 20-30 minutes, depending on size and freshness.
  12. Test for doneness by poking the bottom with a sharp knife. If it goes in easily, it's ready.
  13. Serve hot, warm, or cold.

Instructions for Artichoke Bottoms

  1. Break off the stem of the artichoke.
  2. Break off the leaves to about halfway up the heart, bending them until they snap.
  3. Cut off the bottom of the heart with a knife, just above the choke.
  4. Rub the cut portions with lemon to prevent discoloration.
  5. Shave off any tough green parts from the heart with a sharp knife, leaving a pale yellow or white surface.
  6. Drop the heart into acidulated water (1 quart of water with 2 tablespoons of lemon juice).
  7. Cook the heart in a white (flour, water, lemon juice, and salt) for 20-30 minutes.
  8. Test for doneness by poking the bottom with a sharp knife. If it goes in easily, it's ready.
  9. Remove the choke with a spoon or grapefruit knife after cooking.
  10. Rinse the heart to remove any flour.
  11. To reheat, turn the heart upside down in a buttered baking dish, salt and pepper it, cover with wax paper, and bake at 325 degrees Fahrenheit for 5-10 minutes.

Instructions for Serving and Eating

  1. Serve whole boiled artichokes on a dinner plate.
  2. Eat the leaves by biting off the bottom portion, leaving the top on the plate.
  3. Once you reach the heart, push through the cone with a fork and pull it off.
  4. Dip the cone in sauce and eat the edible portion.
  5. Remove the choke from the heart and eat the remaining edible bottom.
  6. For artichoke bottoms, fill with béarnaise sauce, creamed seafood, or other desired fillings.
  7. Serve hot or cold with French dressing, hot sauce, or a butter and salt and pepper mixture.
  8. For a simple first course, fill a heated artichoke bottom with sauce Mornay, top with a poached egg, and garnish with parsley.
  9. Dip leaves in melted butter or vinaigrette while eating.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Le-5_bP5HM8

asparagus_french_chef.txt - Asparagus à la Française

Objectives

  • Learn to select and store fresh asparagus
  • Master the French technique of peeling and tying asparagus
  • Prepare a delicious sauce maltaise to accompany the asparagus

Ingredients

  • 3 tablespoons of salt
  • 3 bunches of asparagus
  • 1 orange, zested and juiced
  • 3 egg yolks
  • 1/4 teaspoon of salt
  • 2 tablespoons of mixed orange and lemon juice
  • 3/4 - 1 cup of melted butter

Instructions

  1. Select fresh asparagus with moist, firm butts, tightly closed tips, and no flower buds or fissures.
  2. Store asparagus in a container with the butts in about half an inch of water, covered with a plastic bag, and refrigerated for up to 2-3 days.
  3. Peel the asparagus by cutting off a quarter inch of the butt and peeling upwards until tender, about two inches from the top.
  4. Wash the peeled asparagus in cold water.
  5. Tie the asparagus into bunches of about two and a half inches in diameter, using four 16-18 inch pieces of string.
  6. Bring a large pot of water to a rapid boil.
  7. Add 3 tablespoons of salt to the boiling water.
  8. Add the asparagus bunches to the boiling water and cook for 5-6 minutes, or until tender-crisp.
  9. While the asparagus is cooking, prepare the sauce maltaise:
  10. Grate the rind of one orange.
  11. Juice the orange and mix with about two tablespoons of lemon juice.
  12. Beat three egg yolks until thick and sticky.
  13. Add 1/4 teaspoon of salt and 2 tablespoons of mixed orange and lemon juice to the egg yolks and beat well.
  14. Heat the egg yolk mixture over moderate heat, beating constantly, until it thickens into a custard.
  15. Gradually whisk in the melted butter, starting with small driblets and increasing the amount as the sauce thickens.
  16. Taste the sauce and adjust seasoning as needed.
  17. Remove the asparagus from the boiling water using a salad basket and let it drain.
  18. Serve the asparagus hot, garnished with a dollop of sauce maltaise.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fG10XAbWi6A

baba_au_rhum.txt - Baba Au Rhum

Objectives

  • Learn to make a basic yeast dough
  • Make baba au rhum using fresh and dry yeast
  • Understand the importance of proper dough rising and soaking

Ingredients

Fresh Yeast Method

  • 1 cake of fresh yeast (about 1 ounce)
  • 2 tablespoons granulated sugar
  • 1/8 teaspoon salt
  • 1 1/2 cups all-purpose flour
  • 2 large eggs
  • 1/4 cup melted butter

Dry Yeast Method

  • 1 package active dry yeast
  • 1/4 cup warm water (110 degrees)
  • 2 tablespoons granulated sugar
  • 1/8 teaspoon salt
  • 1 1/2 cups all-purpose flour
  • 2 large eggs
  • 1/4 cup melted butter

Syrup

  • 1 cup water
  • 1 cup granulated sugar
  • 1/2 cup rum (or half warm orange juice and sugar)

Decoration

  • Apricot glaze (apricot jam boiled with 2 tablespoons of sugar)
  • Slivered almonds
  • Glacéed cherries

Instructions

Fresh Yeast Method

  1. Mash the yeast in a bowl with a fork.
  2. Add the sugar and salt, and stir until the yeast melts into a liquid paste.
  3. Measure out 1 1/2 cups of flour using the scoop-and-level method.
  4. Add the eggs to the yeast mixture and beat with a fork until combined.
  5. Gradually add the flour, reserving a small amount.
  6. Add the melted butter and stir until combined.
  7. Knead the dough until it is no longer sticky and leaves your fingers.
  8. Place the dough in a greased bowl, cover with a damp towel, and let rise in a warm place (85 degrees) for about 2 hours, or until doubled in size.

Dry Yeast Method

  1. Dissolve the yeast in warm water in a bowl.
  2. Add the sugar and salt, and stir until dissolved.
  3. Measure out 1 1/2 cups of flour using the scoop-and-level method.
  4. Add the eggs to the yeast mixture and beat with a fork until combined.
  5. Gradually add the flour, reserving a small amount.
  6. Add the melted butter and stir until combined.
  7. Knead the dough until it is no longer sticky and leaves your fingers.
  8. Place the dough in a greased bowl, cover with a damp towel, and let rise in a warm place (85 degrees) for about 2 hours, or until doubled in size.

Baking the Babas

  1. Butter small baba molds (or muffin tins, popover tins, or oven glass jars).
  2. Once the dough has risen, punch it down.
  3. Fill the molds about one-third full with dough.
  4. Let the dough rise again until it reaches about a quarter-inch above the top of the molds.
  5. Bake in a 375-degree oven for 15 minutes, or until golden brown.

Making the Syrup

  1. Combine water and sugar in a saucepan and heat until the sugar dissolves.
  2. Let cool to tepid.
  3. Add rum (or orange juice and sugar).

Soaking the Babas

  1. Unmold the babas once they have cooled.
  2. Prick the babas all around the edges and in the top with a two-pronged fork.
  3. Immerse the babas in the syrup and let soak for about 30 minutes.
  4. Drain the babas for 30 minutes.

Decorating the Babas

  1. Warm the apricot glaze in a pan of hot water.
  2. Paint the glaze over the drained babas.
  3. Decorate with slivered almonds and a glacéed cherry.
  4. Serve in individual paper cups or a large dish.

Notes

  • You can freeze the babas for a month or two. To thaw, warm in a 350-degree oven until heated through.
  • If you want a stronger rum flavor, add a few drops of rum to the top of the babas before glazing.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WfOciiqNIBc

baby_cakes.txt - Baby Cakes

Objectives

  • Learn to bake classic butter cakes in mini loaf pans.
  • Explore variations on the basic recipe, including hazelnut, upside-down, and rose geranium cakes.
  • Master the technique of creaming butter and sugar for a light and fluffy cake texture.

Ingredients

Hazelnut Cake - 1 2/3 cups all-purpose flour - 2 teaspoons baking powder - 1 teaspoon kosher salt - 1 cup crème fraîche - 1/2 cup hazelnut flour - 1 cup sugar - 1/2 teaspoon almond extract - 4 large eggs - 1/2 cup unsalted butter, softened

Rhubarb Upside-Down Cake - 1/2 cup packed brown sugar - 4 tablespoons unsalted butter, melted - 1 tablespoon bourbon - 2 tablespoons chopped pecans - 6-8 stalks rhubarb, trimmed and chopped - Same cake batter as hazelnut cake, but without hazelnut flour or almond extract.

Rose Geranium Cake - Same cake batter as hazelnut cake, but without hazelnut flour or almond extract. - 2 teaspoons pure vanilla extract - 2 teaspoons rose water - Rose geranium leaves, chopped

Instructions

  1. Butter and flour 4 mini loaf pans.
  2. Combine 1 2/3 cups flour, 2 teaspoons baking powder, and 1 teaspoon kosher salt in a bowl.
  3. In a separate bowl, whisk together 1 cup crème fraîche, 1/2 cup hazelnut flour, 1 cup sugar, and 1/2 teaspoon almond extract.
  4. Cream softened butter in a mixer until light and fluffy.
  5. Gradually add eggs one at a time, scraping down the bowl between each addition.
  6. Add half the dry ingredients to the wet ingredients, followed by half the crème fraîche mixture, and repeat.
  7. Fold in remaining dry ingredients and crème fraîche mixture until just combined.
  8. Divide batter evenly between prepared pans.
  9. Bake at 350 degrees F for 30 minutes, or until a skewer inserted into the center comes out clean.
  10. Let cakes cool in pans for a few minutes before inverting onto a wire rack to cool completely.

For Rhubarb Upside-Down Cake: 1. Heat melted butter in a small saucepan. 2. Add brown sugar and bourbon, stirring until melted and caramelized. 3. Stir in pecans. 4. Divide mixture evenly between prepared pans. 5. Arrange rhubarb slices on top of the caramel mixture. 6. Pour batter over the rhubarb and bake for 20 minutes.

For Rose Geranium Cake: 1. Prepare cake batter as instructed for hazelnut cake, but substitute 2 teaspoons pure vanilla extract and 2 teaspoons rose water for the hazelnut flour and almond extract. 2. Arrange rose geranium leaves in concentric circles on top of the batter. 3. Bake for 20 minutes.

To Assemble the Cakes: 1. Top cakes with whipped cream, marscapone cheese, and fresh fruit, such as peaches or berries. 2. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DtkEe1oMPws

bagel_recipe.txt - Bagel Recipe

Objectives

  • Learn to make fresh, chewy bagels from scratch
  • Understand the importance of dough hydration and gluten development
  • Discover how to create a flavorful and visually appealing bagel spread

Ingredients

  • 1 packet active dry yeast
  • 1/4 cup warm water
  • 1/4 teaspoon sugar
  • 2 cups warm water
  • 3 tablespoons vegetable shortening
  • 1 tablespoon salt
  • 1 tablespoon sugar
  • 1 tablespoon liquid barley malt
  • Freshly ground black pepper (optional)
  • 4 cups super gluten flour (bromated)
  • Butter
  • 1/4 cup ice water
  • 1 teaspoon baking soda
  • Medium-brown cornmeal
  • Sesame seeds
  • Poppy seeds
  • Caraway seeds
  • 1 egg white
  • 12 ounces whipped cream cheese
  • Grated carrots
  • Radishes
  • Scallions
  • Cucumbers
  • Smoked salmon
  • 2 tablespoons rendered chicken fat
  • 2 large Spanish onions
  • Butter
  • Chicken livers
  • 3 hard-boiled eggs
  • Coarse salt
  • Freshly ground black pepper
  • Canola oil or vegetable oil (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. In a small bowl, dissolve one packet of active dry yeast in 1/4 cup of warm water.
  2. Add 1/4 teaspoon of sugar to activate the yeast.
  3. In a large mixing bowl, combine 2 cups of warm water, 3 tablespoons of vegetable shortening, 1 tablespoon of salt, 1 tablespoon of sugar, and 1 tablespoon of liquid barley malt.
  4. Stir in freshly ground black pepper (optional).
  5. Gradually add 4 cups of super gluten flour to the wet ingredients, stirring until a dough forms.
  6. Turn the dough out onto a lightly floured surface and knead for 10-15 minutes, or until smooth and elastic.
  7. Place the dough in a greased bowl, cover with a damp towel, and let rise in a warm place for 1 hour.
  8. Punch down the risen dough and divide it into 10 equal pieces.
  9. Shape each piece of dough into a bagel by pinching one end closed and rolling it into a long rope.
  10. Make a hole in the center of the rope by poking a finger through the middle.
  11. Place the bagels on a lightly floured towel and cover with a damp towel.
  12. Let the bagels rest for 15 minutes.
  13. Preheat oven to 500 degrees Fahrenheit for at least 30 minutes.
  14. Bring a large pot of water to a boil.
  15. Add 1 teaspoon of baking soda to the boiling water.
  16. Gently lower the bagels into the boiling water, 2-3 at a time.
  17. Boil the bagels for 1 minute and 30 seconds on each side.
  18. Remove the bagels from the boiling water and place them on a baking sheet lined with quarry tiles.
  19. Brush the bagels with egg white glaze.
  20. Top the bagels with cornmeal, sesame seeds, poppy seeds, and caraway seeds as desired.
  21. Place the baking sheet in the preheated oven and immediately reduce the oven temperature to 450 degrees Fahrenheit.
  22. Bake the bagels for 25 minutes, or until golden brown.
  23. Let the bagels cool in the oven with the door slightly ajar for 5 minutes.
  24. Remove the bagels from the oven and let them cool completely on a wire rack.
  25. While the bagels are cooling, prepare the spreads.
  26. For the vegetable cream cheese spread, combine whipped cream cheese, grated carrots, radishes, finely diced scallions, and cucumbers in a bowl.
  27. Season with freshly ground pepper to taste.
  28. For the smoked salmon and scallion spread, combine chopped smoked salmon, finely diced scallions, and a pinch of scallions for garnish in a bowl.
  29. For the chopped chicken liver spread, heat rendered chicken fat in a skillet over medium heat.
  30. Add chopped garlic and onions and cook until caramelized.
  31. Push the caramelized onions to the side of the skillet and add chicken livers.
  32. Sear the chicken livers on each side for a few minutes.
  33. Cover the skillet and reduce heat to low, steaming the chicken livers until cooked through.
  34. Remove the chicken livers from the skillet and transfer them to a food processor.
  35. Add the caramelized onions, 3 hard-boiled eggs, and coarse salt to the food processor.
  36. Pulse until coarsely chopped.
  37. Season with freshly ground pepper to taste.
  38. Transfer the chopped chicken liver spread to a bowl.
  39. To garnish the chopped chicken liver spread, arrange caramelized onions around the edge of the bowl.
  40. Sprinkle with coarse salt and freshly ground black pepper.
  41. Serve the bagels with your choice of spreads.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=S_13NZH8BGM

bavarian_cream_orange.txt - Bavarian Cream with Oranges

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic Bavarian cream, a luscious custard with cream and gelatin.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh ingredients and proper techniques for a smooth and velvety texture.
  • Discover how to mold and unmold the Bavarian cream for a dramatic presentation.

Ingredients

  • 5-6 oranges (large, juicy)
  • 2/3 cup orange juice
  • 1 1/2 packages unflavored gelatin (about 1 1/2 tablespoons)
  • 2 sugar lumps
  • 1 1/2 cups hot milk
  • Zest of 2 oranges
  • 7 egg yolks
  • 1 cup sugar
  • 2 teaspoons cornstarch
  • 5 egg whites
  • 1/4 teaspoon cream of tartar
  • 1/4 teaspoon salt
  • 1 cup heavy whipping cream
  • 2 tablespoons orange liqueur (optional)
  • Wax paper
  • String
  • Soufflé dish or other serving dish
  • Charlotte mold (optional)
  • Hot water
  • Orange segments (for decoration)

Instructions

  1. Soften the gelatin in the orange juice.
  2. Rub two sugar lumps over two oranges to extract the oil and enhance orange flavor.
  3. Combine the sugar lumps, orange zest, and hot milk in a saucepan.
  4. Beat seven egg yolks in a bowl until pale and lemon-colored.
  5. Gradually add the hot milk mixture to the egg yolks, stirring constantly.
  6. Cook the custard sauce over moderate heat, stirring constantly, until it thickens enough to coat the back of a spoon.
  7. Stir the softened gelatin into the hot custard sauce until it dissolves completely.
  8. Cool the custard sauce over ice.
  9. Beat five egg whites with cream of tartar and salt in an electric mixer until stiff peaks form.
  10. Fold the beaten egg whites into the cooled custard sauce.
  11. Chill the mixture in the refrigerator, folding every 15-20 minutes to prevent the custard from settling.
  12. Whip the heavy cream in a chilled bowl with a chilled beater until soft peaks form.
  13. Once the custard is almost set, fold in the whipped cream and orange liqueur (if using).
  14. Line a soufflé dish with wax paper, extending the paper above the rim of the dish.
  15. Pour the Bavarian cream into the prepared dish.
  16. Chill for at least five hours or overnight.
  17. To unmold, dip the bottom of the dish in hot water for a few seconds.
  18. Invert the dish onto a serving plate.
  19. Peel off the wax paper.
  20. Decorate with orange segments.
  21. Serve chilled.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mDmJ75m7NQw

blanquette_de_veau.txt - Blanquette de Veau

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a traditional French veal stew, Blanquette de Veau
  • Understand the importance of selecting and preparing the right veal cuts for a flavorful stew
  • Master the technique of making a creamy velouté sauce, the foundation of the Blanquette de Veau sauce

Ingredients

  • 3 pounds of veal (combination of bones, shank, breast, and lean meat)
  • 1 carrot, scrubbed
  • 1 celery stalk, broken in half
  • 1 medium onion or 2 small onions
  • 6 parsley sprigs
  • 1/2 bay leaf
  • 1/2 teaspoon thyme
  • Water
  • Chicken stock or veal stock (optional)
  • Canned chicken bouillon (optional)
  • Coarse or kosher salt
  • 3-4 white onions, peeled
  • Butter
  • 1/4 pound fresh mushrooms, trimmed and cleaned
  • Lemon juice
  • 2 1/2 cups veal stock
  • 4 tablespoons butter
  • 5 tablespoons flour
  • Heavy cream
  • 3 egg yolks
  • Parsley (for garnish)
  • Steamed rice (optional)

Instructions

  1. Blanch the veal: Fill a pot with water and bring to a boil. Add the veal and simmer for 2-3 minutes.
  2. Skim off the scum that rises to the surface.
  3. Drain the veal and rinse with cold water to remove any remaining scum.
  4. Prepare the veal stock: Return the blanched veal to the pot. Add water, chicken stock or veal stock (optional), canned chicken bouillon (optional), a carrot, celery, onion, herb bouquet (parsley, bay leaf, and thyme), and salt.
  5. Bring to a simmer and skim off any remaining scum.
  6. Simmer very slowly for 1 1/2 hours, or until the veal is tender.
  7. Prepare the white onions: Peel the onions using the boiling water method.
  8. Drop the onions into boiling water for 2-3 seconds.
  9. Peel the onions immediately while they are still hot.
  10. Pierce the root end of each onion with a knife.
  11. Cook the onions separately in a pan with a little bit of veal stock, salt, and butter.
  12. Simmer for about 30 minutes, or until tender.
  13. Prepare the mushrooms: Trim and clean the mushrooms.
  14. Cut small mushrooms in half and larger mushrooms into quarters.
  15. Cook the mushrooms in a pan with a little bit of veal stock, lemon juice, salt, and butter.
  16. Simmer for about 5 minutes.
  17. Make the velouté sauce: Drain the veal from its cooking stock and reserve the stock.
  18. Melt 4 tablespoons of butter in a saucepan.
  19. Whisk in 5 tablespoons of flour and cook until the mixture foams and froths for about 2 minutes.
  20. Gradually whisk in the reserved veal stock, a little bit at a time, until the sauce reaches the desired thickness.
  21. Add the cooking juice from the onions and mushrooms to the sauce.
  22. Simmer the sauce for a few minutes, if desired.
  23. Assemble the blanquette: Return the veal to the casserole dish.
  24. Add the cooked onions and mushrooms to the veal.
  25. Pour the sauce over the veal, onions, and mushrooms.
  26. Simmer for 2-3 minutes to blend the flavors.
  27. Enrich the sauce: In a separate bowl, whisk together 3 egg yolks and 3-4 tablespoons of heavy cream.
  28. Gradually whisk in a little bit of the hot sauce into the egg yolk and cream mixture.
  29. Pour the enriched egg yolk and cream mixture into the stew.
  30. Gently heat the stew, swirling it around until the sauce lightly thickens.
  31. Serve: Butter a platter and arrange the steamed rice at either end.
  32. Ladle the blanquette de veau onto the platter.
  33. Garnish with parsley.
  34. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jB7gt6LGIiQ

boeuf_bourguignon.txt - Boeuf Bourguignon

Objectives

  • Learn to make Boeuf Bourguignon, a classic French beef stew
  • Understand the importance of browning meat and deglazing the pan
  • Master the art of braising onions and sautéing mushrooms

Ingredients

  • 3 pounds of chuck beef, cut into 1-inch pieces
  • 3 cups of red wine
  • 2 cups of beef stock
  • 1 tablespoon of tomato paste
  • 1/2 teaspoon of thyme
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 4-5 cloves of garlic
  • 1 tablespoon of olive oil
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 pound of mushrooms, quartered
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1 tablespoon of flour per cup of sauce (for thickening)

Instructions

  1. Dry the beef pieces thoroughly with paper towels.
  2. Heat a large skillet over high heat and add olive oil.
  3. Brown the beef pieces in batches, making sure not to overcrowd the pan.
  4. Transfer the browned beef to a Dutch oven or casserole dish.
  5. Deglaze the skillet with red wine, scraping up any browned bits.
  6. Add the deglazed wine to the Dutch oven.
  7. Add beef stock to the Dutch oven, ensuring the meat is barely covered.
  8. Add tomato paste, thyme, bay leaf, and garlic to the Dutch oven.
  9. Bring the mixture to a simmer and season with salt.
  10. Transfer the Dutch oven to a 325-degree oven and cook for 3-4 hours, or until the beef is tender.
  11. While the beef is cooking, prepare the braised onions:
    • Bring a pot of water to a boil.
    • Add onions to the boiling water and cook for 20 seconds to loosen the skins.
    • Peel the onions, leaving them whole.
    • Pierce a small hole in the root end of each onion.
    • Place the onions in a pan with a little bit of water, butter, and salt.
    • Bring the mixture to a simmer, cover, and cook for 25 minutes, or until the onions are tender.
  12. While the beef and onions are cooking, prepare the sautéed mushrooms:
    • Wash the mushrooms thoroughly and dry them completely.
    • Quarter the mushrooms and set aside.
    • Heat a pan with butter and oil over medium heat.
    • Once the butter is hot and the foam has subsided, add the mushrooms.
    • Sauté the mushrooms for 2-3 minutes, or until they are lightly browned.
  13. Once the beef is cooked, remove the Dutch oven from the oven.
  14. Pour the sauce from the Dutch oven into a saucepan.
  15. Skim off any excess fat from the sauce.
  16. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  17. To thicken the sauce, prepare a beurre manié (butter and flour paste):
    • Combine 1 tablespoon of flour per cup of sauce with softened butter.
    • Work the butter and flour together until a paste forms.
  18. Remove the sauce from the simmer and add the beurre manié, whisking to combine.
  19. Bring the sauce to a boil and cook for 1 second.
  20. Return the beef to the Dutch oven and add the braised onions and sautéed mushrooms.
  21. Heat the stew through and serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NlGFkXd-QT0

bouillabaisse_marseillaise.txt - Bouillabaisse Marseillaise

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French fish stew
  • Understand the importance of fresh, high-quality seafood
  • Master the art of creating a flavorful broth

Ingredients

  • 1/2 cup olive oil
  • 2 cups sliced onions
  • 2 cups sliced leeks (or 4 cups onions if leeks are unavailable)
  • 6 cups fresh tomatoes (or 3 cups fresh tomatoes and 1 cup tomato puree)
  • 4-5 cloves garlic, chopped (no need to peel)
  • 6-8 parsley sprigs
  • 1/2 teaspoon thyme
  • 1/2 teaspoon fennel
  • 1 bay leaf (imported if possible)
  • 1 piece dry orange peel or bottled dried orange
  • 2-3 big pinches saffron threads
  • 2 1/2 quarts water (or 1 quart clam juice and 1 1/2 quarts water)
  • 1 tablespoon salt (if using water, omit salt if using clam juice)
  • Variety of fresh or frozen fish (hake, flounder, halibut, pollock, etc.)
  • 1 lobster
  • Scallops (optional)

Instructions

  1. Heat olive oil in a large kettle over medium heat.
  2. Add onions and leeks (or onions) and cook slowly for 5 minutes, covered.
  3. Add tomatoes, garlic, herbs, bay leaf, orange peel, and saffron.
  4. Add water (or clam juice and water) and bring to a rapid boil.
  5. Add 1 tablespoon of salt (if using water).
  6. Add fish frame (bones and head) to the boiling broth.
  7. Cook for 30-40 minutes, then strain the broth.
  8. In the strained broth, add firm-fleshed fish (bass, halibut, lobster) and bring to a boil for 5 minutes.
  9. Add less-firm-fleshed fish (pollock, flounder, scallops) and cook for 5 minutes.
  10. Serve immediately with French bread.

bouillabaisse.txt - Bouillabaisse

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French fish soup, Bouillabaisse.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh, lean fish for the best flavor.
  • Master the technique of making a flavorful fish stock.

Ingredients

  • 1/2 cup olive oil
  • 2 cups chopped onions
  • 2 cups chopped fresh tomatoes
  • 1 teaspoon dried basil
  • 1/2 teaspoon fennel seeds
  • 2 one-inch pieces dried orange peel
  • 2 pinches saffron
  • 1/2 clove garlic
  • 4-5 pounds fish bones and trimmings (or 1 quart canned clam juice)
  • 2 1/2 quarts water
  • 1 1/2 teaspoons salt per quart of water
  • Assortment of fresh, lean fish (halibut, cod, hake, striped bass, porgy, sunfish, perch, eel, mussels, clams, etc.)
  • Parsley
  • French bread, sliced and dried
  • Potatoes (optional)
  • Dry white Riesling or rosé wine (optional)

Instructions

  1. Heat olive oil in a large soup kettle over medium heat.
  2. Add chopped onions and cook for 5 minutes until softened.
  3. Add chopped tomatoes and cook for 5 minutes.
  4. Add dried basil, fennel seeds, dried orange peel, saffron, and garlic. Stir to combine.
  5. Add fish bones and trimmings (or canned clam juice) and water. Bring to a rapid boil.
  6. Skim off any scum that rises to the surface.
  7. Reduce heat to a simmer and cook for 40 minutes.
  8. Strain the fish stock through a fine-mesh sieve. Taste and adjust seasoning as needed.
  9. Return the strained stock to the kettle and bring to a boil.
  10. Add the largest pieces of fish, including any gelatinous fish like halibut. Cook for 10 minutes.
  11. Add the more delicate fish, like porgy, and cook for another 5 minutes.
  12. Add mussels and clams (if using) during the last 5 minutes of cooking.
  13. Arrange the cooked fish on a large platter.
  14. Spoon some of the soup over the fish.
  15. Pour the remaining soup into a tureen, being careful to avoid any sand from the mussels.
  16. Serve with crusty French bread and parsley.
  17. Enjoy with a glass of dry white Riesling or rosé wine.

braised_lamb_shanks_with_barley_risotto.txt - Braised Lamb Shanks with Barley Risotto

Objectives

  • Braise lamb shanks to create a flavorful and tender dish.
  • Prepare a barley risotto as a complementary side dish.
  • Master the art of browning vegetables for enhanced sauce color and flavor.
  • Learn how to deglaze a pan with wine for added depth of flavor.
  • Combine the braised lamb shanks with the barley risotto for a satisfying meal.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole lamb shank
  • 1 lamb shank, already cut
  • salt and pepper
  • flour
  • butter
  • leeks
  • carrots
  • celery
  • shallots
  • garlic
  • thyme
  • tomatoes
  • bay leaf
  • chicken stock (5 cups)
  • veal stock (1 cup)
  • chardonnay (1/4 - 1/2 cup)
  • barley
  • Parmesan cheese
  • flat Italian parsley

Instructions

  1. Salt and pepper the lamb shanks.
  2. Preheat a pan over high heat.
  3. Flour the lamb shanks.
  4. Add a small amount of butter to the hot pan.
  5. Brown the lamb shanks slowly on high heat.
  6. Cut vegetables (leeks, carrots, celery, shallots, garlic) into coarse pieces.
  7. Brown the vegetables in the same pan with a little butter, making sure they are evenly browned.
  8. Add a few sprigs of thyme, tomatoes, and a bay leaf to the vegetables.
  9. Roast the vegetables and herbs for a few minutes over high heat.
  10. Add the lamb shanks to the pan with the vegetables.
  11. Pour in 5 cups of chicken stock and 1 cup of veal stock.
  12. Add a small amount of chardonnay to the pan.
  13. Bring the mixture to a boil, then cover the pan and place it in a preheated 350-degree oven.
  14. Cook for 1 hour and 45 minutes, turning the shanks every 15-20 minutes to ensure even cooking.
  15. Remove the shanks from the oven and let them cool slightly.
  16. Strain the sauce through a chinois or regular strainer.
  17. Reduce the sauce over high heat, skimming off any excess fat.
  18. Cover the lamb shanks with foil to keep them warm and moist.
  19. Prepare the barley risotto.
  20. Finely dice an onion.
  21. Preheat a pan over high heat and melt a small amount of butter.
  22. Add the diced onion to the pan and cook until softened.
  23. Deglaze the pan with chardonnay.
  24. Add the barley to the pan and cook for 1-2 minutes.
  25. Add chicken stock to cover the barley.
  26. Cook the barley for 15-20 minutes over low heat, adding more stock periodically.
  27. While the barley cooks, dice carrots, leeks, and shallots into a brunoise.
  28. Sauté the vegetables in a separate pan with a small amount of butter.
  29. Add the sautéed vegetables to the barley risotto.
  30. Chop flat Italian parsley coarsely.
  31. Add Parmesan cheese to the risotto, making sure it melts.
  32. Add a small amount of butter to the risotto.
  33. Season with salt and pepper.
  34. Serve the braised lamb shanks and barley risotto family-style.
  35. Place the lamb shanks and risotto on a platter, with the shanks in the center and the risotto surrounding them.
  36. Garnish with a sprinkle of parsley.
  37. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xPlICy2nsNk

braised_lettuce_and_sauerkraut.txt - Braised Lettuce and Sauerkraut

Objectives

  • Learn how to braise lettuce and sauerkraut using classic French techniques.
  • Understand the importance of blanching vegetables for optimal flavor and texture.
  • Discover the versatility of braising and how it can be applied to various vegetables.

Ingredients

Braised Lettuce - 1 head Boston lettuce (or chicory, frisée, or escarole) - 1/2 cup blanched bacon, diced - 1/2 cup sliced onions - 1/3 cup sliced carrots - 1/2 cup white vermouth - Brown beef stock or canned beef bouillon - Thyme, parsley, and bay leaf tied together - Salt - Cornstarch - Butter

Braised Sauerkraut - 1 1/2 quarts sauerkraut - 4 ounces blanched bacon, diced - 3/4 cup sliced onions - 1/3 cup sliced carrots - 1/2 cup white vermouth - Chicken stock or canned chicken stock - Salt - Parsley, bay leaf, thyme, and juniper berries tied together - Red wine (for red cabbage)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the lettuce: Trim the stem off the lettuce, leaving a small portion to hold. Wash the lettuce gently in cold water to remove any sand. Blanch the lettuce in rapidly boiling water for 1-2 minutes, until limp. Refresh in cold water, then squeeze out excess water gently.
  2. Make the braising base for lettuce: Heat oil or butter in a low casserole. Add the blanched bacon, onions, and carrots. Cook slowly for 10 minutes, until the bacon has rendered its fat and the vegetables are tender.
  3. Cut and salt the lettuce: Cut the lettuce in half (or leave whole for smaller lettuces). Sprinkle the cut sides with salt. Fold the lettuce into a triangle shape, then turn over to create a neat presentation.
  4. Arrange the lettuce: Remove half of the braising vegetables from the casserole and set aside. Arrange the lettuce in the casserole, alternating different types if desired. Add the remaining braising vegetables on top.
  5. Add liquids and herbs: Pour in white vermouth and brown beef stock or bouillon. Add the herb bouquet. Bring to a simmer, then cover and place in a 350°F oven.
  6. Cook the lettuce: Cook for 2 1/2 hours, or until tender. The lettuce will be tender within an hour, but the braising process allows for a flavor exchange.
  7. Make the sauce: Remove the lettuce from the casserole and arrange on a serving platter. To make the sauce, thicken the remaining braising liquid with cornstarch and white vermouth. Bring to a simmer, then strain through a sieve. Add a final touch of butter off heat.
  8. Serve the lettuce: Pour the sauce over the lettuce and serve immediately.

Instructions for Sauerkraut 9. Prepare the sauerkraut: Drain the sauerkraut and rinse in cold water. Soak in water for 10-20 minutes, tasting periodically until the desired level of sourness is reached. Squeeze out excess water. 10. Make the braising base for sauerkraut: Heat oil or goose fat in a saucepan. Add the blanched bacon, onions, and carrots. Cook slowly for 10 minutes, until the bacon has rendered its fat and the vegetables are tender. 11. Add the sauerkraut: Add the sauerkraut to the braising base and stir to coat. Cover and cook over low heat for 10 minutes. 12. Add liquids and herbs: Pour in white vermouth and chicken stock. Cover the sauerkraut with the liquid. Add salt and the herb bouquet, including juniper berries if desired. 13. Cook the sauerkraut: Cover the saucepan with a piece of wax paper and a lid. Place in a 350°F oven. Cook for 3-5 hours, tasting periodically. Adjust oven temperature to 325°F if cooking too quickly. 14. Assemble the sauerkraut garnie: Once the sauerkraut has cooked for about 2 hours, brown pork chops and Italian sausages. Bury them in the sauerkraut and continue cooking until the meats are done. 15. Serve the sauerkraut: Remove the sauerkraut from the oven and arrange on a platter with the pork chops, sausages, and ham (optional). Drain any excess fat from the juices. Serve with boiled potatoes and mustard.

Additional Tips - If you're braising celery, use the same method as the lettuce. - For red cabbage, use red wine in the stock to maintain its color. - When cooking, think about how the current dish relates to other dishes you've made before. This will help you learn and grow as a cook.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CfGdzFwLD8Y
