french_chop_dinner.txt - French Chop Dinner in Half an Hour

Objectives

  • Prepare a three-course French dinner featuring chops in 30 minutes
  • Learn to cook "en cocotte" style, with vegetables and chops in one pan
  • Master the art of blanching vegetables and making a simple consommé madrilene

Ingredients

Consommé Madrilene

  • 2 cans beef consommé
  • 2 tomatoes
  • 1 tablespoon port wine
  • 1/4 cup chopped parsley

Côtelettes à la Nivernaise

  • 4 veal or pork chops
  • 1 tablespoon cooking oil
  • 3 carrots
  • 2 potatoes
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon black pepper
  • 1/2 teaspoon herbs (tarragon for veal, sage or Italian seasoning for pork)
  • 4 scallions
  • 1 cup frozen artichoke hearts

Petit Pot de Crème au Chocolat

  • 4 ounces semi-sweet chocolate bits
  • 1 1/2 cups heavy cream
  • 1 egg
  • 2 egg yolks
  • 1 tablespoon dark Jamaican rum

Instructions

  1. Brown chops on one side in a hot electric skillet with cooking oil.
  2. Cut carrots into quarters and blanch in boiling salted water for 2-3 minutes.
  3. Cut potatoes into quarters and blanch in boiling salted water with the carrots.
  4. Drain carrots and potatoes thoroughly.
  5. Season chops with salt, pepper, and herbs.
  6. Add blanched carrots, potatoes, and sliced scallions to the skillet with the chops.
  7. Reduce heat to 250 degrees and cover.
  8. Baste vegetables and chops with cooking oil and juices periodically.
  9. While chops cook, prepare consommé madrilene.
  10. Blanch tomatoes in boiling water for 10 seconds, then peel and add to consommé.
  11. Simmer consommé with tomato peels and pulp for a few minutes.
  12. Strain consommé and add chopped tomato pulp, port wine, and parsley.
  13. While chops cook, prepare pot de crème au chocolat.
  14. Melt chocolate bits in heavy cream over moderate heat.
  15. Whisk together egg and egg yolks.
  16. Gradually whisk hot chocolate mixture into egg mixture.
  17. Stir in rum.
  18. Strain custard mixture through a fine-mesh sieve.
  19. Pour custard into individual ramekins or heatproof cups.
  20. Place ramekins in a baking dish and fill with enough boiling water to reach halfway up the sides.
  21. Cover ramekins loosely with aluminum foil and bake in a preheated 350-degree oven for 20 minutes.
  22. Serve consommé madrilene hot or cold.
  23. Serve côtelettes à la nivernaise with a rosé wine.
  24. Serve pot de crème au chocolat hot, warm, or cold.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2DEz07og2a0

french_fruit_tart.txt - French Fruit Tart

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a French fruit tart
  • Master the art of making pastry cream (crème pâtissière)
  • Understand the importance of apricot glaze in French pastry

Ingredients

Pastry Cream (Crème Pâtissière)

  • 5 egg yolks
  • 1 cup granulated sugar
  • 2/3 cup sifted all-purpose flour
  • 2 cups hot milk

Apricot Glaze

  • 1 cup apricot preserves (or jam)
  • 2 tablespoons granulated sugar

Cherry Tart Flambé

  • Canned Bing cherries
  • Brandy
  • Sugar

Pineapple Tart

  • Canned crushed pineapple
  • Sugar

Banana Tart

  • Bananas
  • Cognac (or kirsch)

Strawberry Tart

  • Fresh strawberries
  • Red currant jelly (optional)

Other Ingredients

  • Vanilla extract
  • Cognac (or other liqueur)
  • Softened butter
  • Slivered almonds

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Pastry Cream (Crème Pâtissière):
  2. Beat 5 egg yolks gradually with 1 cup of sugar until thick and pale.
  3. Beat in 2/3 cup of sifted flour.
  4. Gradually beat in 2 cups of hot milk, starting slowly and increasing speed as the mixture warms.
  5. Pour the mixture into a heavy-bottomed saucepan and cook over moderately high heat, stirring constantly, until it comes to a boil.
  6. Remove from heat and beat vigorously with a wire whip to remove lumps.
  7. Return to low heat and cook for about 2 minutes, stirring constantly, to cook the flour. Be careful not to scorch the bottom.
  8. Remove from heat and stir in 2 teaspoons of vanilla extract and 3 tablespoons of cognac (or other liqueur).
  9. Stir in 2 tablespoons of softened butter.
  10. Taste and adjust the amount of liqueur and butter as desired.
  11. If making ahead of time, chill the pastry cream and cover the surface with a thin layer of butter to prevent a skin from forming.
  12. Prepare the Apricot Glaze:
  13. Heat 1 cup of apricot preserves (or jam) in a saucepan.
  14. Push the preserves through a sieve to remove any skins.
  15. Stir in 2 tablespoons of sugar and bring to a boil.
  16. The glaze should thicken and become sticky.
  17. Keep the glaze warm for use.
  18. Assemble the Fruit Tarts:
  19. Cherry Tart Flambé:
    • Soak canned Bing cherries in brandy and sugar.
    • Fill a tart shell with pastry cream and top with the soaked cherries.
    • Just before serving, sprinkle sugar over the tart and caramelize under the broiler.
    • Heat brandy and pour over the tart, igniting it.
  20. Pineapple Tart:
    • Drain canned crushed pineapple and boil the syrup for about 5 minutes until it thickens and caramelizes.
    • Add the crushed pineapple and boil for another 5 minutes.
    • Fill a tart shell with pastry cream and top with the pineapple mixture.
  21. Banana Tart:
    • Slice bananas and arrange them on top of pastry cream in a tart shell.
    • Glaze the tart with apricot glaze.
    • Sprinkle with slivered almonds.
  22. Strawberry Tart:
    • Arrange fresh strawberries on top of pastry cream in a tart shell, starting with the largest strawberry in the center.
    • Glaze the tart with apricot glaze.
    • You can use red currant glaze instead of apricot glaze if desired.
  23. Tiny Tart Shells:
    • Bake two pastry shells together in a 425°F oven for about 10 minutes until they shrink slightly and turn light brown.
    • Glaze the shells with apricot glaze and fill with pastry cream and fruit.
  24. Serve and Enjoy!
  25. All tarts can be made ahead of time and chilled.
  26. Serve the cherry tart flambé immediately after flaming.
  27. Enjoy your delicious French fruit tarts!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LjG4ab-aAjA

french_lamb_stew.txt - Navarin Printanier

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a delicious French lamb stew with root vegetables and green beans.
  • Understand the importance of browning the meat and deglazing the pan.
  • Learn the French technique of blanching green beans and peas.

Ingredients

  • 2-2.5 pounds boneless lamb stew meat
  • 1/2 cup cooking oil
  • 2 tablespoons sugar
  • 2.5 tablespoons flour
  • 4 cups meat stock (lamb, beef, or homemade)
  • 3 tomatoes, chopped
  • 2 bay leaves
  • 1/2 teaspoon rosemary
  • 3 cloves garlic, halved (optional)
  • 1/2 tablespoon coarse kosher salt
  • 8 peeled potatoes
  • 2 yellow turnips (rutabagas)
  • 4 small boiled onions
  • 2 peeled and quartered carrots
  • 1 cup green beans, cut into 1-inch pieces
  • 1 cup peas

Instructions

  1. Cut the lamb stew meat into 2-inch pieces.
  2. Heat the cooking oil in a heavy pan over medium-high heat.
  3. Add the lamb meat to the pan and brown on all sides.
  4. Transfer the browned lamb to a casserole dish.
  5. Add the sugar to the pan and cook over high heat, stirring constantly, until caramelized.
  6. Stir in the flour and cook for 2-3 minutes until golden brown.
  7. Deglaze the pan with the meat stock, scraping up any browned bits.
  8. Add the stock to the casserole dish with the lamb.
  9. Add the chopped tomatoes, bay leaves, rosemary, garlic (optional), and salt to the casserole.
  10. Cover the casserole and cook in a 325-degree oven for 1 hour.
  11. Remove the casserole from the oven and carefully skim off any excess fat.
  12. Add the potatoes, turnips, onions, and carrots to the casserole.
  13. Season with salt and baste with the liquid in the pan.
  14. Cover the casserole and cook for another hour, or until the vegetables are tender.
  15. While the root vegetables are cooking, blanch the green beans and peas in a large pot of boiling salted water for 5-6 minutes.
  16. Drain the green beans and peas and refresh them with cold water.
  17. Once the root vegetables are tender, add the blanched green beans and peas to the casserole.
  18. Cover the casserole and cook for 5-6 minutes until the beans are tender and have absorbed the flavors of the sauce.
  19. Serve the lamb stew on warm plates and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=duqVxpG_1I0

french_omelette.txt - French Omelette

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French omelette
  • Understand the importance of pan preparation and heat control
  • Master the unmolding technique for a smooth, creamy omelette

Ingredients

  • 2-3 eggs
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Optional: fresh herbs (parsley, chives, chervil, tarragon)
  • Optional: ham, cheese, sour cream

Instructions

  1. Crack 2-3 eggs into a bowl and beat with a fork until the yolks and whites are thoroughly mixed.
  2. Heat a non-stick pan over medium heat.
  3. Add 1 tablespoon of butter to the pan and swirl to coat.
  4. Pour the beaten eggs into the pan.
  5. Gently push the edges of the egg towards the center with a spatula.
  6. Tilt the pan to allow uncooked egg to flow to the edges.
  7. When the omelette is mostly set but still slightly wet on top, add fillings if desired.
  8. Fold one-third of the omelette over the center.
  9. Using the pan, slide the omelette onto a plate, flipping and folding the final third.
  10. Serve immediately.

Unmolding the Omelette

  1. Once the omelette is cooked, tilt the pan slightly and rest the lip of the pan on the edge of a plate.
  2. Quickly flip the pan over to unmold the omelette onto the plate.
  3. The omelette should slide out smoothly, leaving no residue in the pan.

Tips for Success

  • Use a non-stick pan with a handle that allows for easy shaking.
  • Ensure the butter is very hot before adding the eggs to prevent sticking.
  • Don't overcook the omelette. It should be soft and creamy inside.
  • Practice the unmolding technique to perfect it.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N40qglGNRlA

french_onion_soup.txt - French Onion Soup

Objectives

  • Learn to make French onion soup from scratch.
  • Master the art of chopping onions quickly and efficiently.
  • Understand the importance of properly browning onions and blending flavors.
  • Discover how to gratinée onion soup in both individual bowls and a large casserole.
  • Learn to poach eggs in the French method for a classic soup topping.
  • Explore ways to enhance and disguise the flavor of canned or packaged onion soup.

Ingredients

  • 1.5 quarts onions
  • 1 tablespoon oil
  • Butter
  • 3 tablespoons flour
  • 2 quarts beef stock (or half canned beef bouillon and half water)
  • 1 cup vermouth (optional)
  • French bread, sliced thick
  • Grated Swiss cheese
  • Grated parmesan cheese
  • Eggs
  • 1 tablespoon white vinegar
  • Worcestershire sauce
  • Corn starch
  • Brandy (optional)
  • Rosé wine (for serving)
  • Vegetable salad (for serving)
  • Cold meats (for serving)
  • Fresh string beans (for serving)
  • French bread (for serving)
  • Cookies (for serving)
  • Bowl of fruit (for serving)

Instructions

  1. Chop onions quickly and efficiently.
  2. Hold the knife with your thumb and forefinger gripping the top of the blade, and the rest of the knife in your other fingers.
  3. Chop straight down, cutting across the onion at the root end.
  4. Practice until you can chop onions quickly and easily.
  5. Soften the onions in a pot over medium heat.
  6. This process is called étouffée in French.
  7. Cover the onions and cook them moderately fast, watching them carefully.
  8. Brown the onions.
  9. Turn the heat up to medium-high and stir the onions every 2-3 minutes to prevent burning.
  10. Continue browning until the onions reach a nice mahogany color.
  11. Thicken the soup with flour.
  12. Add 3 tablespoons of flour to the browned onions and cook for about 3 minutes, stirring constantly, until the flour turns a light brown.
  13. Add the beef stock.
  14. Pour in 2 quarts of beef stock (or half canned beef bouillon and half water) and whisk until the flour is completely blended.
  15. Simmer the soup for 30 minutes.
  16. Allow the flavors to blend and deepen during this time.
  17. Add a cup of vermouth for added complexity, if desired.
  18. Toast the bread.
  19. Cut thick slices of French bread and toast them in a 325 degree oven for about 30 minutes, or until crispy and lightly browned.
  20. Prepare the cheese mixture.
  21. Grate a mixture of Swiss and parmesan cheese.
  22. You can use all parmesan or all Swiss cheese, if you prefer.
  23. Poach the eggs.
  24. Bring a pot of water to a simmer.
  25. Add 1 tablespoon of white vinegar per quart of water.
  26. Carefully drop the eggs into the simmering water and cook for 3 minutes.
  27. To ensure the eggs hold their shape, place them in simmering water for 10 seconds before adding to the poaching water.
  28. Assemble the gratinée.
  29. Place a slice of toasted bread in a bowl or casserole dish.
  30. Ladle hot onion soup over the bread.
  31. Sprinkle the soup with the cheese mixture.
  32. Drizzle a little oil or melted butter over the top.
  33. Bake in the oven until the cheese is melted and bubbly.
  34. Serve the gratinée.
  35. Enjoy the gratinée immediately.
  36. Prepare poached eggs on toast.
  37. Place a poached egg on a slice of toasted bread.
  38. Ladle hot onion soup over the egg and toast.
  39. Disguise canned onion soup.
  40. Pour canned onion soup into a terrine.
  41. Add vermouth, red wine, or grated raw onion for extra flavor.
  42. Sliver some cheese into the soup for a stringy texture.
  43. Add a splash of cognac for a classic French touch.
  44. Gratinée the terrine.
  45. Top the soup with toasted bread rounds.
  46. Sprinkle with a generous amount of cheese.
  47. Drizzle with oil or melted butter.
  48. Bake in the oven until the cheese is melted and bubbly.
  49. Create a rich, creamy filling for the soup.
  50. Combine an egg yolk, a half teaspoon of Worcestershire sauce, a teaspoon of corn starch, and 3 tablespoons of brandy in a bowl.
  51. Gradually whisk in a small amount of hot soup until the mixture is smooth.
  52. Pour the mixture back into the soup and stir gently.
  53. Serve the onion soup.
  54. Enjoy the onion soup with a light supper, such as a vegetable salad, cold meats, fresh string beans, and French bread.
  55. Finish the meal with cookies and a bowl of fruit.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aU8BhMYpJaQ

french_pancakes.txt - French Pancakes

Objectives

  • Learn to make thin, delicate French crepes
  • Explore the versatility of crepes for lunch and supper dishes
  • Master the technique of flipping crepes

Ingredients

  • 1 cup of milk
  • 1 cup of water
  • 2 cups of sifted flour
  • 4 eggs
  • 1 teaspoon of salt
  • 4 tablespoons of melted butter

Instructions

  1. Combine 1 cup of milk, 1 cup of water, 2 cups of sifted flour, 4 eggs, and 1 teaspoon of salt in an electric blender.
  2. Add 4 tablespoons of melted butter to the blender.
  3. Blend the ingredients until smooth.
  4. Let the batter rest for two hours in the refrigerator.
  5. Heat a non-stick pan over medium heat.
  6. Pour a small amount of batter into the center of the pan, tilting the pan to spread the batter evenly.
  7. Cook for about 30 seconds, or until bubbles appear and the edges begin to brown.
  8. Flip the crepe over using a wooden spatula or by lifting it with your fingers.
  9. Cook for an additional 30 seconds.
  10. Repeat steps 6-9 to make additional crepes.
  11. To fill the crepes, spread a desired filling onto the non-public side of the crepe.
  12. Roll or fold the crepe to enclose the filling.
  13. Serve immediately, or refrigerate for later use.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FTHh8tzhAA

french_puff_pastry.txt - French Puff Pastry

Objectives

  • Learn how to make French puff pastry using American flour
  • Understand the importance of chilling and resting the dough
  • Discover the benefits of using granular flour for puff pastry

Ingredients

  • 3 cups granular all-purpose flour
  • 1/3 cup tasteless salad oil
  • 3/4 cup cold water
  • 1 1/2 tablespoons salt
  • 2 sticks unsalted butter

Instructions

  1. Combine 3 cups of granular all-purpose flour and 1/3 cup of oil in a bowl.
  2. Stir the mixture with a rubber spatula until well combined.
  3. Dissolve 1 1/2 tablespoons of salt in 3/4 cup of cold water.
  4. Gradually pour the salt water into the flour mixture, stirring with a rubber spatula.
  5. Squeeze the dough with your hands to ensure it holds together.
  6. If necessary, add a few tablespoons of cold water to the dough, ensuring it is not too moist.
  7. Knead the dough briefly until it forms a cohesive mass.
  8. Press the dough into a 9-inch circle using the palm of your hand.
  9. Soften two sticks of chilled unsalted butter by beating it with a rolling pin.
  10. Shape the softened butter into a 5-inch square.
  11. Place the butter square in the center of the dough circle.
  12. Fold the dough over the butter, ensuring the edges remain even.
  13. Chill the dough-wrapped butter package for 30 minutes.
  14. Roll out the dough into a rectangle, starting slowly and gradually increasing pressure.
  15. Flour the work surface lightly to prevent sticking.
  16. Roll the dough until the butter is visible.
  17. Fold the dough into thirds, first folding one end up and then the other end over.
  18. Roll out the dough again into a rectangle.
  19. Repeat the folding process, folding the dough into thirds twice.
  20. Wrap the dough in wax paper and chill for at least one hour.
  21. To demonstrate the importance of chilling, roll out a dough that has not been properly chilled.
  22. Notice how the dough becomes rubbery and difficult to roll.
  23. Chill the dough again for two hours to relax the gluten.
  24. Roll out a dough that has been properly chilled and rested.
  25. Cut the dough in half and roll each half into a long rectangle.
  26. Roll out one piece of dough thinner than the other, as the bottom crust should be thin to cook more quickly.
  27. Place the thinner dough on a wet pastry sheet to prevent the layers from sticking.
  28. Spread the dough evenly on the pastry sheet.
  29. Place Roquefort cheese in the center of the dough.
  30. Top the cheese with thick cream sauce.
  31. Chill the assembled pastry for at least two hours before baking.
  32. Before baking, brush the pastry with a beaten egg mixture containing one teaspoon of water.
  33. Bake the pastry in a 450-degree oven for 20 minutes.
  34. Reduce the oven temperature to 350 degrees and bake for an additional 20 minutes.
  35. Let the pastry cool slightly before cutting and serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=J3Y2wcjhwJ8

french_salad.txt - French Salad

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare and dress a French salad
  • Understand the importance of using the right ingredients
  • Learn how to make a classic French salad dressing and mayonnaise

Ingredients

French Salad - Boston lettuce - Chicory - Romaine lettuce - Escarole - Endives - Watercress - Olive oil - Wine vinegar - Salt - Pepper - Dry mustard - Green onion or scallion - Parsley - Chives - Garlic - Stale French bread - Hard-boiled egg yolks - Minced herbs

French Potato Salad - Boiled potatoes - Chicken stock, white wine, or vermouth - Green onions, shallots, or scallions - Salt - Pepper - French dressing - Minced parsley and chives

Salade Niçoise - Boston lettuce - French potato salad - Cooked green beans - Tuna - Anchovies - Olives - Capers - Tomatoes - Hard-boiled eggs - Mayonnaise - Green herbs

Instructions

  1. Prepare the salad greens:
  2. Wash and dry all salad greens thoroughly.
  3. For Boston lettuce, cut around the root with a knife.
  4. Wash greens in a basin of water, removing any dirt.
  5. Drain the water and dry the greens by tossing them in a colander.
  6. Wrap the wet greens in a clean towel and roll up gently.
  7. Refrigerate for an hour or two until dry.
  8. Store in a plastic bag for up to a day or two.
  9. Make the French salad dressing:
  10. Combine wine vinegar, dry mustard, salt, pepper, and chopped green onion or scallion in a jar.
  11. Add olive oil and shake well.
  12. Taste and adjust seasoning as needed.
  13. Make the dressing just before serving.
  14. Prepare the French potato salad:
  15. Steam potatoes until tender.
  16. Slice potatoes while hot.
  17. Toss potatoes with chicken stock, white wine, or vermouth.
  18. Let potatoes sit for 3-4 minutes, tossing occasionally.
  19. Add chopped green onions, shallots, or scallions, salt, pepper, and French dressing.
  20. Toss well and serve hot or chilled.
  21. Make the mayonnaise:
  22. Beat egg yolks until thick and sticky.
  23. Slowly drizzle in oil, drop by drop at first.
  24. Continue beating until the mixture thickens.
  25. Add vinegar, lemon juice, salt, and pepper.
  26. Taste and adjust seasoning as needed.
  27. Assemble the salade niçoise:
  28. Arrange Boston lettuce leaves on a platter.
  29. Add French potato salad, cooked green beans, tuna, anchovies, olives, capers, tomatoes, hard-boiled eggs, and mayonnaise.
  30. Season each ingredient separately before arranging on the platter.
  31. Garnish with green herbs.
  32. Serve:
  33. Enjoy the salade niçoise as a first course or a main course for a summer luncheon.
  34. Pair with rosé wine.

french_vegetables.txt - French Vegetables

Objectives

  • Learn to cook vegetables the French way
  • Master the technique of blanching vegetables for optimal freshness and flavor
  • Explore various methods for preparing and serving delicious vegetables

Ingredients

Green string beans 8-9 quarts of water Butter Salt Shallot (or spring onions) Carrots Chicken broth (optional) Mushrooms Mushroom stems Butter Minced shallot Heavy cream Flour Parsley Swiss cheese Spinach Water Flour Butter Cream (or chicken stock) Salt Pepper French rolls Alsatian Traminer wine Hollandaise sauce (optional)

Instructions

  1. Wash the green beans in hot water just before cooking.
  2. Bring a large kettle of water to a rapid boil.
  3. Add the green beans to the boiling water and cook for 5 minutes.
  4. Use a hot stainless steel rod to bring the water back to a boil quickly after adding the beans.
  5. Drain the beans in a colander and immediately refresh them in cold water for 3-4 minutes.
  6. Drain the beans again and pat them dry.
  7. Heat the beans in a pot over medium heat, tossing them with butter, lemon juice, parsley, and salt and pepper.
  8. Prepare the carrots by cutting them into quarters and then in half.
  9. Place the carrots in a pot with water, butter, salt, and a chopped shallot (or spring onions).
  10. Bring to a simmer, cover, and cook for 20 minutes.
  11. Prepare the stuffed mushrooms by removing the stems and chopping them finely.
  12. Squeeze the chopped mushroom stems to remove excess juice.
  13. Sauté the chopped mushroom stems in butter with minced shallot.
  14. Add flour and cook for a minute.
  15. Pour in heavy cream and cook until thickened.
  16. Season with salt and pepper.
  17. Rub the mushroom caps with butter and fill them with the mushroom sauce.
  18. Sprinkle grated Swiss cheese on top and broil until golden brown.
  19. Blanch the spinach in boiling water for 1-2 minutes until limp.
  20. Remove the stems from the spinach.
  21. Wash the spinach and squeeze out excess water.
  22. Chop the spinach using a stainless steel knife.
  23. Heat the spinach in a pan over medium heat, stirring until the water evaporates.
  24. Add flour and cook for a minute.
  25. Stir in cream (or chicken stock) and cook until thickened.
  26. Season with salt and pepper.
  27. Cover the pan and cook slowly for 15 minutes.
  28. Serve the vegetables with hot French rolls, Alsatian Traminer wine, and hollandaise sauce (optional).

fried_chicken_biscuits_sweet_potato_pie.txt - Fried Chicken, Biscuits, and Sweet Potato Pie

Objectives

  • Learn how to cut and prepare a whole chicken for frying
  • Master the art of making a classic Southern biscuit
  • Discover Leah Chase's secret to the perfect sweet potato pie

Ingredients

Fried Chicken

  • 1 chicken (3-3.5 pounds)
  • Salt and white pepper
  • 2 eggs
  • 2 (12-ounce) cans evaporated milk
  • Water
  • 3 cups flour
  • Seasoned salt (garlic and other spices)
  • Black pepper
  • Heavy vegetable oil

Biscuits

  • 2 cups self-rising flour
  • 2 heaping teaspoons baking powder
  • 1 teaspoon sugar
  • 1 cup shortening
  • Milk

Sweet Potato Pie

  • 1 1/2 cups white flour
  • 1 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 cup pecans
  • 1/2 cup shortening
  • 1/4 cup ice water
  • 2 quarts peeled sweet potatoes
  • 1 cup sugar
  • 1 teaspoon cinnamon
  • 1/4 teaspoon grated nutmeg
  • 2 eggs
  • 1/2 cup condensed milk
  • Butter
  • Vanilla extract
  • Whipped cream (optional)

Instructions

  1. Cut the chicken into desired pieces.
  2. Cut the chicken into smaller pieces for a larger family or for use in gumbo.
  3. For a smaller family, leave the breast whole.
  4. Season the chicken with salt and white pepper.
  5. Prepare the egg wash: Crack 2 eggs into a bowl and beat until well combined.
  6. Add 2 cans of evaporated milk and a little water to the egg wash.
  7. Combine 3 cups of flour, seasoned salt, and black pepper in a separate bowl.
  8. Dip each piece of chicken into the egg wash, then dredge in the flour mixture.
  9. Heat a heavy pot filled with vegetable oil to 350 degrees Fahrenheit.
  10. Fry the chicken in the hot oil for about 15-20 minutes, or until golden brown and cooked through.
  11. Remove the wings first, as they will cook faster.
  12. Make the biscuits: Combine 2 cups self-rising flour, 2 heaping teaspoons of baking powder, and 1 teaspoon of sugar in a bowl.
  13. Cut in 1 cup of shortening until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs.
  14. Add milk gradually, mixing until a soft dough forms.
  15. Turn the dough out onto a lightly floured surface and pat it out to about 1/2 inch thickness.
  16. Cut the dough into biscuits using a biscuit cutter.
  17. Bake the biscuits in a preheated oven at 400 degrees Fahrenheit for 15-20 minutes, or until golden brown.
  18. Prepare the sweet potato pie crust: Combine 1 1/2 cups of flour, 1 teaspoon of salt, and 1/4 cup of pecans in a bowl.
  19. Cut in 1/2 cup of shortening until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs.
  20. Add 1/4 cup of ice water gradually, mixing until a dough forms.
  21. Pat the dough into a pie plate and crimp the edges.
  22. Prick the bottom of the crust with a fork to prevent it from bubbling up.
  23. Bake the crust in a preheated oven at 375-400 degrees Fahrenheit for about 10 minutes.
  24. Make the sweet potato pie filling: Mash the peeled sweet potatoes until smooth.
  25. Add 1 cup of sugar, 1 teaspoon of cinnamon, 1/4 teaspoon of grated nutmeg, and 2 eggs to the mashed sweet potatoes.
  26. Beat the mixture until well combined.
  27. Stir in 1/2 cup of condensed milk and a little vanilla extract.
  28. Pour the filling into the partially baked crust.
  29. Sprinkle the top of the pie with a few pecans and a little cinnamon.
  30. Bake the pie in a preheated oven at 375 degrees Fahrenheit for about 45-50 minutes, or until the filling is set.
  31. Let the pie cool completely before serving.
  32. Serve the fried chicken, biscuits, and sweet potato pie warm.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9vjnBHCn7Bg

frito_misto_artichoke.txt - Frito Misto with Fried Baby Artichokes

Objectives

  • Learn how to make aioli sauce with raw egg yolks, garlic, and olive oil.
  • Prepare baby artichoke hearts for frying by trimming and blanching.
  • Learn how to fry artichoke hearts for a crispy, tender texture.

Ingredients

  • 2 egg yolks
  • 2 cloves garlic
  • 1 cup olive oil
  • salt
  • baby artichokes
  • lemon juice
  • peanut oil
  • fennel
  • lemon slices
  • flour
  • coarse sea salt
  • freshly ground black pepper
  • Parmesan cheese
  • mussels
  • cod
  • 3-4 pounds salt
  • egg whites
  • summer vegetables (potatoes, artichokes, carrots, green beans, cipolline onions, heirloom tomatoes)
  • butter
  • olive oil
  • flowering marjoram
  • thyme
  • cresses

Instructions

  1. Crush garlic cloves in half, removing any shoots, and add to a mortar and pestle with egg yolks and a pinch of salt.
  2. Slowly add olive oil while continuously mashing, forming an emulsion.
  3. Trim baby artichoke hearts, removing outer leaves, and cut off the top and bottom.
  4. Place artichoke hearts in a bowl with lemon juice to prevent browning.
  5. Spin artichoke hearts in a salad spinner to remove excess water.
  6. Heat peanut oil to 330° - 340° and fry artichoke hearts for 2-3 minutes to cook through.
  7. Remove artichoke hearts and drain on paper towels.
  8. Heat peanut oil to 400° and fry artichoke hearts again until crispy and browned.
  9. While waiting for oil to heat, shave fennel thinly using a vegetable slicer.
  10. Cut off the ends of a lemon to flatten it and slice thinly.
  11. Toss fennel with flour, salt, and pepper.
  12. Coat lemon slices with flour.
  13. Add artichoke hearts, fennel, and lemon slices to hot oil and fry until browned.
  14. Season artichoke hearts with salt and pepper and toss with a few drops of olive oil.
  15. Serve artichoke hearts with aioli sauce and shaved Parmesan cheese.
  16. Scrub mussels and remove beards.
  17. Heat a skillet and add mussels, allowing them to open from the heat.
  18. Serve mussels on the skillet with melted butter, salt, and pepper.
  19. Combine salt and egg whites to form a loose paste.
  20. Place a layer of salt mixture on the bottom of a baking dish.
  21. Place cod on top of the salt mixture, leaving the tail sticking out.
  22. Mound salt mixture on top of the cod, ensuring the fish is completely covered.
  23. Bake at 500° until the crust turns golden brown and there are pockets of boiling water underneath.
  24. Gently tap the crust with the back of a knife to remove it from the fish.
  25. Use a pastry brush to remove any remaining salt from the fish.
  26. Peel the skin back from the cod.
  27. Serve cod on a platter with steamed vegetables, including potatoes, artichokes, carrots, green beans, grilled cipolline onions, and heirloom tomatoes.
  28. Garnish with flowering marjoram, thyme, and cresses.
  29. Drizzle with aioli sauce.

genoise_cake.txt - Genoise Cake

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French genoise cake.
  • Understand the importance of using whole eggs and beating them over hot water.
  • Learn to make a classic French buttercream frosting.

Ingredients

Cake - 5 tablespoons (4 ounces) of melted butter, tepid - 1 1/2 cups of sifted cake flour (plain bleached cake flour) - 4 large eggs (U.S. graded) - 2/3 cup of granulated sugar - 2 teaspoons of vanilla extract - Grated rind of an orange or a lemon (optional)

Buttercream - 2/3 cup of granulated sugar - 1/4 cup of water - 1 large egg (U.S. graded) - 3 egg yolks - 2 sticks (1/2 pound) of softened, unsalted butter - 1 teaspoon of vanilla extract - 2-3 tablespoons of kirsch (or strong coffee)

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 325 degrees F (160 degrees C).
  2. Prepare a cake pan by lightly buttering it, lining the bottom with wax paper, buttering the paper, and dusting with flour.
  3. Melt butter and set aside to cool until tepid.
  4. In a metal bowl, whisk together eggs, sugar, vanilla extract, and optional citrus zest.
  5. Place the bowl over a pan of simmering water (not boiling) and whisk continuously for 5-6 minutes, until the mixture has doubled in volume, is foamy, and is warm to the touch.
  6. Remove the bowl from the heat and continue beating for another 5-6 minutes, until the mixture is cool and thick enough to make a ribbon when lifted from the bowl.
  7. Gently fold in the melted butter and sifted flour in 4 additions, alternating between butter and flour, ensuring to fold continuously.
  8. Pour the batter into the prepared pan and bake for 35-45 minutes, or until the cake is golden brown, springy to the touch, and shows a hairline of shrinkage around the edges.
  9. Let the cake cool in the pan for 10 minutes, then invert it onto a wire rack and peel off the paper.
  10. Once cool, cover the cake with plastic wrap to prevent drying out.
  11. For the buttercream, combine sugar and water in a saucepan and bring to a boil, stirring until the sugar dissolves completely and the liquid becomes clear.
  12. While the sugar syrup is heating, whisk together the whole egg and egg yolks in a bowl.
  13. Slowly pour the hot sugar syrup into the egg mixture, whisking constantly to prevent curdling.
  14. Place the bowl over simmering water and whisk for 7-8 minutes, until the mixture is thick and makes a ribbon when lifted from the bowl.
  15. Remove the bowl from the heat and beat in the softened butter gradually until smooth and fluffy.
  16. Stir in vanilla extract and kirsch (or coffee) until well combined.
  17. Cut the cooled genoise cake in half horizontally.
  18. Spread a thin layer of buttercream on one cake layer, then top with the other layer.
  19. Frost the entire cake with the remaining buttercream, smoothing it out with a spatula dipped in hot water.
  20. Decorate the cake with melted chocolate using a pastry bag with a toothed nozzle.
  21. Refrigerate the cake to set the frosting and chocolate decoration.
  22. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ROOIYTdEzec

gigot_farci.txt - Gigot Farci (Stuffed Leg of Lamb)

Objectives

  • Learn how to bone a leg of lamb for easier carving.
  • Prepare a delicious stuffing for the lamb.
  • Create a flavorful mustard coating for the roast.
  • Roast the lamb to medium-rare perfection.
  • Make a flavorful sauce to accompany the lamb.

Ingredients

Lamb: - 1 leg of lamb (6.5 pounds) - 1 cup ground lamb

Stuffing: - 3/4 cup white bread crumbs (somewhat stale) - few tablespoons of milk - 1 tablespoon shallots, finely diced - 1/8 teaspoon rosemary - 1 clove garlic, minced - 1/4 teaspoon salt - freshly ground pepper

Mustard Coating: - 1/2 teaspoon rosemary, ground - 1/2 cup Dijon mustard - 1 clove garlic, minced - 1 tablespoon soy sauce - 4 tablespoons olive oil

Sauce: - 1 tablespoon mustard coating - meat stock - 1 teaspoon cornstarch

Other: - butter - skewers - white string - cooking oil - chopped carrot - chopped onion - thermometer

Instructions

  1. Bone the lamb: If you're not having the butcher bone the lamb, carefully remove the hip bone and leg bone. This will make carving much easier.
  2. Trim the fat: Ask the butcher to remove most of the fell (filament) off the big end of the lamb. Use a knife to slice off any remaining fat from the outside and inside of the lamb.
  3. Prepare the stuffing: Moisten the bread crumbs with a few tablespoons of milk, ensuring they are damp but not soggy. Sauté the shallots in a tablespoon of butter for a minute. Combine the shallots, rosemary, garlic, ground lamb, salt, and pepper with the bread crumbs and mix thoroughly.
  4. Stuff the lamb: Fill the cavity where the bone was with the stuffing, pressing it all the way down to the knee. Secure the stuffing in place with skewers, threading them through the lamb flap.
  5. Prepare the mustard coating: Grind the rosemary in a mortar. Combine the ground rosemary, Dijon mustard, garlic, soy sauce, and olive oil in a bowl. Mix well, slowly adding the olive oil in a drizzling motion.
  6. Coat the lamb: Use a rubber spatula to evenly coat the lamb with the mustard mixture, both inside and out. Set aside for at least 30 minutes to allow the flavors to meld.
  7. Roast the lamb: Preheat the oven to 350 degrees Fahrenheit. Place the lamb on a rack in a roasting pan, fat side up. Add a chopped carrot and onion to the pan for added flavor. Insert a meat thermometer into the thickest part of the meat, making sure it doesn't touch the stuffing. Let the lamb rest at room temperature for 2 hours before roasting.
  8. Roast to medium rare: Roast the lamb for 1.5 to 2 hours, or until the internal temperature reaches 140 degrees Fahrenheit. Do not baste, as the mustard coating will keep the lamb moist.
  9. Rest the lamb: Remove the lamb from the oven and let it rest for 20 minutes before carving.
  10. Make the sauce: Deglaze the roasting pan with meat stock, scraping up any browned bits. Simmer the sauce for a few minutes. Combine a tablespoon of the mustard coating with cornstarch and mix into a paste. Add a bit of the lamb juice to the paste and whisk until smooth. Pour the mixture into the sauce and simmer until thickened.
  11. Serve: Carve the lamb into slices, serve on hot plates, and drizzle with the sauce. Enjoy with your favorite side dishes.

Tips: - If you are using a whole leg of lamb, it will take approximately 1.5 hours to roast to medium-rare. - The lamb is done when you see juices running in the pan. - Serve with a red Bordeaux Saint-

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RTXIeWcPPiA

glamour_pouding.txt - Glamour Pouding

Objectives

  • Transform simple custard into a glamorous dessert.
  • Learn to make a "pouding" using custard, cake, rum, and glaceed fruit.
  • Understand the traditional method of making glaceed fruits.

Ingredients

  • 1 quart milk
  • 5 whole eggs
  • 5 egg yolks
  • 1 cup sugar
  • 1 tablespoon vanilla
  • 1/3 cup dark Jamaican rum
  • 1 cup glaceed fruit (soaked in boiling water)
  • 1/2 cup cherries (halved and soaked in boiling water)
  • 1 store-bought cake (pound cake or yellow cake)
  • 1/2 cup apricot jam
  • 1 tablespoon sugar
  • Chopped almonds

Instructions

  1. Soak the glaceed fruit and cherries in boiling water for 1-2 minutes to remove preservatives.
  2. Drain and shake off excess water from the fruit and cherries.
  3. Combine the glaceed fruit with 1/3 cup of rum and stir well.
  4. Combine the cherries with 1 tablespoon of rum and stir well.
  5. In a bowl, beat together 5 whole eggs and 5 egg yolks until well combined.
  6. Gradually add 1 cup of sugar to the egg mixture, beating until thoroughly combined.
  7. Slowly whisk in 1 quart of hot milk to the egg mixture, ensuring the yolks don't scramble.
  8. Add 1 tablespoon of vanilla to the custard mixture.
  9. Preheat oven to 350 degrees Fahrenheit.
  10. Grease an 8x8 inch baking pan.
  11. Arrange the halved cherries in the bottom of the pan, cut side down, to create a decorative pattern.
  12. Cut the cake into 1/2 inch thick slices and then into squares.
  13. Place a piece of cake on top of each group of cherries in the pan.
  14. Carefully pour the custard mixture over the cake, making sure not to dislodge the cherries.
  15. Spread the remaining glaceed fruit evenly over the custard.
  16. Add more cake pieces on top of the fruit, depending on your preference.
  17. Pour more custard over the cake, filling the pan to the top.
  18. Place the pan in a larger pan filled with water, ensuring the water comes halfway up the sides of the baking pan.
  19. Bake in the oven for about an hour, or until a knife inserted into the center comes out clean.
  20. While the custard is baking, prepare the apricot glaze by straining apricot jam and boiling it down with 1 tablespoon of sugar until it becomes sticky.
  21. Let the custard cool in the oven for 20 minutes, or overnight, before unmolding.
  22. Unmold the custard onto a serving platter, carefully removing any paper used for decoration.
  23. Glaze each individual custard with the warm apricot glaze.
  24. While the glaze is still warm, sprinkle chopped almonds around the edges of the custard.
  25. Serve the custards warm, tepid, or cold.
  26. Pair with a sweet wine, such as Vouvray, Barsac, or sweet champagne.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ylC0z1SUNUQ

goose_with_prune_and_liver_stuffing.txt - Goose with Prune and Liver Stuffing

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare and cook a whole goose for a large gathering.
  • Master the techniques of trussing, browning, and braising a goose.
  • Explore different stuffing options for a goose, including prune and liver.

Ingredients

  • 9 pound goose
  • 1 quart and a half of stuffing
  • 1/2 cup of liver paste
  • 1/4 cup of dry white breadcrumbs
  • 2 tablespoons of parsley
  • 1/4 teaspoon of sage
  • 1/4 teaspoon of allspice
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 tablespoon of chopped scallion or shallot
  • 2 cups of red wine
  • 1/3 cup of flour
  • 2 sliced carrots
  • 2 sliced onions
  • 2 teaspoons of salt
  • Boiling water for basting
  • Prunes (amount depends on desired stuffing quantity)
  • Goose liver (optional)

Instructions

  1. Defrost the goose in the refrigerator for two to three days or in cold water for four to five hours.
  2. Prepare the prune and liver stuffing:
    • Pit the prunes by dropping them in boiling water for two to three minutes.
    • Sauté the chopped goose liver in butter until it stiffens slightly.
    • Add chopped scallion or shallot and sauté for about a minute or two.
    • Combine the sautéed liver mixture, liver paste, parsley, allspice, sage, and the sauté juice.
    • Deglaze the pan with port wine or stock, letting it boil down.
    • Stir in dry white breadcrumbs until the stuffing has enough body to easily stuff the prunes.
    • Stuff the prunes with a small teaspoon of the stuffing mixture.
  3. Truss the goose:
    • Cut off the wing tips and save them for stock.
    • Truss the wings to the body using a needle and thread.
    • Salt the cavity of the goose with two teaspoons of salt.
    • Stuff the goose with the prepared prunes.
    • Fold the tail over and truss the legs to the tail.
    • Prick the skin of the goose with a pin or needle to allow fat to render out during roasting.
    • Dry the goose thoroughly.
  4. Brown the goose:
    • Preheat oven to 450 degrees Fahrenheit.
    • Place the goose breast-side up in a roasting pan.
    • Brown the goose under the broiler for a few minutes, keeping a close eye on it to prevent burning.
    • Turn the goose over every two to three minutes to brown all sides.
  5. Prepare the sauce:
    • Chop the goose wings, giblets (heart, neck, and peeled giblets), and liver.
    • Brown the chopped ingredients in oil or rendered goose fat.
    • Add the sliced carrots and onions and brown them as well.
    • Stir in 1/3 cup of flour and cook until it takes on a light brown color.
    • Deglaze the pan with red wine, white wine, white vermouth, or meat stock.
    • Bring the mixture to a simmer and cook for two hours.
  6. Braise the goose:
    • Transfer the browned goose to a covered roasting pan with a rack.
    • Pour the sauce ingredients around the goose.
    • Bring the braising liquid to a simmer on the stovetop.
    • Season with salt.
    • Cover the pan and bake in a 325-degree oven for two hours.
  7. Finish the goose:
    • Remove the goose from the oven.
    • Untie the trussing strings.
    • Let the goose rest for 15 to 20 minutes before carving.
    • To check for doneness, wiggle the legs and press into the leg with a knife. The juice should be slightly rosy.
  8. Prepare the sauce:
    • Degrease the sauce by skimming off excess fat.
    • Strain the sauce through a strainer into a pan.
    • Bring the sauce to a simmer and reduce until thickened.
    • Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  9. Serve:
    • Pour some sauce over the goose.
    • Serve the remaining sauce in a warm sauce boat.
    • Accompany the goose with braised onions, carrots, and pureed chestnuts.
    • Enjoy with a red Burgundy wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SVY0hnZ-UzI

grissini_bread_sticks.txt - Grissini Breadsticks

Objectives

  • Learn how to make Grissini Breadsticks
  • Understand the importance of a long rise for Grissini Breadsticks
  • Learn how to shape Grissini Breadsticks

Ingredients

  • 1 1/3 cup of water (105-110 degrees F)
  • 1 1/2 teaspoon of yeast
  • 1/4 cup of olive oil (extra virgin)
  • 3 3/4 cups of unbleached all-purpose flour
  • 1 1/2 teaspoons of sea salt
  • Sesame seeds (optional)

Instructions

  1. Pour warm water into a bowl.
  2. Whisk in 1 1/2 teaspoons of yeast.
  3. Let the yeast mixture sit for 10 minutes until creamy.
  4. Add the yeast mixture to a mixer bowl.
  5. Add 1/4 cup of olive oil and whisk.
  6. Add 1 cup of flour and whisk until combined.
  7. Add the remaining 2 3/4 cups of flour and 1 1/2 teaspoons of salt.
  8. Using the paddle attachment, mix the dough for 1 minute.
  9. Turn the mixer to the dough hook attachment and knead for 3 minutes.
  10. Remove the dough from the mixer bowl and knead briefly by hand.
  11. Spread a thin layer of olive oil on a work surface.
  12. Stretch the dough into a rectangle approximately 16 inches by 10 inches.
  13. Roll out the dough with a rolling pin to maintain a rectangular shape.
  14. Brush the dough with olive oil.
  15. Cover the dough with plastic wrap and let it rise for 1 hour and 45 minutes.
  16. Oil a baking sheet.
  17. Using a pizza cutter, cut the dough into strips the width of a finger.
  18. Place the cut strips on the prepared baking sheet.
  19. Brush the Grissini with olive oil and sprinkle with sesame seeds if desired.
  20. Preheat oven to 400 degrees F.
  21. Bake the Grissini for 18-20 minutes until golden brown.
  22. Let the Grissini cool before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xwW4S2rRiZ0

ham_dinner.txt - Ham Dinner

Objectives

  • Create a quick and elegant 3-course meal in half an hour.
  • Prepare a delicious ham dinner with a French twist.
  • Master the art of flambéing cherries jubilee.

Ingredients

First Course:

  • 4 tomatoes
  • 1/4 cup butter
  • 2 shallots, chopped
  • 2 scallions, chopped
  • 3 eggs
  • salt and pepper
  • watercress
  • anchovies
  • capers
  • parsley

Main Course:

  • sliced ham
  • oil
  • butter
  • 2 tablespoons French mustard
  • 1 tablespoon tomato paste
  • heavy cream
  • scallions, chopped
  • 1/4 cup Madeira
  • canned beef bouillon
  • 1 cup frozen peas
  • 1/2 cup canned chicken stock
  • 1 1/2 tablespoons butter
  • watercress
  • leeks
  • salt

Dessert:

  • sour cherries
  • grated lemon rind
  • cognac
  • sugar
  • cinnamon
  • arrowroot
  • brandy
  • cherry juice
  • granulated sugar
  • vanilla ice cream

Instructions

  1. Macerate cherries: Combine sour cherries, lemon rind, cognac, sugar, and a pinch of cinnamon in a bowl. Set aside.
  2. Braise leeks: Wash leeks thoroughly, trimming off the roots. Cut in half and place in a pot with a small amount of boiling water, salt, and butter. Cover with aluminum foil and braise for 15-20 minutes.
  3. Cook peas: Defrost frozen peas in the refrigerator. Cook in chicken stock with salt and butter until tender.
  4. Prepare tomatoes: Cut tomatoes in half and squeeze out the juice. Scoop out the pulp with a grapefruit knife. Season with salt and drain upside down.
  5. Make cold scrambled eggs: Melt butter in a pan. Sauté shallots and scallions until softened. Beat 3 eggs with salt and pepper. Slowly scramble the eggs over low heat, stirring constantly until they are just set. Remove from heat and let cool.
  6. Assemble tomatoes: Line a dish with watercress. Fill tomatoes with cold scrambled eggs. Garnish with anchovies, capers, and parsley.
  7. Puree peas: Puree cooked peas and watercress in a food mill, using the coarse blade.
  8. Sauté ham: Heat oil and butter in a pan. Sauté ham slices until lightly browned on both sides. Remove from pan and set aside.
  9. Make ham sauce: Combine mustard, tomato paste, and cream in a bowl. Set aside.
  10. Finish ham sauce: Add chopped scallions to the pan where the ham was cooked. Pour in Madeira and beef bouillon. Bring to a boil and reduce until syrupy. Add ham sauce and stir to combine.
  11. Reheat ham: Return ham to the sauce and heat through.
  12. Assemble main course: Arrange pureed peas on a hot platter. Place ham on top of the peas. Spoon sauce over ham. Surround with braised leeks.
  13. Thicken cherries: Combine macerated cherries, arrowroot, and brandy in a saucepan. Bring to a simmer and cook until thickened and clear.
  14. Flame cherries: Add more brandy to the cherries and heat through. Sprinkle with granulated sugar. Flame the cherries using a heat-resistant device.
  15. Serve: Serve the ham dinner with chilled rosé wine and French bread. Serve cherries jubilee over vanilla ice cream while still flaming.

hearts_of_palm_stew.txt - Hearts of Palm Stew

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare hearts of palm for a stew
  • Master the technique of making a flavorful base for the stew
  • Discover how to cook yellowtail snapper for a delicious meal

Ingredients

  • 1 heart of palm
  • 1/2 cup lemon juice
  • 1/2 cup water
  • 2-3 cloves garlic
  • 1/2 cup olive oil
  • 1 stalk celery
  • 1 onion
  • 1 scotch bonnet pepper
  • 2 large tomatoes
  • 1 pound hearts of palm
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon black pepper
  • 2 tablespoons capers
  • 1/4 cup green olives
  • 1/4 cup fresh basil
  • 1/4 cup butter
  • 1 tablespoon fresh ginger
  • 1/4 cup diced mango
  • 1/4 cup fresh mint leaves
  • 1 tablespoon rum
  • 1/4 cup toasted macadamia nuts
  • 1 key lime

Instructions

  1. Remove the tough bottom portion of the heart of palm.
  2. Make a cut down through the palm to begin peeling.
  3. Continue peeling, discarding the outer layer and keeping the tender, white portion.
  4. Cut the peeled palm into rings.
  5. As you work, place the palm rings into a bowl of acidulated water (lemon juice and water) to prevent darkening.
  6. Slice the garlic thinly.
  7. Heat olive oil in a pan over medium heat.
  8. Sauté the garlic until lightly brown.
  9. Peel the celery and cut it on a bias.
  10. Dice the onion.
  11. Add the celery, onion, and a small piece of scotch bonnet pepper to the pan.
  12. Sweat the onions until translucent, making sure the vegetables do not brown.
  13. Drain the hearts of palm from the acidulated water.
  14. Core the tomatoes and blanch them in hot water for 20 seconds.
  15. Transfer the tomatoes to an ice bath to loosen the skin.
  16. Peel the tomatoes and squeeze out the seeds.
  17. Dice the tomatoes.
  18. Add the hearts of palm to the pan with the vegetables.
  19. Add a little of the lemon acidulated water, salt, and pepper to the pan.
  20. Rinse the capers and cut the green olives around the stone.
  21. Roll up the basil leaves and cut them finely into a chiffonade.
  22. Add the capers and green olives to the pan.
  23. Stir the stew and taste for seasoning.
  24. Add the basil to the stew.
  25. Set the stew aside and prepare the yellowtail snapper.
  26. Scale the yellowtail snapper.
  27. Carefully fillet the snapper, following the backbone and leaving a portion of the belly on.
  28. Remove the lateral bones from the fillets using a V-cut.
  29. Score the skin of the fillets to prevent curling during cooking.
  30. Season the fillets with salt and pepper.
  31. Lightly coat the fillets in flour and shake off any excess.
  32. Heat clarified butter in a pan over medium heat.
  33. Sear the fillets on the skin side until a crust forms.
  34. Flip the fillets and cook until just barely done.
  35. Remove the fillets from the pan and set them aside.
  36. Add the remaining butter to the pan and cook until it begins to brown.
  37. Add the ginger, diced mango, mint leaves, and rum to the pan.
  38. Flame the sauce to burn off the alcohol.
  39. Add the macadamia nuts to the sauce.
  40. Season the sauce with salt and pepper.
  41. Taste the sauce and adjust the seasoning as needed.
  42. Plate the fish fillets, skin-side up on one fillet and skin-side down on the other.
  43. Spoon a little of the butter sauce over the fish.
  44. Garnish with a squeeze of key lime.
  45. Serve the hearts of palm stew as a side dish.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pN5ytnNqkBo

instant_mashed_potatoes_mold_and_lamb_stew.txt - Tambour Parmentier with Ragoût à l'Improviste

Objectives

  • Learn to make a molded potato dish using instant mashed potatoes.
  • Improvise a flavorful stew using leftover roast lamb.
  • Create a visually appealing presentation for a simple meal.

Ingredients

For the Tambour Parmentier: - 1 1/2 packages of instant mashed potatoes (serves 6) - 3 3/4 cups boiling water - 6 tablespoons (3/4 stick) butter - 1 1/2 tablespoons salt - 3 egg yolks - 3/4 cup grated Swiss cheese - Pinch of nutmeg - 1/8 teaspoon pepper - 1/2 cup heavy cream - Softened butter - Wax paper - Bread crumbs

For the Ragoût à l'Improviste: - 3 1/2 - 4 cups chopped leftover roast lamb - 2 cups chopped onions - 1 cup chopped green peppers - Cooking oil - Red wine (about 1 cup or 1 1/2 cups) - Leftover lamb gravy - Smithfield Ham Spread - Canned mushroom juice - Canned beef bouillon - Fresh rosemary (almost a teaspoon) - Tomato paste - Bay leaf - 2 garlic cloves - Canned carrots - Butter - Canned mushrooms - Salt and pepper - Chopped parsley (optional) - Chopped scallions (optional)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Tambour Parmentier:
  2. Bring 3 3/4 cups of water to a boil.
  3. Combine the instant mashed potatoes with the boiling water, 6 tablespoons of butter, and 1 1/2 tablespoons of salt.
  4. Beat the mixture with a wire whip until smooth.
  5. Beat in 3 egg yolks, 3/4 cup grated Swiss cheese, a pinch of nutmeg, 1/8 teaspoon of pepper, and 1/2 cup heavy cream.
  6. Taste and adjust seasonings as needed.
  7. Prepare the Mold:
  8. Butter a 6-cup straight-sided baking dish heavily.
  9. Line the bottom of the dish with a piece of wax paper, cut to size.
  10. Sprinkle the bottom and sides of the dish with bread crumbs.
  11. Assemble the Tambour Parmentier:
  12. Pour the potato mixture into the prepared dish.
  13. Bake in a preheated 375-degree oven for about an hour, until puffed and browned.
  14. Prepare the Ragoût:
  15. Sauté 2 cups chopped onions and 1 cup chopped green peppers in a large pan with a small amount of cooking oil until lightly browned and softened (about 5-10 minutes).
  16. In a separate pan, brown the chopped leftover roast lamb in cooking oil.
  17. Season the browned lamb with salt and pepper.
  18. Sprinkle the lamb with about 1 tablespoon of flour per cup of sauce desired.
  19. Cook the lamb for 2-3 minutes, until the flour has lightly browned.
  20. Assemble the Ragoût:
  21. Remove the lamb from the pan and add about 1 cup or 1 1/2 cups of red wine to deglaze the pan.
  22. Add the lamb, the sautéed onions and peppers, leftover lamb gravy, Smithfield Ham Spread, canned mushroom juice, and enough canned beef bouillon to barely cover the meat to the casserole dish.
  23. Add almost a teaspoon of rosemary, a small amount of tomato paste, a bay leaf, and 2 garlic cloves pressed through a garlic press.
  24. Taste and adjust seasonings as needed.
  25. Simmer the Ragoût:
  26. Cover the casserole dish and simmer the stew for about an hour, until the meat is tender.
  27. Prepare the Vegetable Garniture:
  28. Sauté canned carrots in butter until lightly browned (about 3-4 minutes).
  29. Add canned mushrooms and sauté until lightly browned.
  30. Season the carrots and mushrooms with salt and pepper.
  31. Finish the Ragoût:
  32. Add the sautéed carrots and mushrooms to the simmered stew.
  33. Baste the stew with the sauce.
  34. Unmold the Tambour Parmentier:
  35. Remove the baked potato mold from the oven.
  36. Let cool slightly.
  37. Run a knife around the edge of the mold to loosen the potatoes.
  38. Invert the mold onto a buttered serving platter.
  39. Carefully peel off the wax paper.
  40. Serve:
  41. Arrange the Tambour Parmentier on a serving platter.
  42. Surround the potato mold with the Ragoût à l'Improviste.
  43. Serve immediately with a green salad and French bread.
  44. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=81y-3-LBRZc

ladyfingers_charlotte_malakoff.txt - Ladyfingers and Charlotte Malakoff

Objectives

  • Learn to make homemade ladyfingers from scratch
  • Understand the importance of proper ingredient proportions and techniques
  • Learn to assemble and chill a classic French dessert, Charlotte Malakoff

Ingredients

Ladyfingers - 3 large egg yolks - 1/2 cup granulated sugar - 1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract - 3 large egg whites - 1/8 teaspoon salt - 1/4 teaspoon cream of tartar - 1 tablespoon granulated sugar - 2/3 cup sifted cake flour - Powdered sugar, for coating

Charlotte Malakoff - 2 sticks unsalted butter - 1 cup instant superfine sugar - 1/4 cup orange liqueur - 1 cup melted chocolate (melted with 2 tablespoons strong coffee) - 1 1/3 cup pulverized almonds - 1/4 teaspoon almond extract - 1 cup heavy cream - Grated bitter chocolate, for garnish (optional)

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 300 degrees F (150 degrees C).
  2. Prepare baking sheet by rubbing with softened butter and dusting with all-purpose flour.
  3. In a mixer bowl, beat 3 large egg yolks with 1/2 cup granulated sugar until pale and thick.
  4. In a separate bowl, beat 3 large egg whites with 1/8 teaspoon salt and 1/4 teaspoon cream of tartar until soft peaks form.
  5. Gradually add 1 tablespoon granulated sugar to the egg whites and continue beating until stiff peaks form.
  6. Fold the beaten egg whites into the egg yolk mixture.
  7. Sift 2/3 cup cake flour over the mixture and fold gently until just combined.
  8. Transfer the batter to a pastry bag fitted with a 3/8-inch nozzle or use a spoon to form ladyfingers on the prepared baking sheet.
  9. Dust the ladyfingers generously with powdered sugar.
  10. Bake in preheated oven for 20 minutes, or until lightly browned and the powdered sugar remains white.
  11. Transfer the baked ladyfingers to a wire rack to cool completely.
  12. Prepare the Charlotte Malakoff filling:
    • In a mixer bowl, cream 2 sticks of unsalted butter with 1 cup instant superfine sugar until light and fluffy.
    • Add 1/4 cup orange liqueur and 1 cup melted chocolate to the creamed butter mixture and mix well.
    • Stir in 1 1/3 cup pulverized almonds and 1/4 teaspoon almond extract.
  13. Whip 1 cup heavy cream until soft peaks form.
  14. Gently fold the whipped cream into the chocolate mixture.
  15. Prepare the Charlotte Malakoff mold:
    • Line the bottom of a high-sided, cylindrical dessert mold with a round of wax paper.
    • Arrange the ladyfingers around the sides of the mold, curved ends facing out.
    • Place additional ladyfingers in the bottom of the mold.
  16. Fill the mold with the chocolate mixture, alternating layers of mixture and ladyfingers.
  17. Cover the top of the mold with wax paper and place a plate or saucer on top as a weight.
  18. Refrigerate the Charlotte Malakoff for at least 6 hours, or overnight, to set.
  19. To unmold, run a thin knife around the edge of the mold and carefully invert it onto a serving dish.
  20. Garnish with grated bitter chocolate, if desired.
  21. Serve chilled.

Note: This recipe can be made ahead of time and will keep well in the refrigerator for 2-3 days.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PV-cDho1cwY

lamb_renaissance.txt - Roast Leg of Lamb in the "Renaissance" Manner

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a roast leg of lamb using a Renaissance-inspired recipe
  • Discover how to create a flavorful marinade for the lamb
  • Master the art of making a pan sauce to complement the roasted lamb

Ingredients

  • 10-pound leg of lamb
  • 4 large oranges (zest and juice)
  • 6 cloves garlic
  • 1/3 cup fresh basil leaves
  • 3 tablespoons olive oil
  • 1 tablespoon lemon juice
  • 1/2 cup salted anchovies
  • 1 cup dry red wine
  • 1 cup chicken or poultry stock
  • 1 tablespoon tomato paste
  • 1 cup black olives
  • 1 pound pre-cooked green beans
  • 1/2 cup toasted walnuts
  • Salt and freshly ground black pepper to taste
  • Optional: a small amount of water for basting

Instructions

  1. Remove the sirloin chop from the leg of lamb and set aside.
  2. Trim the excess fat and skin from the leg of lamb, leaving a thin layer of fat for flavor.
  3. Using a sharp knife, make deep slits all over the leg of lamb, about an inch deep.
  4. Zest the oranges and blanch the zest in boiling water for 3 minutes.
  5. Peel the garlic cloves and remove the skin.
  6. Rinse the salted anchovies and remove the bones.
  7. In a bowl, combine the garlic, anchovies, basil, olive oil, lemon juice, and blanched orange zest.
  8. Using a mortar and pestle, coarsely crush the ingredients together, leaving some texture.
  9. Rub the marinade all over the leg of lamb, making sure to get into the slits.
  10. Refrigerate the marinated lamb overnight.
  11. Preheat the oven to 350°F (175°C).
  12. Remove the lamb from the refrigerator and season both sides with salt and black pepper.
  13. Place the lamb in a roasting pan and roast for 20 minutes.
  14. Pour 1 cup of dry red wine into the roasting pan.
  15. Continue roasting the lamb, basting every 10-15 minutes with the pan juices.
  16. After 20 minutes of roasting, add the black olives to the roasting pan.
  17. Continue roasting the lamb until the internal temperature reaches 135°F (57°C) for a medium-rare doneness.
  18. Transfer the lamb to a turned-off oven with the door slightly ajar to rest for 20 minutes.
  19. While the lamb is resting, prepare the pan sauce.
  20. Pour the pan juices into a saucepan and bring to a simmer.
  21. Deglaze the pan with 1 cup of chicken or poultry stock, scraping up any browned bits from the bottom.
  22. Add 1 tablespoon of tomato paste to the pan sauce and simmer until reduced by half.
  23. Season the pan sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  24. Sauté the green beans in a pan with olive oil until heated through.
  25. Add the mortadella to the green beans and sauté until warmed.
  26. Serve the roasted leg of lamb with the pan sauce, green beans with mortadella, and toasted walnuts.
  27. Enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BdgjRpoQW-0

langue_du_boeuf_braise_a_la_menagere.txt - Langue de Bœuf Braisée à la Ménagère

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare and braise a beef tongue.
  • Create a flavorful sauce using aromatic vegetables and stock.
  • Assemble a beautiful and delicious platter with braised tongue, vegetables, and mashed potatoes.

Ingredients

  • 1 beef tongue (3 1/2 pounds, trimmed)
  • Kosher salt
  • 1 1/2 teaspoons salt (if not salting the tongue)
  • 1/2 cup onions, finely diced
  • 1/2 cup carrots, finely diced
  • 1/2 cup celery, finely diced
  • 1/4 cup diced ham
  • 2 tablespoons butter
  • 3 cups beef stock
  • 1 tablespoon tomato paste
  • 1/2 teaspoon thyme
  • 2 heaping teaspoons arrowroot
  • Port wine (for mixing with arrowroot)
  • Bay leaf
  • Mashed potatoes
  • Carrots and onions (parboiled)

Instructions

  1. Scrub the beef tongue under warm water with a vegetable brush.
  2. Soak the tongue in several changes of cold water for 2 hours.
  3. Optionally, salt the tongue by placing it in a bowl with a layer of kosher salt, covering it with more salt, and weighting it down. Let it sit for 2-3 days.
  4. If salting the tongue, wipe off the salt and wash the tongue under cold water before cooking.
  5. Bring a large pot of water to a boil.
  6. If you salted the tongue, add it to the boiling water without additional salt.
  7. If you did not salt the tongue, add 1 1/2 teaspoons of salt per quart of water.
  8. Skim off any scum that forms on the surface of the water.
  9. Reduce the heat to a slow boil or simmer for 2 hours.
  10. Remove the tongue from the pot and allow it to cool slightly.
  11. Peel the skin off the tongue. Start by slitting the skin along the edge between the top and bottom.
  12. Peel the skin off the top of the tongue, working your way down.
  13. Use a knife to peel the skin off the thick end of the tongue.
  14. Peel the skin off the sides of the tongue, loosening it with your hands.
  15. To peel the underside of the tongue, slit it in strips with a knife and peel away the skin.
  16. Trim off any inedible parts from the tongue.
  17. Slice the tongue into 3/8 inch thick slices.
  18. To make the braising sauce, sauté the diced onions, carrots, celery, and ham in butter for 10 minutes until lightly browned.
  19. Add the beef stock, tomato paste, and thyme to the pan.
  20. Simmer the sauce for 30 minutes.
  21. Thicken the sauce with arrowroot mixed with port wine. Simmer for 1 minute.
  22. Taste the sauce and adjust seasoning as needed.
  23. Place the tongue slices in a flat pan.
  24. Add the parboiled carrots and onions to the pan.
  25. Pour the braising sauce over the tongue and vegetables.
  26. Simmer for 30 minutes or until the tongue is tender.
  27. To serve, mound the mashed potatoes on a hot platter.
  28. Arrange the tongue slices around the potatoes.
  29. Place the cooked vegetables around the tongue.
  30. Drizzle some of the braising sauce over the tongue and vegetables.
  31. Serve with a red Bordeaux wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zDftfdS5ppY

lasagna_a_la_francaise.txt - Lasagna à la Française

Objectives

  • Prepare a quick and easy lasagna dish for unexpected guests.
  • Learn to make a classic French-style lasagna with a focus on simplicity and flavor.
  • Understand the importance of using quality ingredients and proper cooking techniques.

Ingredients

  • 1 box lasagna noodles
  • 3 tablespoons coarse salt
  • 1 large onion, chopped
  • 10 fresh tomatoes
  • 1 can Italian plum tomatoes
  • 1/2 teaspoon Italian seasoning
  • salt and pepper to taste
  • 1/2 teaspoon saffron (optional)
  • dried orange peel (optional)
  • 1/2 cup chicken stock
  • 3 cups white sauce (béchamel)
  • 1/4 cup vermouth
  • 1 large clove garlic, minced
  • 1/2 cup leftover provolone cheese
  • 1/2 cup leftover Swiss cheese
  • 1/2 cup Parmesan cheese
  • 1 cup leftover chicken, poached in white wine
  • 1 cup leftover spinach
  • 1 cup leftover sautéed mushrooms
  • 1/2 cup leftover cottage cheese
  • Olive oil
  • 1/2 cup grated cheese (for topping)

Instructions

  1. Boil a large pot of water with 3 tablespoons of coarse salt.
  2. Add the lasagna noodles to the boiling water and cook for 13 minutes.
  3. While the noodles are cooking, chop the onion and set aside.
  4. Blanch the fresh tomatoes in boiling water for 10 seconds, then peel and seed them.
  5. Squeeze the tomatoes over a sieve to extract the juice and seeds.
  6. Roughly chop the fresh tomato pulp.
  7. Put the canned tomatoes through a food mill to remove the seeds.
  8. Sauté the chopped onions in olive oil for 10-15 minutes, until translucent.
  9. Add the fresh tomato pulp and canned tomatoes to the onions.
  10. Season with Italian seasoning, salt, pepper, saffron (optional), and dried orange peel (optional).
  11. Simmer the tomato sauce for at least 30 minutes, or up to an hour, for optimal flavor.
  12. Drain the cooked lasagna noodles and rinse with cold water.
  13. Arrange the noodles in a single layer on a baking sheet to prevent sticking.
  14. In a saucepan, combine the white sauce, chicken stock, and vermouth.
  15. Simmer the white sauce with the onions for a few minutes to blend flavors.
  16. Add the minced garlic to the tomato sauce.
  17. Continue to cook the tomato sauce until the onions practically disappear.
  18. Grease a lasagna baking dish with olive oil.
  19. Layer the lasagna dish with a bottom layer of lasagna noodles.
  20. Spread a thin layer of white sauce over the noodles.
  21. Top with half of the spinach, followed by half of the provolone, Swiss, and Parmesan cheese.
  22. Add half of the chicken and half of the sautéed mushrooms.
  23. Layer with another layer of lasagna noodles.
  24. Repeat layers 20-22, using the remaining ingredients.
  25. Top with a final layer of lasagna noodles.
  26. Spread a generous layer of white sauce over the top.
  27. Drizzle with tomato sauce, leaving some for the sides.
  28. Sprinkle with a generous amount of grated cheese.
  29. Bake in a 400° oven for 30 minutes, or until the top is browned and bubbly.
  30. Let the lasagna cool slightly before serving.
  31. Serve immediately and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vijibDontnU

watercress_soup.txt - Watercress Soup

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic French leek and potato soup.
  • Understand the variations of this soup, including vichyssoise and watercress soup.
  • Learn how to use a pressure cooker safely and effectively.

Ingredients

  • 3-4 cups leeks, chopped
  • 3-4 cups potatoes, chopped
  • 1 quart water
  • 2 teaspoons salt
  • 2 cups milk (optional, added just before serving)
  • Heavy cream (optional, added just before serving)
  • Butter (optional, added just before serving)

Instructions

  1. Wash leeks thoroughly by splitting them lengthwise and rubbing each leaf under cold water.
  2. Chop leeks into roughly 1-inch pieces, including the green part.
  3. Chop potatoes into roughly 1-inch pieces.
  4. Combine leeks, potatoes, water, and salt in a pressure cooker.
  5. Secure the lid of the pressure cooker and bring to high heat.
  6. Once steam begins to vent, set a timer for 5 minutes.
  7. After 5 minutes, release the pressure by running the pressure cooker under cold water until a hissing sound is heard.
  8. Remove the lid and simmer the soup uncovered for 10-15 minutes.
  9. Taste the soup and add more salt if needed.
  10. For a richer flavor, add 2 cups of milk just before serving.
  11. Optionally, mash the vegetables with a fork or potato masher for a more rustic texture.
  12. To further enrich the soup, add a dollop of heavy cream and a pat of butter just before serving.

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a delicate and refreshing French watercress soup.
  • Understand the importance of properly cooking the leeks or onions for added flavor.
  • Discover tips for storing and preparing watercress.

Ingredients

  • 2/3 cup leeks or onions, chopped
  • 1 bunch watercress
  • 3 tablespoons flour
  • 4 cups light chicken stock or canned chicken bouillon and water
  • 2 egg yolks
  • 1/2 cup cream
  • Butter (optional, added just before serving)

Instructions

  1. Sauté the chopped leeks or onions in butter over low heat until soft and limp.
  2. Wash and chop the watercress, keeping the stems as they are tender.
  3. Add the watercress to the pan with the leeks or onions and cook over medium heat until wilted.
  4. Stir in 3 tablespoons of flour and cook for 1-2 minutes.
  5. Gradually whisk in 4 cups of hot chicken stock or bouillon and water.
  6. Simmer the soup for 5 minutes.
  7. To enrich the soup, whisk together 2 egg yolks and 1/2 cup cream.
  8. Slowly pour the hot soup into the egg yolk mixture, whisking constantly.
  9. Cook the soup over moderate heat, stirring constantly, until it thickens slightly.
  10. For an extra touch of richness, add a pat of butter just before serving.
  11. Season the soup with salt and pepper to taste.
  12. Serve hot or chilled.

lobster_a_l_americaine.txt - Homard à l'Américaine

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare and cook a classic French lobster dish, Homard à l'Américaine.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh, lively lobsters and proper techniques for chopping and sautéing.
  • Master the art of creating a rich and flavorful sauce using lobster coral, mirepoix, and various flavorings.

Ingredients

  • 1 lobster, approximately 1 1/4 pounds (chicken lobster)
  • 1/2 cup light olive oil or cooking oil
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1/4 cup cognac
  • 1 cup dry white wine or 3/4 cup dry white vermouth
  • 1/4 cup beef bouillon (homemade or canned)
  • 1/2 cup fish stock or canned clam juice
  • 6 tomatoes
  • 2 tablespoons tomato paste
  • 1 clove garlic
  • 2 tablespoons tarragon (dry leaves)
  • 2 tablespoons parsley
  • 3 tablespoons softened butter
  • 3 tablespoons lobster coral (green matter)
  • Rice or French bread for serving

Instructions

  1. Chop the lobster.
  2. Cut off the claws first using a large knife.
  3. Cut through the underpart of the lobster with scissors or lobster shears.
  4. Cut through the back of the shell and then down through the middle with a knife.
  5. Break the lobster apart.
  6. Remove the sand sac and intestinal vein.
  7. Reserve the lobster coral and green matter in a bowl.
  8. Chop the lobster into bite-sized pieces, saving scraps for soup.
  9. Sauté the lobster.
  10. Heat the olive oil in a large, heavy pan (chicken fryer) over medium-high heat.
  11. When the oil is hot, add the lobster pieces, flesh side down.
  12. Sauté for 1-2 minutes per side, until the shells turn red.
  13. Season with salt and pepper.
  14. Add mirepoix and green onions.
  15. Add 2-3 tablespoons of finely diced carrots and onions (mirepoix) that have been cooked in butter.
  16. Add 2 tablespoons of finely chopped green onions or shallots.
  17. Flame with cognac.
  18. Add 1/2 cup cognac and ignite with a match.
  19. Shake the pan to distribute the flames.
  20. Add wine or vermouth and other liquids.
  21. Extinguish the flames with 1 cup of dry white wine or 3/4 cup of dry white vermouth.
  22. Add 1/4 cup beef bouillon and 1/2 cup fish stock or canned clam juice.
  23. Add tomatoes, tomato paste, garlic, and herbs.
  24. Peel and chop 6 tomatoes, removing the seeds and juice.
  25. Add the chopped tomatoes to the pan.
  26. Add 2 tablespoons of tomato paste.
  27. Press 1 clove of garlic into the pan.
  28. Add 2 tablespoons of tarragon and 2 tablespoons of parsley.
  29. Simmer for 20 minutes.
  30. Reduce the heat to low, cover the pan, and simmer for 20 minutes.
  31. Prepare the lobster coral sauce.
  32. Combine the lobster coral and softened butter in a sieve.
  33. Push the mixture through the sieve with a masher or wooden spoon.
  34. Use a rubber spatula to push any remaining coral through.
  35. Reduce the sauce.
  36. Remove the lobster from the pan and set aside.
  37. Bring the sauce to a simmer and reduce until it thickens slightly.
  38. Taste the sauce and adjust seasoning as needed.
  39. Return the lobster to the sauce.
  40. Return the lobster to the sauce and let it heat through.
  41. Thicken the sauce with lobster coral.
  42. Warm the lobster coral mixture over low heat.
  43. Gradually add the hot sauce to the coral mixture, whisking constantly.
  44. Pour the thickened sauce back into the pan with the lobster.
  45. Serve.
  46. Serve the lobster à l'Américaine in its shell, with rice or French bread.
  47. Garnish with chopped parsley.
  48. Serve with a chilled, full-bodied white wine, such as Côtes du Rhône.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XUzr0OTFBak

lobster_souffle.txt - Lobster Souffle

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare a classic lobster souffle
  • Understand the importance of steaming lobsters for the souffle
  • Discover how to make a sauce americaine for the souffle

Ingredients

  • 4 live lobsters
  • 4 cups water
  • 1 cup white wine
  • 1/2 cup tomato juice
  • 2 bay leaves
  • 2 teaspoons paprika
  • 1/2 teaspoon fennel seed
  • 1/4 teaspoon cayenne pepper
  • 1 tablespoon herbes de provence
  • 2 tablespoons butter
  • 3 tablespoons flour
  • 1 cup hot milk
  • 3 egg yolks
  • 1/2 cup Swiss cheese
  • 1/4 cup Parmesan cheese
  • 1 tablespoon potato starch
  • 1/2 cup cream
  • 1 tablespoon cognac
  • 1 tablespoon fresh tarragon

Instructions

  1. Steam the lobsters for 12 minutes.
  2. Break the lobsters apart and remove the meat.
  3. Save the tomalley, roe, and juices.
  4. Strain the juices and set aside.
  5. Saute celery, garlic, and onion in olive oil.
  6. Add the lobster carcasses to the sauteed vegetables.
  7. Flambe with cognac.
  8. Add white wine, lobster juice, tomato juice, bay leaves, paprika, fennel seed, cayenne pepper, and herbes de provence.
  9. Simmer for 20-30 minutes.
  10. Strain the sauce and reduce to 1 1/2 cups.
  11. Butter a springform pan and coat with a mixture of breadcrumbs, paprika, and Parmesan cheese.
  12. Make a classic bechamel sauce by melting butter and flour, whisking in hot milk, and then adding egg yolks.
  13. Beat egg whites until stiff peaks form.
  14. Fold the egg whites into the bechamel sauce.
  15. Add the Swiss cheese and lobster meat.
  16. Pour the mixture into the prepared pan.
  17. Bake at 375 degrees for 30-35 minutes.
  18. Thicken the sauce with potato starch and add cream and cognac.
  19. Garnish with fresh tarragon.
  20. Serve the lobster souffle with the sauce and lobster claws.
