potato_recipes.txt - Potato Recipes

Objectives

  • Explore diverse potato dishes beyond basic preparations.
  • Learn to cook four unique potato recipes: gratin dauphinois, sausage and potato casserole, mashed potato pancakes, and potato pancakes with ham and eggs.
  • Understand the importance of potato variety and cooking methods for different dishes.

Ingredients

Gratin Dauphinois - Potatoes (boiling potatoes) - Milk - Butter - Garlic (1 clove) - Salt - Pepper

Sausage and Potato Casserole - Potatoes (boiling potatoes, sliced and boiled) - Onions (cooked slowly in butter until tender) - Polish sausage - Light cream - Eggs (2) - Grated Swiss cheese - Butter

Mashed Potato Pancakes - Potatoes (raw, grated) - Cream cheese (4 ounces) - Egg (1) - Salt - Pepper - Grated Swiss cheese (2/3 cup, diced 1/4 inch thick) - Butter - Oil

Potato Pancakes with Ham and Eggs - Mashed potato pancake mixture (from previous recipe) - Diced ham - Onions (cooked slowly in butter until tender) - Poached eggs - Tomato sauce (simmered with diced ham, onions, and herbs) - Parsley

Instructions

  1. Gratin Dauphinois:
  2. Peel and thinly slice potatoes.
  3. Dip potatoes in water to remove starchy coating.
  4. Drain potatoes.
  5. Heat milk in a fireproof dish.
  6. Add garlic, salt, and pepper to milk.
  7. Add sliced potatoes to milk mixture, ensuring dish is no more than 2 inches high.
  8. Top with butter.

  9. Bake in a 450-degree oven for 20 minutes.

  10. Sausage and Potato Casserole:

  11. Butter an oven-proof dish.
  12. Layer boiled potatoes, onions, Polish sausage, and more potatoes in the dish.
  13. Beat eggs with cream.
  14. Pour egg and cream mixture over potato layers.
  15. Sprinkle with grated Swiss cheese.
  16. Top with butter.

  17. Bake until heated through and cheese is melted.

  18. Mashed Potato Pancakes:

  19. Grate raw potatoes until you have 2 cups.
  20. Squeeze grated potatoes in a clean towel to remove excess water.
  21. Combine potatoes with cream cheese, egg, salt, and pepper.
  22. Mix in diced Swiss cheese.
  23. Heat butter and oil in a pan.

  24. Pour potato mixture into pan and cook for 3-4 minutes per side, or until golden brown.

  25. Potato Pancakes with Ham and Eggs:

  26. Prepare mashed potato pancakes as in the previous recipe.
  27. Top pancakes with diced ham, cooked onions, poached eggs, tomato sauce, and parsley.
  28. Serve immediately.

Tips and Notes:

  • For best results, use boiling potatoes for gratin dauphinois and sausage and potato casserole.
  • When squeezing grated potatoes, use a clean towel to avoid discoloration.
  • Don't be afraid to experiment with different fillings and toppings for potato pancakes.
  • Poached eggs can be made ahead of time and reheated in hot water.
  • Serve potato dishes with green vegetables, salads, bread, and chilled rosé wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PeYsNMn_35E

pot_au_feu.txt - Pot-au-Feu

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional French pot-au-feu, a boiled beef dinner.
  • Understand the importance of using cheaper cuts of meat and bones for boiling.
  • Explore different techniques for cooking vegetables to ensure they are cooked perfectly.

Ingredients

  • 4 quarts of bones (knuckle bones and bones with meat)
  • 1 boneless chuck (including flunken and undercut)
  • 1 large onion
  • 3 cloves garlic
  • 1 leek
  • 1 celery stalk
  • 1 bunch parsley
  • 1 bay leaf
  • 1 teaspoon dried thyme
  • 1 tablespoon coarse salt
  • 1 cup water
  • 4 white turnips
  • 2 parsnips
  • 1 savoy cabbage
  • 2-3 carrots
  • 2-3 onions
  • 4-5 potatoes
  • French bread
  • Red wine

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 450 degrees Fahrenheit.
  2. Brown the bones in the oven for about 30 minutes, basting them with the rendered fat.
  3. Transfer the browned bones to a large pot.
  4. Deglaze the roasting pan with water and scrape the bottom with a wooden spoon to collect the flavorful residue.
  5. Add the deglazed liquid to the pot with the bones.
  6. Add the chopped onion, carrots, leek, celery, garlic cloves, and parsley to the pot.
  7. Add 1 tablespoon of coarse salt and 2-3 cloves of garlic to the pot.
  8. Wrap the bay leaf, parsley, and thyme in cheesecloth to create a bouquet garni and add it to the pot.
  9. Add enough water to cover the bones by 2-3 inches.
  10. Bring the pot to a simmer and skim off any scum that rises to the surface.
  11. Cover the pot partially and simmer for 8 hours.
  12. Remove the bones from the stock and strain the broth.
  13. Degrease the stock and set aside.
  14. Tie the boneless chuck with string to keep it together during cooking.
  15. Add the tied chuck to the stock and simmer for 2-3 hours.
  16. Peel and cut the turnips into quarters or halves.
  17. Peel and cut the parsnips into quarters.
  18. Cut the cabbage in half, remove the core, and cut into three wedges.
  19. Steam the cabbage in a sieve or vegetable steamer with a little bit of stock, salt, and pepper for about 10 minutes.
  20. Cook the turnips and parsnips in a separate pot with a cup of stock and a little bit of salt for about 10 minutes.
  21. Cook the carrots and onions in a separate pot with a little bit of stock until tender.
  22. Remove the chuck from the stock and let it rest for 20 minutes before carving.
  23. Carve the chuck into slices, cutting across the grain.
  24. Reheat the vegetables before serving.
  25. To assemble the pot-au-feu, arrange the carved meat, vegetables, and potatoes on a large platter.
  26. Pour the stock over the meat and vegetables.
  27. Serve the pot-au-feu with French bread and red wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JqGFwrsKK_g

pot_au_normand.txt - Pot au Normand

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French boiled dinner called Pot au Normand
  • Understand how to tie and cook different meats for a one-pot meal
  • Discover the benefits of using cheesecloth for easy vegetable removal

Ingredients

  • 6 lbs beef chuck (undercut)
  • 4 lbs pork shoulder (butt)
  • 1 stewing chicken (about 5.5 lbs)
  • 1 smoked Polish sausage
  • 2-3 leeks
  • 4 carrots
  • 3 cloves garlic
  • 4 bay leaves
  • 1/2 teaspoon thyme
  • 1/4 cup parsley
  • 1 cup diced onions (sautéed in butter)
  • 1 cup bread crumbs (stale)
  • 1/2 cup butter
  • 1 egg
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • Freshly ground black pepper
  • Kosher salt
  • Water

Instructions

  1. Tie the beef chuck with string to maintain its shape while cooking.
  2. Tie the pork shoulder with string.
  3. Truss the chicken:
  4. Place wings akimbo.
  5. Poke a knitting needle through the legs and bring the string out.
  6. Tie the string around the neck end of the chicken.
  7. Put a little salt in the cavity.
  8. Stuff the chicken with the breadcrumb and giblet mixture, leaving about an inch of space.
  9. Tie the other end of the chicken.
  10. Place the tied beef, pork, and chicken in a large pot.
  11. Add enough water to cover the meats and future vegetables.
  12. Add 2-3 tablespoons of kosher salt to the pot.
  13. Tie the leeks, carrots, garlic, bay leaves, and thyme in cheesecloth.
  14. Add the cheesecloth bundles to the pot.
  15. Bring the pot to a boil, then reduce heat and simmer for 2.5-3 hours.
  16. Add the Polish sausage to the pot 30 minutes before serving.
  17. Remove the meats and vegetables from the pot using the cheesecloth.
  18. Arrange the meats and vegetables on a platter for serving.
  19. Serve with rosé or red wine, French bread, and rice or potatoes simmered in the soup stock.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Wawjiso77zQ

poularde_demi_desosse.txt - Poularde Demi Désossé (Boned Chicken Breast)

Objectives

  • Learn how to bone a chicken breast for a poularde demi désossé.
  • Discover the French technique for stuffing and trussing a boned chicken.
  • Explore the history and variations of the Albufera stuffing.

Ingredients

  • 1 roasting chicken (4 1/2 pounds)
  • 2 cups stuffing (recipe for Albufera provided)
  • 1/4 teaspoon cognac (optional)
  • Salt to taste
  • Butter for massaging the chicken

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Chicken:
  2. Remove the giblets, neck, and fat from the chicken.
  3. Remove the wishbone by cutting on either side and twisting it out.
  4. Remove the fat glands at the base of the tail.
  5. Bone the Breast:
  6. Slit the skin on top of the breast from the neck to the tail.
  7. Peel the skin back on both sides.
  8. Cut down one side of the breastbone, scraping the meat against the bone.
  9. Continue cutting and peeling the meat until you reach the end of the white meat.
  10. Repeat on the other side of the breastbone.
  11. Separate the breast meat into two pieces, the filet mignon and the fillet.
  12. Remove the tendon from the filet mignon.
  13. Prepare the Carcass:
  14. Cut the breastbone and half of the rib cage off the carcass, leaving a boat shape.
  15. Season the cavity with salt and a few drops of cognac, if desired.
  16. Cut the breast meat into strips about 1/2 inch wide.
  17. Season the breast meat with salt and a few drops of cognac, if desired.
  18. Assemble the Chicken:
  19. Push the legs back under the shoulder blades and secure with a skewer.
  20. Place the breast meat strips lengthwise on top of the stuffing in the carcass.
  21. Fold the skin over the breast meat, tucking in any loose edges.
  22. Truss the Chicken:
  23. Thread a needle with white string and tie a knot at the end.
  24. Sew up the skin along the back of the chicken, starting at the tail.
  25. Turn the chicken over and attach the stuffing at the back end.
  26. Truss the legs by sewing a string under the knees and then under the wings.
  27. Truss the tail by sewing a string under the tail and then under one of the drumsticks.
  28. Secure any gaps with a trussing pin if needed.
  29. Massage and Cook:
  30. Massage the chicken with butter.
  31. Cook the chicken in the oven or poach it in a covered casserole with wine and herbs.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dc3dAV5Jf1I

pressed_duck_rouennaise.txt - Canard à la Rouennaise (Pressed Duck)

Objectives

  • Learn to make pressed duck à la Rouennaise, a classic French dish.
  • Understand the process of pressing duck and creating the accompanying sauce.
  • Explore the difference between pressed duck and duck salmis.

Ingredients

  • 1 duck (about 4.5 pounds)
  • Red Burgundy wine
  • Cognac
  • Dijon mustard
  • Fine dry bread crumbs (chapelure)
  • Sea salt
  • Black pepper
  • Minced shallots
  • Duck stock (made with wing ends, neck, gizzard, carrots, onions, chicken stock, wine, and seasoning)
  • Arrowroot
  • Unsalted butter
  • Raw duck liver

Instructions

  1. Roast the duck in a 450-degree oven for 20 minutes.
  2. Carve the duck:
  3. Remove a leg.
  4. Cut down the center of the breast.
  5. Remove the skin from the breast.
  6. Slice the breast meat very thinly and parallel to the cutting board.
  7. Slice the top of the wing.
  8. Separate the drumstick from the second joint of the leg.
  9. Remove the lower part of the wing.
  10. Trim excess fat from the legs and wings.
  11. Prepare the legs and wings:
  12. Spread Dijon mustard on each side of the legs and wings.
  13. Roll in bread crumbs.
  14. Place on a platter.
  15. Bake in a 400-degree oven for 20 minutes.
  16. Prepare the duck carcass for the sauce:
  17. Chop the carcass.
  18. Saute in hot oil for 2-3 minutes until lightly browned.
  19. Make the sauce:
  20. Add 2-3 ladles of duck stock to the browned carcass.
  21. Add red Burgundy wine.
  22. Simmer for 30-40 minutes.
  23. For salmis, thicken the sauce with arrowroot.
  24. For pressed duck, the sauce will naturally thicken from the juices.
  25. Prepare the liver:
  26. Press the raw duck liver through a sieve with 2 tablespoons of softened butter.
  27. Add a small amount of the thickened sauce.
  28. Finish the salmis sauce:
  29. Gently reheat the sauce with the liver.
  30. Add 2-3 tablespoons of cognac.
  31. Season with salt, pepper, and a sprinkle of shallots.
  32. Light the cognac and let it burn out.
  33. Strain the sauce over the thinly sliced duck.
  34. Poach the duck meat:
  35. Gently heat the duck meat in the sauce over a chafing dish flame.
  36. This will poach the meat and ensure it is cooked through.
  37. Serve:
  38. Serve the duck meat with the sauce.
  39. Optionally, serve the legs and wings separately.
  40. Pair with a good Burgundy wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=R-dV4RiuUiI

puff_pastry_ham_tart.txt - Puff Pastry Ham Tart (Feuillete au Jambon)

Objectives

  • Learn to make French puff pastry (pate feuillete) from scratch.
  • Understand the importance of chilling and resting the dough.
  • Create a delicious and elegant ham tart using puff pastry.

Ingredients

Dough (Detrempe) - 2 3/4 cups all-purpose flour (AP flour) - 3/4 cup cake flour - 2 teaspoons salt - 1/4 cup salad oil - 1 cup ice water

Butter Mixture - 3 1/2 sticks chilled butter - 1/2 cup mixed flours (from reserved dough)

Ham Tart Filling - 2 cups ham pieces - 1 1/2 cups cream sauce (with egg yolk) - 1/2 cup mixed Parmesan and Swiss cheese

Glaze - 1 whole egg - 1 teaspoon water

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Dough (Detrempe):
  2. Combine 2 3/4 cups all-purpose flour and 3/4 cup cake flour in a bowl.
  3. Remove 1/2 cup of the mixed flour and set aside.
  4. Add 2 teaspoons salt, 1/4 cup salad oil, and 1 cup ice water to the remaining flour mixture.
  5. Mix well to form a rough dough.
  6. Shape the dough into a ball and set aside.
  7. Prepare the Butter Mixture:
  8. Beat 3 1/2 sticks of chilled butter with a rolling pin until softened.
  9. Spread the softened butter with the heel of your hand until malleable but still cold.
  10. Add the 1/2 cup of reserved flour to the butter.
  11. Roll Out the Dough:
  12. Gently press and push the dough into a rectangle approximately 16 inches long and 8 inches wide.
  13. Do not overwork the dough.
  14. Spread the Butter:
  15. Spread the softened butter mixture evenly over 2/3 of the dough, leaving a 1/4 inch border unbuttered on all sides.
  16. First Fold:
  17. Fold the bottom third of the dough up to the middle.
  18. Fold the top third (with the buttered layer) down over the middle.
  19. Lightly flour the dough.
  20. Refrigerate if necessary.
  21. Roll Out and Second Fold:
  22. Roll out the dough to about 16 inches long and 3/8 inch thick.
  23. Fold the two ends of the dough towards the middle so they meet.
  24. Fold the dough over to create a single layer.
  25. Lightly flour the dough.
  26. Mark the dough with two finger marks to indicate two turns.
  27. Wrap the dough in plastic and refrigerate for at least 40 minutes.
  28. Third and Fourth Turns:
  29. After chilling, beat the dough with your hands to soften the butter.
  30. Roll out the dough to about 20 inches long and 10 inches wide.
  31. Fold the bottom third up to the middle and the top third down to cover it.
  32. Turn the dough as if opening a book.
  33. Lightly flour the dough.
  34. Roll out the dough again.
  35. Repeat the folding and rolling process for a total of four turns.
  36. Mark the dough with two finger marks to indicate four turns.
  37. Refrigerate for at least two hours.
  38. Prepare the Tart:
  39. Roll out the chilled dough to about 1/4 inch thick.
  40. Cut a strip of dough and set aside for the top of the tart.
  41. Roll out the remaining dough into a rectangle as long and wide as desired.
  42. Place the dough on a floured pastry sheet.
  43. Prick the dough with a roller pricker or forks to prevent it from puffing up too much.
  44. Assemble the Tart:
  45. Spread the ham filling over the bottom layer of dough.
  46. Trim the corners of the dough to prevent it from being too thick.
  47. Place the reserved dough strip over the filling and press the edges together.
  48. Use a fork to create decorative marks around the edges of the tart.
  49. Glaze and Bake:
  50. Brush the tart with an egg glaze made from one whole egg beaten with 1 teaspoon of water.
  51. Cut steam holes in the top of the tart.
  52. Bake in a 450-degree oven for 20-25 minutes, until puffed and golden brown.
  53. Reduce the oven temperature to 350 degrees and bake for another 20-25 minutes, until the sides are crisp.
  54. Serve:
  55. Let the tart cool slightly before serving.
  56. Enjoy with a green salad and red wine.

Notes:

  • Puff pastry is a delicate dough, so it's important to chill it thoroughly between each turn.
  • Don't be afraid to stop and refrigerate the dough if it becomes too soft or difficult to work with.
  • You can use any type of filling you like for the tart.
  • The tart can be frozen for up to a year.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-XtOpzLRnUM

puff_pastry_tart.txt - Puff Pastry Tart with Onions and Bacon

Objectives

  • Learn how to make classic French puff pastry from scratch.
  • Discover techniques for working with puff pastry scraps.
  • Master the art of making a delicious Alsatian tart.

Ingredients

Pastry Dough: - 1 pound pastry flour (farine) - 1 ½ teaspoons salt (sel) - 1 ¼ cups water (eau) - 1 pound sweet butter (beurre doux)

Tart Filling: - 1 large onion (oignon) - 1 cup chicken stock (bouillon de poulet) - Freshly ground pepper (poivre noir) - 2 tablespoons cream (crème fraiche) - ¼ pound bacon (lardons) - Fresh basil (basilic) - Goat cheese (fromage de chèvre)

Pizza: - Cherry tomatoes (tomates cerises) - Cheese (fromage) - Sweet basil (basilic) - Olive oil (huile d'olive)

Deep-fried Diamonds: - Parmesan cheese (parmesan) - Peanut oil (huile d'arachide)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Dough:
  2. Combine flour and salt in a food processor.
  3. Add water and process until a smooth ball forms.
  4. Remove dough from the processor and knead lightly.
  5. Cut the top of the dough to release tension.
  6. Cover with a wet towel and let rest for a few minutes.
  7. Pound cold butter into a square shape.
  8. Roll out the dough into a rectangle.
  9. Place the butter in the center of the dough and fold the dough over the butter.
  10. Tap the dough lightly and add flour to prevent sticking.
  11. Roll out the dough again into a rectangle.
  12. Fold the dough in thirds.
  13. Wrap and refrigerate for 30 minutes.
  14. Repeat the folding and chilling process twice more.
  15. Prepare the Tart Filling:
  16. Dice onion into very small pieces.
  17. Combine onion with chicken stock, pepper, and a pinch of salt in a saucepan.
  18. Bring to a boil and simmer for 30 minutes until translucent.
  19. Cut bacon into small pieces.
  20. Boil bacon for a few minutes to remove excess salt.
  21. Drain and sauté until crisp.
  22. Assemble the Tart:
  23. Roll out chilled puff pastry scraps into a thin rectangle.
  24. Place the pastry on a buttered tray.
  25. Spread the cooked onion mixture evenly over the pastry.
  26. Sprinkle with bacon pieces.
  27. Refrigerate while preparing the pizza and deep-fried diamonds.
  28. Prepare the Pizza:
  29. Roll out remaining puff pastry into a thin rectangle.
  30. Cut into small squares.
  31. Top each square with cherry tomatoes, cheese, and basil.
  32. Brush with olive oil.
  33. Bake at 350 degrees for 15 minutes.
  34. Prepare the Deep-fried Diamonds:
  35. Cut remaining puff pastry scraps into small diamond shapes.
  36. Heat peanut oil to 325 degrees.
  37. Fry the diamonds until golden brown.
  38. Drain on paper towels.
  39. Sprinkle with parmesan cheese while still hot.
  40. Bake the Tart:
  41. Bake the tart at 350 degrees for 30-45 minutes until golden brown.
  42. Assemble the Pizza and Deep-fried Diamonds:
  43. Bake the pizzas at 375 degrees for 20 minutes.
  44. Serve the tart, pizzas, and deep-fried diamonds with a glass of wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=12TM0b-Ubz8

puff_pastry_tourte_milanese.txt - Puff Pastry Tourte Milanaise

Objectives

  • Learn how to make puff pastry from scratch
  • Master the technique of turning and chilling puff pastry
  • Create a delicious and visually appealing tourte milanese

Ingredients

Puff Pastry: - 1 pound pastry flour - 1 1/4 cups water - 1 1/2 teaspoons salt - 1 pound sweet butter

Tourte Milanaise Filling: - 1 pound spinach, blanched, sautéed, and stems removed - 1 teaspoon olive oil - 2 cloves garlic - Fresh ground pepper - Salt - 1/2 cup heavy cream - 1 tablespoon butter - 6 eggs - 1/4 cup flat parsley - 1 tablespoon tarragon - 1 tablespoon chives - Fresh nutmeg - 1 pound ham - 1/2 pound Swiss cheese - 1 red bell pepper, roasted

Oeuf Sur le Plat: - Puff pastry dough - Granulated sugar - Pastry cream - Fresh apricots

Pastry Cream: - 2 cups milk - 1/2 cup sugar - 1 pinch of salt - 1 vanilla bean, split lengthwise - 4 egg yolks - 1/3 cup cornstarch

Apricot Glaze: - Fresh apricots - Sugar - Water

Instructions

  1. Combine pastry flour, water, and salt in a food processor. Process until a dough forms.
  2. Remove dough from processor and form into a ball.
  3. Cover dough with a wet towel and let rest for a few minutes.
  4. Pound the cold butter into a square shape.
  5. Place the butter in the center of the dough and fold the dough over the butter.
  6. Roll the dough into a rectangle and fold it in thirds.
  7. Refrigerate the dough for 30 minutes.
  8. Repeat steps 6 and 7 two more times, chilling the dough for 30 minutes after each turn.
  9. To prepare the tourte milanese filling, sauté the spinach with olive oil, garlic, pepper, and salt.
  10. Add cream and butter to the spinach and cook until the spinach is wilted.
  11. Transfer the spinach to a dish and refrigerate until cool.
  12. Scramble the eggs with parsley, tarragon, chives, pepper, salt, and nutmeg.
  13. Cook the eggs over low heat until they are just set.
  14. Transfer the eggs to a dish and refrigerate until cool.
  15. Roast the red bell pepper until the skin is charred.
  16. Remove the pepper from the oven and rub it with a wet paper towel to loosen the skin.
  17. Peel the pepper and remove the seeds.
  18. Cut the pepper in half lengthwise.
  19. To assemble the tourte milanese, roll out a portion of the puff pastry dough into a circle large enough to fit in a springform pan.
  20. Place the dough in the pan and press it down to the edges.
  21. Spread half of the scrambled eggs over the dough.
  22. Top the eggs with a layer of spinach.
  23. Add a layer of ham.
  24. Sprinkle with Swiss cheese.
  25. Arrange half of the roasted red bell pepper over the cheese.
  26. Top with another layer of Swiss cheese.
  27. Add another layer of ham.
  28. Spread the remaining scrambled eggs over the ham.
  29. Roll out another portion of the puff pastry dough into a circle the same size as the bottom layer.
  30. Place the top layer of dough over the filling.
  31. Press the edges of the dough together to seal.
  32. Cut a small hole in the center of the top layer of dough to allow steam to escape.
  33. Brush the top of the tourte milanese with egg glaze.
  34. Use a knife to create a decorative design on the top of the tourte.
  35. Bake the tourte in a preheated 350-degree oven for 1 hour and 15 minutes.
  36. Allow the tourte to cool completely before slicing.
  37. To make the oeuf sur le plat, roll out a portion of the puff pastry dough to a thickness of 1/2 inch.
  38. Use a cookie cutter to cut out 4 circles.
  39. Brush one side of each circle with flour and the other side with sugar.
  40. Roll the circles in the sugar to coat both sides.
  41. Place the circles on a baking sheet and bake in a preheated 350-degree oven for 30 minutes, or until golden brown and crispy.
  42. While the oeuf sur le plat is baking, prepare the pastry cream.
  43. Combine milk, sugar, salt, and vanilla bean in a saucepan.
  44. Bring the milk mixture to a boil over medium heat.
  45. In a separate bowl, whisk together the egg yolks and cornstarch.
  46. Slowly whisk the hot milk mixture into the egg yolk mixture.
  47. Return the mixture to the saucepan and cook over medium heat, stirring constantly, until the cream thickens.
  48. Strain the pastry cream through a fine-mesh sieve.
  49. Remove the vanilla bean from the cream.
  50. Cool the pastry cream completely.
  51. To assemble the oeuf sur le plat, fill each pastry circle with pastry cream.
  52. Top with a halved apricot.
  53. Brush the apricots with apricot glaze.
  54. Bake the oeuf sur le plat in a preheated 350-degree oven for 15 minutes, or until the glaze is golden brown.
  55. Serve the oeuf sur le plat warm.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vYECP-ravME

puff_pastry_vol_au_vent.txt - Puff Pastry Vol-au-Vent with Braised Sweetbreads and Truffle Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to make classic puff pastry from scratch
  • Master the art of forming a vol-au-vent pastry container
  • Explore the techniques of braising and seasoning sweetbreads
  • Create a rich and flavorful truffle sauce to complement the dish

Ingredients

Puff Pastry - 1 pound all-purpose flour (3 cups) - 1/2 pound (3 sticks) unsalted butter, cold and cut into 4 pieces - 1 cup water, plus more as needed - 1/2 teaspoon salt

Sweetbreads - 3 pounds sweetbreads (throat or pancreas) - 1-2 tablespoons butter - Salt and freshly ground black pepper

Truffle Sauce - Brown chicken stock, reduced to 2 cups - 1/2 cup Madeira wine - 1/2 cup brown chicken stock - 2 tablespoons butter - 1 celery stalk, finely diced - 1 leek, finely diced - 1 carrot, finely diced - Fresh thyme sprigs - 1/3 cup water - 1 black truffle, peeled and coarsely chopped - 1-2 teaspoons cognac - Optional: soy sauce to darken sauce

Instructions

Puff Pastry 1. Combine flour and salt in a bowl. 2. Gradually add water, mixing with a fork until a dough forms. Add more water if needed. 3. Turn dough onto a lightly floured surface and knead until smooth. 4. Roll dough into a 3/8-inch thick rectangle. 5. Arrange butter on 2/3 of the dough, leaving a 1/3 inch border. 6. Fold the uncovered 1/3 of the dough over the butter, then fold the other end over. 7. Roll the dough into a large rectangle, then fold it in half. 8. Refrigerate the dough for at least 1 hour. 9. Repeat the rolling and folding process 2 more times, refrigerating for 1 hour after each turn. 10. Roll the chilled dough into a thin rectangle, about 1/8-inch thick. 11. Cut the dough in half, keeping one half for the vol-au-vent base. 12. Place the base dough on a parchment-lined baking sheet. 13. Using aluminum foil, create a ball shape to place on top of the base dough. 14. Roll the remaining dough into a thin rectangle and place it on top of the foil ball. 15. Trim excess dough and use it for decoration. 16. Wet the edges of the dough with water or egg wash. 17. Gently roll the top dough over a rolling pin and place it on top of the base. 18. Use a round object (like a wok) to cut out the vol-au-vent shape. 19. Press the edges of the dough with a floured fork to seal and decorate. 20. Brush the dough with egg wash for shine. 21. Refrigerate the vol-au-vent for 30-60 minutes before baking.

Sweetbreads 1. Blanch the sweetbreads by boiling them in water for 1 minute, then immediately shock them in ice water. 2. Remove any surface sinews. 3. Place the sweetbreads between two cookie sheets lined with clean towels and weight them down with cans or cartons. 4. Refrigerate for several hours. 5. Melt butter in a pan over medium heat. 6. Season the sweetbreads with salt and pepper. 7. Cook the sweetbreads for 2-2.5 minutes on each side, until browned.

Truffle Sauce 1. While the sweetbreads are browning, reduce the brown chicken stock to 2 cups. 2. Remove 1/2 cup of the reduced stock and set aside. 3. Add the Madeira wine to the remaining stock and reduce to 2 cups. 4. In a separate pan, melt butter and sauté the celery, leek, and carrot for 1 minute. 5. Add thyme and 1/3 cup water. 6. Cover and simmer for 10 minutes until the vegetables are tender and most of the liquid has evaporated. 7. Add the sautéed vegetables to the reduced stock. 8. Add the reserved 1/2 cup of stock. 9. Season with salt or soy sauce to taste. 10. Coarsely chop the truffle and add to the sauce. 11. Stir in 1-2 teaspoons of cognac. 12. Cover and let the sauce steep.

Assembly and Serving 1. Bake the vol-au-vent in a preheated oven at 400°F (200°C) until golden brown and puffed. 2. While the vol-au-vent is baking, braise the sweetbreads in the reserved 1/2 cup of stock and 1/2 cup of white wine. 3. Braise gently for 30 minutes. 4. Slice the remaining truffle thinly for decoration. 5. Remove the vol-au-vent from the oven and carefully remove the foil ball. 6. Arrange the braised sweetbreads around the vol-au-vent. 7. Place a piece of sweetbread inside the vol-au-vent. 8. Pour the truffle sauce over the sweetbreads. 9. Garnish with sliced truffle. 10. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_kwaqwPBYoU

pumpernickel_matzo.txt - Pumpernickel Bread and Matzo

Objectives

  • Learn to make a flavorful and tender pumpernickel bread.
  • Master the art of kneading dough by hand.
  • Create delicious, homemade matzo from scratch.

Ingredients

Pumpernickel Bread - 1 tablespoon instant espresso - 2 1/2 ounces unsweetened chocolate, chopped - 1 stick unsalted butter - 1/4 cup molasses - 1/2 cup warm water - 2 1/2 packages active dry yeast (about 2 tablespoons) - Pinch of sugar - 1/4 cup solid vegetable shortening - 2 tablespoons ground caraway seeds - 1 1/2 tablespoons whole caraway seeds - 1/2 cup prune lekvar - 2 cups plain yogurt (room temperature) - 1 tablespoon salt - 3 1/2 cups coarse rye flour (rye meal) - Bread flour (as needed) - Butter (for greasing bowl) - Plastic wrap - Sesame seeds (optional) - Caraway seeds (optional) - 1 egg white - 1 1/2 teaspoons water - Ice water (for steam injection)

Matzo - 4 cups all-purpose flour - 1/4 cup sesame seeds (optional) - 1/4 teaspoon black pepper (optional) - 2 teaspoons coarse salt - 1 1/2 cups warm water - Flour (for dusting) - Coarse salt (for sprinkling) - Baking sheet

Instructions

Pumpernickel Bread

  1. Dissolve 1 tablespoon of instant espresso in 1 cup of boiling water.
  2. In a saucepan, melt 2 1/2 ounces of chopped unsweetened chocolate and 1 stick of unsalted butter over low heat.
  3. Add 1/4 cup of molasses to the melted chocolate and butter mixture.
  4. In a separate bowl, proof 2 1/2 packages of active dry yeast in 1/2 cup of warm water with a pinch of sugar.
  5. In a large bowl, combine 1/4 cup of solid vegetable shortening, 2 tablespoons of ground caraway seeds, and 1 1/2 tablespoons of whole caraway seeds.
  6. Add 1/2 cup of prune lekvar to the shortening and caraway seed mixture.
  7. Stir in 2 cups of room temperature plain yogurt and 1 tablespoon of salt.
  8. Once the yeast mixture is foamy, add it to the yogurt mixture.
  9. Gradually add 3 1/2 cups of coarse rye flour, mixing until a dough forms.
  10. Add bread flour, 1 cup at a time, until the dough becomes less sticky and pulls away from the sides of the bowl.
  11. Turn the dough out onto a floured surface and knead for several minutes, until it becomes smooth and elastic.
  12. Grease a large bowl with butter. Place the dough in the bowl, cover with plastic wrap and a towel, and let rise in a warm, draft-free spot for 2 1/2 hours, or until doubled in size.
  13. Punch down the dough and let rise again for 1 hour and 15 minutes.
  14. Turn the dough out onto a lightly floured surface and divide it in half.
  15. Shape each half into a loaf, gently pressing the dough to prevent tunnels.
  16. Brush the loaves with a mixture of 1 egg white and 1 1/2 teaspoons of water.
  17. Sprinkle the loaves with sesame seeds or caraway seeds, as desired.
  18. Preheat oven to 450 degrees F (232 degrees C). Place tiles in the oven to preheat.
  19. Place the loaves on a baking sheet lined with parchment paper.
  20. Bake for 10 minutes at 450 degrees F (232 degrees C), then reduce heat to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C) and bake for an additional 30 minutes.
  21. Let the loaves cool completely on a wire rack before slicing and serving.

Matzo

  1. In a large bowl, combine 4 cups of all-purpose flour, 1/4 cup of sesame seeds (optional), and 1/4 teaspoon of black pepper (optional).
  2. In a separate bowl, dissolve 2 teaspoons of coarse salt in 1 1/2 cups of warm water.
  3. Make a well in the center of the flour mixture and pour in the salt water.
  4. Using your hands, mix the ingredients until a dough forms.
  5. Turn the dough out onto a lightly floured surface and knead for a few minutes, until smooth and elastic.
  6. Divide the dough into 12 equal pieces.
  7. On a lightly floured surface, roll out each piece of dough into a thin sheet, using a rolling pin.
  8. Use a docker or fork to prick holes in the dough to prevent bubbling during baking.
  9. Sprinkle the dough with coarse salt.
  10. Preheat oven to the highest setting. Place a baking sheet upside down on the lowest rack and preheat.
  11. Carefully transfer the dough sheet to the preheated baking sheet.
  12. Bake for 1 minute, then check for tiny blisters and a golden color.
  13. Continue baking for another minute, or until the matzo is golden brown and crisp.
  14. Repeat steps 7-13 for the remaining dough pieces.
  15. Let the matzo cool completely on a wire rack before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jXv0_HNLb40

wok_seared_ono.txt - Wok-Seared Ono with Banana Curry and Ti Leaf Steamed Banana

Objectives

  • Learn how to prepare a refreshing Puna Green Papaya Salad with a Thai Vinaigrette
  • Discover the unique qualities of green papaya and its versatility in Hawaiian cuisine
  • Understand the importance of fresh, local ingredients in creating flavorful dishes

Ingredients

  • Green papaya
  • Tomatoes
  • Red Serrano chili peppers
  • Cilantro
  • Thai Vinaigrette (recipe below)

Thai Vinaigrette Ingredients

  • Vegetable oil
  • Fresh lime juice
  • Fresh ginger
  • Oriental fish sauce
  • Sambal chili
  • Chili pepper

Instructions

  1. Cut off the ends of the green papaya and cut it in half.
  2. Remove the seeds from the papaya.
  3. Peel the papaya and grate it.
  4. Blanch and peel a tomato.
  5. Julienne the tomato and add it to other julienned tomatoes.
  6. Clean the red Serrano chili peppers by removing the seeds.
  7. Combine the grated papaya, julienned tomatoes, chili peppers, and whole cilantro leaves in a bowl.
  8. Make the Thai Vinaigrette by combining all ingredients in a jar and shaking well.
  9. Add the Thai Vinaigrette to the salad and toss to combine.
  10. Serve the salad with seared "ahi" or grilled beef.

queen_of_sheba_chocolate_almond_cake.txt - Queen of Sheba Chocolate Almond Cake

Objectives

  • Learn to make a delicious and moist chocolate almond cake
  • Understand the importance of proper chocolate melting and egg white beating techniques
  • Learn to make a simple chocolate and butter glaze

Ingredients

  • 4 ounces semisweet baking chocolate (4 squares)
  • 2 tablespoons dark Jamaican rum
  • 2/3 cup semisweet chocolate bits (4 ounces)
  • 1 stick (4 ounces) unsalted butter, softened
  • 2/3 cup granulated sugar
  • 3 large egg yolks
  • 3 large egg whites
  • 1/3 cup pulverized almonds
  • 1/4 teaspoon almond extract
  • 3/4 cup sifted cake flour
  • 6 tablespoons unsalted butter, un-softened

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C).
  2. Grease and flour an 8-inch by 1 1/2-inch cake pan.
  3. Melt the chocolate:
    • Place the chocolate bits in a heatproof bowl.
    • Fill a larger pan with water and bring to a boil.
    • Remove the pan from heat and place the bowl of chocolate in the hot water.
    • Stir occasionally until the chocolate is melted and smooth.
  4. Cream the butter and sugar:
    • In a mixing bowl, cream together the softened butter and sugar until light and fluffy.
  5. Add the egg yolks:
    • Beat in the egg yolks one at a time, mixing well after each addition.
  6. Beat the egg whites:
    • In a clean, dry bowl, beat the egg whites until they form soft peaks.
    • Add a scant 1/4 teaspoon cream of tartar and a pinch of salt.
    • Continue beating until the egg whites are stiff but not dry.
    • Gradually add 2 tablespoons of sugar while beating.
  7. Fold in the egg whites:
    • Add 1/4 of the beaten egg whites to the chocolate mixture and stir gently.
    • Gently fold in the remaining egg whites, being careful not to deflate them.
  8. Add the remaining ingredients:
    • Stir in the pulverized almonds and almond extract.
    • Gradually fold in the sifted cake flour.
  9. Pour the batter into the prepared pan:
    • Spread the batter evenly in the pan.
  10. Bake the cake:
    • Bake for 25 minutes, or until a toothpick inserted into the center comes out with a few moist crumbs attached.
  11. Cool the cake:
    • Let the cake cool in the pan for 10 minutes.
    • Invert the cake onto a wire rack to cool completely.
  12. Make the icing:
    • In a mixing bowl, combine the melted chocolate and rum.
    • Beat in the un-softened butter, one tablespoon at a time, until the icing is smooth and creamy.
    • If the icing is too soft, chill it over ice water until it thickens.
  13. Ice the cake:
    • Pour the icing over the cooled cake, spreading it evenly over the top and sides.
  14. Decorate the cake:
    • Arrange whole blanched almonds on top of the icing.
  15. Serve and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IuzBruGLqcQ

quenelle_a_la_francais.txt - Quenelle à la Française

Objectives

  • Learn how to make quenelles, a light and delicate fish dish.
  • Understand the importance of using cold ingredients and a stiff Pernod mixture.
  • Discover different ways to serve quenelles, from simple to elaborate.

Ingredients

  • 1 cup water
  • 2 teaspoons salt
  • 4 tablespoons butter
  • 1 cup all-purpose flour
  • 2 eggs
  • 1/4 cup egg whites
  • 2 cups (about 1 pound) lean skinless fish (e.g., halibut, cusk, grey sole)
  • White pepper (to taste)
  • Chopped truffle or nutmeg (optional)
  • Chilled heavy cream (2-8 tablespoons)
  • Salt (to taste)
  • Poached oysters (optional)
  • Shrimp (optional)
  • Cheese sauce (optional)
  • Spinach (optional)
  • Hollandaise sauce (optional)
  • Velouté sauce (optional)
  • Mushrooms (optional)
  • Madeira or Port wine (optional)
  • Truffles (optional)
  • French bread (optional)
  • White Burgundy or other full white wine (optional)

Instructions

  1. Make the Pernod sauce:
    • Combine 1 cup of water and 2 teaspoons of salt in a saucepan.
    • Bring to a boil.
    • Add 4 tablespoons of butter and stir until melted.
    • Remove from heat and immediately add 1 cup of flour.
    • Stir until thoroughly mixed.
    • Return to medium-high heat and cook, stirring constantly, until the sauce cleans the sides of the pan and begins to film on the bottom.
    • Remove from heat and let cool slightly

quiche_lorraine.txt - Quiche Lorraine

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French quiche lorraine
  • Master the art of making a flaky pastry crust
  • Discover different variations and fillings for quiche

Ingredients

  • 2 cups all-purpose flour
  • 1 stick (1/4 pound) butter, chilled
  • 3 tablespoons white vegetable shortening
  • 5-6 tablespoons cold water
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/8 teaspoon sugar
  • 5 eggs
  • 2 cups heavy cream or light cream (or milk)
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • Freshly ground pepper
  • Nutmeg
  • Bacon, cooked and crumbled
  • Cooked onions (for onion quiche)
  • Cheese (optional)
  • Spinach (optional)
  • Lobster, warmed with butter, cognac, salt, and pepper (optional)

Instructions

  1. Make the pastry crust:
  2. Sift 2 cups of flour onto a piece of wax paper.
  3. Cut 1 stick of chilled butter into small pieces.
  4. Add 3 tablespoons of white vegetable shortening.
  5. Using your fingertips, rub the fat into the flour until it resembles small oatmeal flakes.
  6. Add 1/2 teaspoon salt and 1/8 teaspoon sugar.
  7. Add 5-6 tablespoons of cold water, working the dough together with your hand.
  8. Use your heel to push the dough down and create a smooth ball.
  9. Wrap the dough in wax paper and chill in the refrigerator for at least 2 hours.
  10. Roll out the dough:
  11. Roll out the chilled dough on a floured surface to about 1/8 inch thickness.
  12. Line a buttered French tart ring or a false-bottom pie tin with the dough.
  13. Press the dough against the edges of the mold, making them thicker than the sides.
  14. Use a knife to create a decorative edge.
  15. Prick the bottom of the dough with a fork to prevent it from rising.
  16. Pre-bake the crust:
  17. Place the dough in a 425-degree oven for 5 minutes.
  18. Remove the dough from the oven, remove the foil and beans (or weight), and bake for another 2-3 minutes.
  19. Make the quiche mixture:
  20. Beat 5 eggs in a bowl.
  21. Add 2 cups of heavy cream, light cream, or milk.
  22. Season with 1/2 teaspoon salt, freshly ground pepper, and a pinch of nutmeg.
  23. Whisk until the eggs and cream are well combined.
  24. Assemble the quiche:
  25. Place the cooked and crumbled bacon in the pre-baked crust.
  26. Pour the quiche mixture over the bacon, filling the crust about two-thirds full.
  27. Bake at 375 degrees until the quiche is set and the top is golden brown.
  28. Variations:
  29. For onion quiche: Add cooked onions to the pre-baked crust before pouring in the quiche mixture.
  30. For cheese quiche: Sprinkle cheese on top of the quiche mixture before baking.
  31. For spinach quiche: Add cooked spinach to the quiche mixture before baking.
  32. For lobster quiche: Warm a little butter in a pan, add cognac, salt, and pepper. Add the lobster to the pre-baked crust, then pour on the quiche mixture.
  33. Serve:
  34. Once the quiche is baked, let it cool slightly before serving.
  35. Cut the quiche into wedges and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zTkf9qzL_xU

ramequin_forestiere.txt - Ramequin Forestière

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French dish called Ramequin Forestière
  • Understand the difference between a bouilli sauce and a velouté sauce
  • Explore various filling options for a Ramequin Forestière

Ingredients

  • 1/2 cup granular flour
  • 2 cups milk
  • 3.5 tablespoons butter
  • 4 whole eggs
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 2-3 grinds of pepper
  • 1 point of nutmeg
  • 1 cup grated Swiss cheese
  • 1 cup chopped mushrooms
  • 1 tablespoon chopped shallots or scallions
  • 1 tablespoon flour (optional, for creamed mushrooms)
  • Heavy cream (optional, for creamed mushrooms)
  • 1 cup sugar
  • 1/3 cup water
  • Oranges (for segments and peel)
  • Pineapple ice (optional)

Instructions

  1. Chop mushrooms into approximately 1/8-inch pieces.
  2. Sauté mushrooms in a non-stick pan with butter and oil until they separate from each other.
  3. Add shallots or scallions to the mushrooms and stir.
  4. In a separate pan, whisk together flour and 2 cups of milk.
  5. Bring the mixture to a boil, stirring constantly.
  6. Remove from heat and stir in butter.
  7. Add eggs one at a time, beating well after each addition.
  8. Season with salt, pepper, and nutmeg.
  9. Stir in grated Swiss cheese.
  10. Butter an ovenproof baking dish.
  11. Pour half of the ramequin mixture into the dish.
  12. Top with the sautéed mushrooms.
  13. Pour the remaining ramequin mixture over the mushrooms.
  14. Sprinkle with additional cheese.
  15. Dot with softened butter.
  16. Bake in a 400-degree oven for 25-30 minutes, or until golden brown and puffed.
  17. Serve immediately.

Orange à Glacé

  1. Using a vegetable peeler, remove the orange peel from oranges, avoiding the white pith.
  2. Cut the peel into matchstick-sized julienne strips.
  3. Blanch the peel in boiling water for 10 minutes, or until softened.
  4. In a saucepan, combine sugar and water.
  5. Swirl the pan over high heat, avoiding stirring, until the sugar dissolves and the liquid clears.
  6. Cover the pan and cook for 1-2 minutes to prevent crystallization.
  7. Test the syrup for the hard-ball stage by dropping a small amount into cold water. If it forms a hard ball, the syrup is ready.
  8. Add the blanched orange peel to the syrup and simmer until the syrup thickens slightly.
  9. Pour the hot syrup over orange segments.
  10. Chill in the refrigerator for 2-3 hours.

Serving Suggestions

  • Serve Ramequin Forestière as a main course with a watercress and tomato salad, French bread, and an Alsatian wine.
  • Serve Orange à Glacé with pineapple ice for a refreshing dessert.
  • Use the candied orange peel as a garnish for cakes, puddings, or fruit.

risotto_with_wild_mushrooms.txt - Risotto with Wild Mushrooms

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a classic Italian risotto with wild mushrooms.
  • Understand the importance of using Arborio rice for risotto.
  • Master the techniques for properly cooking risotto, including toasting the rice, adding stock gradually, and creating a creamy texture.

Ingredients

  • 1 cup Arborio rice
  • 1/2 cup dry white wine
  • 6 cups hot mushroom stock
  • 1/4 cup olive oil
  • 1 medium onion, chopped
  • 2 shallots, chopped
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • 1/4 teaspoon black pepper
  • 1/2 cup dry porcini mushrooms, reconstituted in hot stock
  • 1/2 cup oyster mushrooms, cleaned and sliced
  • 1/2 cup shiitake mushrooms, cleaned and sliced
  • 1/2 cup chanterelle mushrooms, cleaned and sliced
  • 1/4 cup grated Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese
  • 2 tablespoons butter

Instructions

  1. Prepare the mushrooms:
  2. Reconstitute dry porcini mushrooms in hot stock for 30 minutes.
  3. Clean and slice oyster, shiitake, and chanterelle mushrooms.
  4. Cut off the tough stems of the shiitake mushrooms and save them for stock.
  5. Sauté the mushrooms:
  6. Heat olive oil in a sauté pan over medium heat.
  7. Add the mushrooms and salt lightly.
  8. Simmer slowly until the water evaporates and the mushrooms concentrate in flavor.
  9. Begin the risotto:
  10. Heat olive oil in a saucepan over medium heat.
  11. Add the onion and salt. Sauté until softened.
  12. Add the shallots and continue sautéing until they soften.
  13. Toast the rice:
  14. Add the Arborio rice to the pan and stir continuously for 2-3 minutes until the rice is slightly golden and dry.
  15. Add the wine:
  16. Pour in the white wine and let it be completely absorbed by the rice.
  17. Add the stock:
  18. Gradually add the hot mushroom stock, a little bit at a time, stirring continuously.
  19. Ensure the stock is always at a boiling temperature.
  20. Cook the risotto:
  21. Continue adding the stock, a little at a time, as the rice absorbs the previous addition.
  22. Stir frequently to prevent the rice from sticking to the bottom of the pan.
  23. Cook until the rice is al dente and the risotto is creamy.
  24. Add the porcini mushrooms:
  25. Chop the reconstituted porcini mushrooms finely.
  26. Strain the porcini stock through cheesecloth or a coffee filter to remove any grit.
  27. Add the chopped porcini mushrooms and the strained porcini stock to the risotto.
  28. Add the remaining mushrooms:
  29. Add the remaining mushrooms to the risotto.
  30. Finish the risotto:
  31. Remove the risotto from the heat.
  32. Stir in the butter and Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese.
  33. Season with salt and pepper to taste.
  34. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wA2xB2Crn4A

riz_a_l_imperatrice.txt - Riz à l'Impératrice (Empress's Rice)

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French dessert, Riz à l'Impératrice
  • Master the techniques of blanching rice, making crème anglaise, and assembling a Bavarian cream
  • Understand the importance of using high-quality ingredients for a delicate dessert

Ingredients

  • 1/2 cup raw rice
  • 4 quarts rapidly boiling water
  • 1 2/3 cups milk
  • 1/3 cup sugar
  • 2 tablespoons butter
  • 1 vanilla bean
  • 5 egg yolks
  • 1 teaspoon cornstarch
  • 1 1/2 cups hot milk
  • 3/4 cup diced glacéed fruits
  • 1/4 cup kirsch
  • 2 envelopes plain unflavored gelatin
  • 3 tablespoons apricot jam
  • 1 cup heavy cream

Instructions

  1. Blanch the rice: Bring 4 quarts of water to a rapid boil. Add 1/2 cup of raw rice and stir. Boil for exactly 5 minutes, then drain thoroughly.
  2. Prepare the rice: In a fireproof casserole, combine 1 2/3 cups of milk, 1/3 cup of sugar, 2 tablespoons of butter, and the blanched rice. Add a vanilla bean and cover the casserole with a piece of wax paper. Bake in a 300-degree oven for 30-40 minutes, or until the rice is tender.
  3. Make the crème anglaise: In a bowl, whisk together 5 egg yolks and 3/4 cup of sugar until thick and sticky. Gradually whisk in 1 1/2 cups of hot milk. Add 1 teaspoon of cornstarch.
  4. Cook the crème anglaise: Place the mixture over moderately high heat in a non-staining pan. Stir constantly with a wooden spoon, ensuring the bottom and sides of the pan are heated evenly. Continue stirring until the custard thickens enough to coat the spoon and steam begins to rise.
  5. Combine the crème anglaise and fruit mixture: In a separate bowl, combine 3/4 cup of diced glacéed fruits, 1/4 cup of kirsch, and 2 envelopes of plain unflavored gelatin. Stir until the gelatin is dissolved. Add this mixture to the hot crème anglaise and stir until the gelatin is fully incorporated.
  6. Cool the custard mixture: Place the custard mixture in a bowl of ice water to cool quickly. Stir occasionally to prevent the rice from floating to the top.
  7. Add apricot flavoring: Once the custard mixture has cooled slightly, stir in 3 tablespoons of apricot jam, sieved to remove any pieces of peel. Taste and add more vanilla extract if desired.
  8. Whip the cream: In a chilled bowl, whip 1 cup of heavy cream with a chilled whisk until it forms soft peaks and leaves light traces on the surface.
  9. Fold in the whipped cream: Once the custard mixture is almost set, gently fold in the whipped cream using a rubber spatula.
  10. Mold the dessert: Pour the mixture into a chilled ring mold or individual dessert cups. Cover with plastic wrap or wax paper and refrigerate for at least 4 hours, preferably 6.
  11. Unmold the dessert: To unmold, run a hot knife around the edge of the mold. Dip the mold in hot water for 5 seconds, then invert onto a chilled platter. Serve with a fresh strawberry sauce.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uEY2JCfzqkw

roast_chicken_lemon_garlic.txt - Roast Chicken with Lemon and Garlic

Objectives

  • Learn to make a flavorful roast chicken with lemon and garlic.
  • Understand the importance of marinating the chicken for maximum flavor.
  • Master the technique of roasting vegetables alongside the chicken.

Ingredients

  • Flat-leaf parsley
  • 2-3 garlic cloves, peeled
  • 2 shallots, peeled
  • Herbes de Provence
  • Rosemary
  • Dijon mustard
  • Olive oil
  • Salt
  • Coarsely ground pepper
  • Lemon zest
  • 3-pound chicken, organic
  • 1 Spanish onion
  • Baking potatoes
  • Oil
  • Kosher salt
  • Cracked pepper
  • Chicken stock
  • Lemon slices
  • Roasted garlic cloves
  • Butter
  • Lemon juice
  • Whipped cream
  • Sprig of mint

Instructions

  1. Chop flat-leaf parsley.
  2. Peel and roughly chop garlic cloves and shallots.
  3. Combine chopped parsley, garlic, shallots, Herbes de Provence, rosemary, Dijon mustard, and olive oil in a food processor.
  4. Pulse until ingredients are roughly chopped and combined.
  5. Scrape mixture into a glass bowl.
  6. Season with salt, pepper, and lemon zest.
  7. Stir to combine.
  8. Marinate the chicken in the marinade for at least one hour outside the refrigerator or four to six hours in the refrigerator.
  9. Trim the ends of a Spanish onion, leaving the core intact.
  10. Cut the onion in half through the core and then lengthwise through the root.
  11. Cut baking potatoes lengthwise in half and then into quarters.
  12. Preheat oven to 350 degrees Fahrenheit.
  13. Heat a sheet pan in the oven.
  14. Drizzle a small amount of oil on the hot sheet pan.
  15. Place the potato quarters cut side down onto the sheet pan.
  16. Add the onions to the sheet pan.
  17. Season the potatoes and onions with kosher salt and cracked pepper.
  18. Place the chicken into the roasting pan.
  19. Season the chicken with salt and pepper.
  20. Roast the chicken, potatoes, and onions at 350 degrees Fahrenheit for 1 hour and 20 minutes.
  21. Remove the potatoes and onions from the oven.
  22. Allow the chicken to cool slightly and rest for the juices to return to the bird.
  23. Peel the skin off the chicken.
  24. Carve the chicken into pieces, keeping as much skin as possible.
  25. Remove the chicken juices from the roasting pan and add them to the chicken stock.
  26. Ladle some of the fat from the roasting pan into the chicken stock.
  27. Arrange the carved chicken pieces, lemon slices, and roasted garlic cloves in the roasting pan.
  28. Pour the chicken stock around the chicken pieces.
  29. Broil the chicken until the skin is crispy.
  30. Pour the chicken juices into a saucepan.
  31. Bring the chicken juices to a simmer.
  32. Add lemon juice to the chicken juices.
  33. Arrange the potatoes and onions on a platter.
  34. Serve each person a half chicken, potatoes, and onions.
  35. Add a knob of butter to the chicken juices.
  36. Pour the chicken juices around the chicken pieces, avoiding the crispy skin.
  37. Garnish with a sprig of parsley.
  38. Serve with whipped cream and a sprig of mint.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=biqe5A9nm-M

roast_chicken_on_spit.txt - Roast Chicken on a Spit

Objectives

  • Learn how to identify different types of chickens for roasting
  • Understand the importance of preparing a chicken for roasting
  • Learn how to roast a chicken on a spit

Ingredients

  • 1 6-7 pound chicken
  • 1/4 teaspoon salt
  • 1/2 teaspoon dried tarragon
  • 1 shallot, minced
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 2 lengths of blanched bacon (thick-sliced bacon simmered in 2 quarts of water for 10 minutes)

Instructions

  1. Remove the giblets from the chicken and save them for soup.
  2. Wash the chicken inside and out with water.
  3. Inspect the chicken for extra neck, elbow knobs, pin feathers, and fat glands. Remove any extra neck and elbow knobs.
  4. Optionally, remove the wishbone by cutting around it on both sides and pulling it out.
  5. Truss the chicken by pushing the knees under the armpits and using a trussing needle to secure them.
  6. Turn the chicken over and truss the wings close to the sides.
  7. Pull the neck skin over the opening in the neck.
  8. Truss the legs by going through the lower part of the tail flap, then through the top part of the drumstick, and finally catching the tip of the breast. Pull this through and tie it tight.
  9. Place a small amount of butter, salt, dried tarragon, and minced shallot inside the chicken.
  10. Massage the chicken with butter.
  11. Place the chicken on the spit, starting from the neck end. Secure the chicken with the prongs on the spit and tighten them.
  12. Tie the chicken onto the spit with string for added security.
  13. Wrap the chicken with blanched bacon, tying it securely to prevent dripping.
  14. Place the chicken on the rotisserie and roast for 2 1/2 hours.
  15. Remove the bacon in the last half hour of roasting and baste the chicken.
  16. To check if the chicken is done, press the legs to see if they feel tender and move in their sockets. Also, check the juices dripping from the vent; they should be clear yellow with no rosy color.
  17. Carve the chicken by nudging the leg off, cutting the leg and second joint in half, and cutting the wing off with a little breast meat.
  18. Serve and enjoy!

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0C0Xofjh74s

roast_lamb_with_mustard_sauce.txt - Roast Leg of Lamb with Mustard Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn how to trim and prepare a leg of lamb for roasting.
  • Master the art of creating a flavorful mustard sauce for the lamb.
  • Discover a simple yet elegant way to prepare grits with cheese and eggs.
  • Explore the steps involved in poaching pears in caramel for a delightful dessert.
  • Learn how to carve a roast leg of lamb using the French technique.
  • Gain insights into wine pairings for a lamb-centric meal.

Ingredients

Lamb: - 9-pound leg of lamb - 2 cloves garlic, pureed - 2 tablespoons Dijon mustard - Dried rosemary - Soy sauce - Olive oil - Skewers - White string - Chicken stock - Vermouth - Cold water

Grits: - 2 1/2 cups grits - 10 cups boiling water - 1 teaspoon salt - 1 tablespoon butter - 1 cup sour cream - 3 eggs - 1 cup grated cheddar cheese - 10 grinds of black pepper - Tiny speck of nutmeg - 1/2 cup grated Swiss cheese

Pear Dessert: - Pear halves - Lemon juice - 1 stick (4 ounces) butter - 3/4 cup sugar - Puff pastry - Pastry cream flavored with dark rum - Caramel sauce - Whipped cream flavored with rum

Lobster Dish: - Buttercup squash - Chicken broth - 2 tablespoons shallots - 1 branch fresh tarragon - Cracked peppercorns - 2 cups Chardonnay - 2 tablespoons heavy cream - 2 sticks sweet butter - 1/3 cup heavy cream - 1 whole egg - 2 egg yolks - Salt - White peppercorns - Fresh nutmeg - Lemon juice - Live lobsters - Red wine vinegar - Chanterelles - Peas - Lobster roe - Fresh chives

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 350 degrees Fahrenheit.
  2. Trim excess fat from the leg of lamb using a sharp knife.
  3. Remove the hip bone from the lamb leg to make carving easier.
  4. Secure the flap of skin back onto the leg using skewers and white string.
  5. Make the mustard sauce by combining pureed garlic, Dijon mustard, dried rosemary, soy sauce, and olive oil.
  6. Coat the lamb with the mustard sauce.
  7. Place a rack underneath the lamb for air circulation and cover the shank with foil to prevent it from touching the oven.
  8. Prepare the lamb sauce by browning chopped lamb bones, onion, garlic, and carrot in a 450-degree oven for 30 minutes.
  9. Stir in four tablespoons of flour and continue browning in the oven for five minutes.
  10. Transfer the browned ingredients to a saucepan.
  11. Deglaze the baking pan with chicken stock and add to the saucepan.
  12. Add additional chicken stock, vermouth, and cold water to the saucepan.
  13. Simmer the lamb sauce for three hours, then strain and degrease.
  14. Roast the lamb in the 350-degree oven for 90 minutes.
  15. Let the lamb cool and then place it in a 120-degree warming oven until ready to serve.
  16. Cook the grits by combining 2 1/2 cups of grits with 10 cups of boiling water.
  17. Stir in salt, butter, sour cream, eggs, grated cheddar cheese, pepper, and nutmeg.
  18. Transfer the grits to a buttered baking dish.
  19. Sprinkle with grated Swiss cheese and bake in a 375-degree oven for 40 minutes.
  20. Prepare the pear dessert by poaching pear halves in caramel.
  21. To make the caramel, melt butter and add sugar.
  22. Cook the caramel until it browns and becomes smooth.
  23. Add the pears to the caramel and cook covered for a few minutes.
  24. Transfer the pears to a baking sheet to cool.
  25. Assemble the pear dessert by placing a pool of caramel on a plate, followed by a layer of puff pastry, pastry cream, a poached pear half, more caramel, whipped cream, and the top of the puff pastry case.
  26. Carve the roast lamb using a sharp knife and the French technique.
  27. Serve the roast lamb with the mustard sauce, grits, and pear dessert.
  28. Enjoy the meal with a selection of wines, including a Chardonnay, Pinot Noir vin gris, and Pinot Noir.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=od0wWxA440g

roast_saddle_of_lamb_persillade.txt - Selle d'agneau rotie persillade

Objectives

  • Learn how to trim and prepare a saddle of lamb.
  • Understand the proper roasting technique for a saddle of lamb.
  • Create a delicious persillade sauce to accompany the lamb.

Ingredients

  • 1 saddle of lamb (about 6.5 pounds)
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Rosemary to taste (about 1/4 teaspoon)
  • White kitchen string
  • Melted butter
  • 1 onion, roughly chopped
  • 1 carrot, roughly chopped
  • 1 large piece of garlic
  • Dry white vermouth
  • Canned beef bouillon (optional)
  • Tomato paste (about 1 teaspoon)
  • 1/4 cup chopped parsley
  • 2 tablespoons chopped shallot or scallion
  • 1 cup fresh white breadcrumbs

Instructions

  1. Trim the saddle of lamb by removing the kidneys, kidney fat, spleen, and excess inside fat.
  2. Score the top fat layer of the saddle to about 1/4 inch thickness.
  3. Season the inside of the saddle with salt, pepper, and rosemary.
  4. Tie the flank over the tenderloin to protect it during roasting.
  5. Preheat oven to 475 degrees F.
  6. Place the saddle in a roasting pan that fits snugly.
  7. Insert a meat thermometer into the center of the saddle.
  8. Brush the ends of the saddle with melted butter.
  9. Roast for 15 minutes at 475 degrees F.
  10. Reduce oven temperature to 400 degrees F.
  11. Add the chopped onion, carrot, and garlic to the roasting pan.
  12. Baste the saddle and continue roasting for another 15 minutes.
  13. Reduce oven temperature to 375 degrees F if the vegetables are browning too quickly.
  14. Roast for an additional 45 minutes, basting and stirring the vegetables every 10 minutes.
  15. Check the meat thermometer after 45 minutes. Ideal internal temperature is 140 degrees F for a pink, juicy lamb.
  16. Let the saddle rest in the oven with the door slightly ajar for 20 minutes before carving.
  17. To make the persillade, sauté the chopped shallot or scallion and breadcrumbs in melted butter until the breadcrumbs are golden brown.
  18. Season the persillade with salt and pepper.
  19. Stir in the chopped parsley.
  20. Carve the saddle by slicing down the backbone on either side.
  21. Remove the tenderloin and slice the loin strip into 1-inch or 3/4-inch pieces.
  22. Reassemble the carved lamb on a warm platter, placing the bone back on top to steady the meat.
  23. To make the sauce, skim any excess fat from the roasting pan.
  24. Add dry white vermouth, beef bouillon (optional), and tomato paste to the pan.
  25. Simmer the sauce for 10-15 minutes.
  26. Strain the sauce and spoon some over the carved lamb. Serve the remaining sauce in a warm bowl.
  27. Sprinkle the persillade over the lamb.
  28. Serve the saddle of lamb with pommes Anna, braised endive, and baked tomatoes.
  29. Pair with a good chateau bottled red Bordeaux Médoc.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z1q3AG9Nwag

roast_squab.txt - Roast Squab

Objectives

  • Learn to roast small game birds in the classic French style.
  • Understand the importance of basting and trussing for proper cooking.
  • Create a delicious sauce using the bird's giblets and stock.

Ingredients

  • 2 squabs (baby pigeons)
  • 1/2 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 teaspoon of chopped scallion or shallot
  • 1/8 teaspoon of salt
  • 1 pinch of tarragon (or other herbs)
  • 1/2 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 tablespoon of oil
  • Carrots and onions (for sauce)
  • Beef or chicken stock
  • Clarified butter
  • White bread
  • Fresh pork fat or bacon
  • Cognac (optional)
  • Madeira or port (optional)
  • Pepper
  • White bread crumbs
  • Watercress (for garnish)

Instructions

  1. Defrost frozen squabs in the refrigerator for a day or in cold water.
  2. Remove the giblets from the squabs. Save the livers for canapés.
  3. Trim the wing tips from the squabs and save for sauce.
  4. Truss the squabs using a needle and white thread, or tie with string.
  5. Season the squabs with scallion or shallot, salt, tarragon, and butter.
  6. Cover the breasts of the squabs with pork fat, bacon, or suet.
  7. Roast the squabs in a 400-degree oven for about 30 minutes.
  8. Brown the breasts of the squabs by removing the fat for the last 5 minutes of cooking.
  9. Sauté the wing tips and necks in oil, then add carrots and onions.
  10. Add beef or chicken stock to the pan and simmer for a delicious sauce base.
  11. Prepare canapés by sautéing white bread in clarified butter.
  12. Chop the livers with pork fat or bacon into a puree.
  13. Season the liver puree with cognac, Madeira or port, pepper, salt, and herbs.
  14. Add white bread crumbs to the liver puree to thicken.
  15. Broil the canapés topped with the liver puree for 1 minute.
  16. Remove the roasted squabs from the oven and let rest.
  17. Pour off excess fat from the roasting pan.
  18. Add the sauce base, roasting juices, and brown vegetables to a pan.
  19. Simmer the sauce.
  20. Cut the squabs in half.
  21. Arrange the canapés on a hot serving platter.
  22. Arrange the squabs on the platter.
  23. Add the sauce to the squabs.
  24. Garnish with sautéed mushrooms, watercress, and parsley.
  25. Serve with home-fried potato chips or shoestring potatoes and French bread.
  26. Pair with a red Bordeaux wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BkWEz0geS5c

rognon_saute_et_flambe.txt - Rognons Sauté et Flambé

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare and cook veal and lamb kidneys
  • Master the art of sautéing kidneys for a delicious dish
  • Explore two variations: mustard sauce and flambéed with brandy

Ingredients

  • 4 veal kidneys
  • 4 lamb kidneys
  • 1/4 cup butter
  • 1/2 cup dry white French vermouth
  • 1 tablespoon shallots, diced
  • 2 tablespoons Dijon mustard
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • 1/2 cup chopped parsley
  • 1/2 cup sautéed mushrooms
  • 1/2 cup thickened meat stock
  • 1/2 teaspoon Worcestershire sauce
  • 1/4 cup cream
  • 1/2 cup brandy
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • 1/2 lemon, juiced

Instructions

  1. Peel the fat off the kidneys, removing any filaments or nubs.
  2. Heat butter in a non-stick pan over medium-high heat.
  3. Add the kidneys and cook for 7-8 minutes for veal kidneys and 5-6 minutes for lamb kidneys, turning frequently.
  4. While the kidneys cook, prepare the mustard sauce:
  5. Dice shallots.
  6. Combine Dijon mustard, 1 tablespoon butter, and chopped parsley in a jar.
  7. Prepare the flambéed sauce:
  8. Sauté mushrooms ahead of time.
  9. Combine thickened meat stock, Worcestershire sauce, and cream in a jar.
  10. Once the kidneys are slightly stiffened, remove them from the pan and set aside.
  11. Add diced shallots to the pan and cook for a moment.
  12. Pour in the dry white vermouth and bring to a boil.
  13. Reduce the vermouth until it is almost a syrup.
  14. Slice the kidneys.
  15. Add the mustard butter to the reduced vermouth.
  16. Stir in lemon juice.
  17. Add the sliced kidneys and their juices to the sauce.
  18. Stir in the chopped parsley.
  19. Serve the kidneys with the mustard sauce.
  20. For the flambéed kidneys:
    • Heat the pan with the kidneys.
    • Pour in the brandy and ignite.
    • Once the flames subside, add the sautéed mushrooms, thickened meat stock mixture, and Worcestershire sauce.
    • Stir in cream.
    • Slice the kidneys.
    • Add the sliced kidneys and their juices to the sauce.
    • Season with salt and pepper.
  21. Serve the flambéed kidneys with hot French bread.

rustic_tart.txt - Rustic Tart

Objectives

  • Learn to make a quick and easy rustic tart dough
  • Create two different tart variations: one sweet and one savory
  • Discover the versatility of this dough for various fillings

Ingredients

Sweet Tart - 1 1/2 cups berries (any combination) - 1 tablespoon sugar - 1 dab butter - 1 teaspoon sugar (for sprinkling) - 1 tablespoon water (for brushing)

Savory Tart - 2 ounces Monterey Jack cheese - 2 ounces mozzarella cheese - Basil (chiffonade or torn) - Sliced plum tomatoes

Tart Dough - 1 cup unsifted all-purpose flour - 1/4 cup cornmeal - 1/2 teaspoon salt - 1 teaspoon sugar - 3 tablespoons sour cream - 5 tablespoons water - 7 tablespoons unsalted butter (cold, cut into chunks)

Instructions

  1. Combine flour, cornmeal, salt, and sugar in a bowl.
  2. Cut in butter using a pastry blender until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs.
  3. Whisk together sour cream and water.
  4. Gradually add sour cream mixture to the flour mixture, stirring until just combined.
  5. Divide the dough in half and shape each half into a disc.
  6. Wrap each disc in plastic wrap and chill for 2 hours.
  7. Roll out one disc of dough into an 11-inch circle.
  8. Transfer the dough to a baking sheet, letting it drape over the edges.
  9. Arrange Monterey Jack and mozzarella cheese in the center of the dough.
  10. Top with torn basil and sliced plum tomatoes.
  11. Fold the edges of the dough over the filling.
  12. Roll out the second disc of dough into an 11-inch circle.
  13. Place the berries in the center of the dough.
  14. Sprinkle with sugar and dot with butter.
  15. Fold the edges of the dough over the filling.
  16. Brush both tarts with water and sprinkle with sugar.
  17. Bake both tarts at 400 degrees Fahrenheit for 20 minutes, or until golden brown and the filling is bubbly.
  18. Let the tarts cool slightly before serving.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GfPBSc6xXyw

salade_nicoise.txt - Salade Niçoise

Objectives

  • Learn to make the classic composed salad, Salade Niçoise.
  • Understand the importance of using fresh ingredients and preparing each component separately.
  • Discover the history and cultural significance of this French dish.

Ingredients

  • 1/4 teaspoon salt
  • 1/2 teaspoon dry mustard
  • Freshly ground pepper
  • Lemon juice
  • 1/2 cup olive oil
  • 1/2 cup wine vinegar
  • 1 clove garlic
  • 1/2 teaspoon basil
  • 1/2 cup water
  • 2-3 tablespoons white wine or chicken stock
  • 1 shallot or scallion
  • 1 head Boston lettuce
  • 5 salted anchovies
  • 100 grams olives from Venice
  • 100 grams capers
  • 1 can tuna
  • 1 pound boiling potatoes
  • 1 bunch string beans
  • 4-6 hard-boiled eggs
  • Fresh parsley

Instructions

  1. Make the vinaigrette:
  2. Using a garlic press, crush the garlic with 1/4 teaspoon of salt.
  3. Add the crushed garlic to a bowl and mix in the wine vinegar, lemon juice, dry mustard, pepper, and basil.
  4. Gradually whisk in the olive oil until the dressing is emulsified.
  5. Prepare the potatoes:
  6. Steam the potatoes in their jackets until tender, about 20 minutes.
  7. While still warm, slice the potatoes and place them in a bowl.
  8. Add chopped shallot, salt, pepper, white wine or chicken stock, and water to the potatoes.
  9. Gently toss the potatoes and let them sit for a while to absorb the liquid.
  10. Prepare the lettuce:
  11. Wash the Boston lettuce thoroughly and dry it thoroughly using a salad spinner or by wrapping it in a towel.
  12. Prepare the anchovies:
  13. Rinse the anchovies to remove excess salt and soak them in water for 40 minutes.
  14. Fillet the anchovies using forks and arrange them on a small plate.
  15. Drizzle a small amount of vinaigrette over the anchovies.
  16. Assemble the salad:
  17. Arrange the lettuce on a large platter.
  18. Place the potato salad in the center of the platter.
  19. Arrange the tomatoes in groups around the outside of the platter.
  20. Season the tomatoes with salt and a little vinaigrette.
  21. Place the string beans in four piles around the platter.
  22. Arrange the halved hard-boiled eggs around the platter.
  23. Scatter the olives and capers around the platter.
  24. Place the tuna in the center of the platter.
  25. Garnish with fresh parsley.
  26. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-hhssf-dHnE

salmon_coulibiac.txt - Salmon Coulibiac

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic Russian salmon dish
  • Create a decorative pastry crust using mock puff pastry
  • Utilize canned salmon to create a delicious and impressive meal

Ingredients

For the Pastry Case:

  • 4 cups all-purpose flour
  • 1 3/4 sticks (14 tablespoons) chilled, unsalted butter
  • 4 tablespoons shortening
  • 2 teaspoons salt
  • 3/4 cup cold water

For the Filling:

  • 2 cups finely chopped mushrooms, sautéed in butter
  • 1/2 cup chopped scallions
  • 1/2 cup chopped shallots
  • 1 cup white vermouth
  • 1/4 cup cognac (optional)
  • 1 large can of salmon
  • 1 small can of salmon
  • 1 teaspoon oregano
  • 1/2 cup fresh parsley
  • Salt to taste
  • Risotto (cooked with onions and fish or chicken stock)

For the Sauce:

  • 2 tablespoons butter
  • 2 tablespoons all-purpose flour
  • 2 cups hot milk
  • Salmon juices
  • Salt to taste

Instructions

  1. Prepare the pastry case:
  2. Combine flour, chilled butter, shortening, and salt.
  3. Gradually add cold water until a firm, pliable dough forms.
  4. Chill the dough for at least one hour or overnight.
  5. Butter a 13-inch angel loaf pan.
  6. Roll out the dough and place it in the pan.
  7. Trim the excess dough to create a case about 2 inches wide.
  8. Prick the bottom and sides of the dough with a fork.
  9. Bake in a 425 degree oven for 8 minutes.
  10. Turn the case upside down on a rack to cool.
  11. Prepare the filling:
  12. Sauté chopped mushrooms in butter.
  13. Add chopped scallions and shallots and cook until softened.
  14. Deglaze the pan with white vermouth and cognac (optional).
  15. Remove the skin and bones from the canned salmon using a fork.
  16. Add the salmon to the pan along with the oregano and parsley.
  17. Simmer until the sauce has reduced slightly.
  18. Prepare the sauce:
  19. Melt butter in a saucepan.
  20. Whisk in flour and cook for 2 minutes until the mixture is foamy.
  21. Gradually whisk in hot milk, starting with a small amount.
  22. Add the reserved salmon juices and cook until the sauce thickens.
  23. Season with salt to taste.
  24. Assemble the coulibiac:
  25. Place a layer of risotto in the bottom of the cooled pastry case.
  26. Top with a layer of salmon mixture.
  27. Spoon some sauce over the salmon.
  28. Repeat the layers of risotto, salmon, and sauce until the case is full.
  29. Prepare the top crust:
  30. Roll out the remaining pastry dough into a rectangle.
  31. Brush the dough with egg wash.
  32. Fold the dough in thirds, then chill for an hour.
  33. Roll out the dough again into a rectangle, slightly longer and wider than the case.
  34. Brush the top of the filling with egg wash.
  35. Gently place the top crust over the filling, pressing the edges to seal.
  36. Decorate the top crust:
  37. Cut out leaf shapes from the remaining pastry.
  38. Use a knife to make ribs in the leaves.
  39. Attach the leaves to the top crust using egg wash.
  40. Cut long strips of pastry and make "S" shapes for the salmon.
  41. Attach the strips to the top crust.
  42. Use a knife to make air holes in the top crust.
  43. Create funnels from triangular pieces of paper.
  44. Insert the funnels into the air holes.
  45. Bake the coulibiac:
  46. Bake in a 425 degree oven for 40 minutes to an hour, or until the steam comes out of the funnels.
  47. Serve:
  48. Let the coulibiac cool slightly before serving.
  49. Serve with a green salad, buttered peas, or buttered broccoli.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3lSP7TvAqBg

salmon_poaching.txt - Poached Salmon with Carpaccio and Chocolate Sac du Bonbon

Objectives

Ingredients

For the Salmon - 10-pound silver salmon - 1 teaspoon of salt - Oil (optional) - 2 cups sliced onions - 1 cup sliced carrots - 1 cup sliced celery - 1 herb bouquet (bay leaf, parsley, thyme) - 1 bottle dry white vermouth (or dry white wine) - 2 cups chicken stock (or fish stock) - Water (as needed) - Aluminum foil

salmon_roulade.txt - Salmon Roulade with Gazpacho Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a Salmon Roulade with a Gazpacho sauce.
  • Understand how to remove pin bones from salmon.
  • Learn how to pound salmon into a flat shape.
  • Learn how to roll salmon in parchment paper and foil.
  • Learn how to prepare a Gazpacho sauce with mayonnaise.
  • Understand the importance of chilling the salmon and sauce.
  • Learn to cook the salmon in foil and then sear it.
  • Learn how to prepare a horseradish crust for grouper.
  • Learn how to bread a grouper with a horseradish crust.
  • Learn how to cook a grouper with a horseradish crust.

Ingredients

  • 1 Fileted Norwegian Salmon
  • Kosher Salt
  • Fresh Pepper
  • Cooked Leek Julienne
  • Parchment Paper
  • Plastic Wrap
  • Meat Pounder
  • String
  • Canola Oil
  • Black Pepper
  • 1/2 Lemon
  • Red Wine Vinegar
  • Olive Oil Mayonnaise
  • Cucumber Juice
  • Tomato Juice
  • Mineral Water
  • Cayenne Pepper
  • Peanut Oil
  • Mashed Potatoes
  • Chive Oil
  • Crisp Leeks
  • Long Chives
  • Red Grouper
  • Horseradish Root
  • Bread Crumbs
  • Eggs
  • Milk
  • Flour
  • Fresh Parsley
  • Fresh Thyme
  • Fresh Rosemary

Instructions

  1. Remove the pin bones from the salmon by running your finger down the middle of the fillet and uplifting them.
  2. Use needle-nose pliers to pull out the bones.
  3. Split the salmon like a book, following the full length with a sharp knife.
  4. Place the salmon on a piece of parchment paper and cover with plastic wrap.
  5. Pound the salmon with a meat pounder until it is evenly flattened.
  6. Season the salmon with salt and pepper.
  7. Spread a thin layer of cooked leek julienne across the salmon.
  8. Roll the salmon tightly in the parchment paper, tucking the paper as you go.
  9. Twist the ends of the parchment paper and tie with a piece of string.
  10. Refrigerate the salmon for one hour.
  11. Brush a piece of foil with canola oil.
  12. Unroll the salmon onto the foil, removing the parchment paper.
  13. Lightly coat the salmon with cracked black pepper.
  14. Roll the salmon tightly in the foil, twisting the ends.
  15. Refrigerate the salmon for 3-4 hours.
  16. Prepare the Gazpacho sauce by whisking together olive oil mayonnaise, cucumber juice, tomato juice, mineral water, salt, cayenne pepper, lemon juice, and red wine vinegar.
  17. Refrigerate the sauce for two hours.
  18. Heat peanut oil in a pan to 500-550 degrees.
  19. Place the salmon in the hot oil and roll it to brown all sides.
  20. Cook for 3-5 minutes, depending on the size of the salmon.
  21. Remove the salmon from the pan and let cool to room temperature for one hour.
  22. Adjust the seasoning in the sauce, adding more salt or pepper as needed.
  23. Trim the ends of the salmon and slice it into 3/4 inch thick pieces while still in the foil.
  24. Place the salmon slices on a plate and ladle the Gazpacho sauce over them.
  25. Garnish with diced cucumber, roasted red pepper, and chopped chives.
  26. Season the red grouper with salt and pepper.
  27. Grate the horseradish root until you have 3/4 cup.
  28. Mix the grated horseradish with bread crumbs.
  29. Prepare the egg wash by whisking together eggs and milk.
  30. Bread the grouper by dusting it with seasoned flour, dipping it in the egg wash, and then coating it with the horseradish bread crumb mixture.
  31. Refrigerate the breaded grouper for a couple of hours.
  32. Heat canola oil in a pan to 350 degrees.
  33. Cook the grouper with the crust side down first for 2 minutes to brown the crust.
  34. Turn the grouper over and cook until the fish is cooked through.
  35. Drain the grouper on paper towels.
  36. Place the grouper on a mound of mashed potatoes.
  37. Drizzle chive oil around the potatoes.
  38. Garnish with crisp leeks and long chives.
