santa_barbara_fish_stew.txt - Santa Barbara Fish Stew

Objectives

  • Prepare a flavorful and hearty Santa Barbara fish stew.
  • Learn how to properly prepare and cook fish stock.
  • Discover the secrets to making a delicious red garlic sauce.

Ingredients

Fish Stock - 1 whole cowcod - Water to cover the fish frame - Salt to taste

Soup Base - 1/2 cup fruity olive oil - 1 big handful of onions, chopped - 1 big handful of leeks, chopped - Chopped garlic to taste - Chopped fresh tomatoes - Canned Italian plum tomatoes - Thyme sprigs - Fennel seeds - Pinch of saffron flowers - 2 pieces of dried orange peel - 3 quarts of fish stock

Red Garlic Sauce - 4-5 cloves of garlic, mashed to a puree - Salt to taste - Red pimento, pounded - 2 egg yolks - 2-3 tablespoons breadcrumbs - Hot pepper sauce - Cayenne pepper - Olive oil

Stew - Spider crabs - Mussels - Finfish (rock cod filet, halibut tail, pompano, white sea bass, halibut steaks)

Rolls - 1 1/2 tablespoons dry, active yeast - 1 cup warm water (89-100 degrees) - 1/4 teaspoon sugar - 3 1/2 cups all-purpose flour - 3 tablespoons whole wheat flour - 2 1/2 teaspoons salt - 1/2 cup water - Cornmeal

Dessert - 2 vanilla beans - 1 1/2 cups sugar - 12 egg yolks - Hot milk - 1 quart lightly whipped cream - 1 stick of melted butter - 1 cup egg whites - 2/3 cup flour - 1/2 pound confectioners' sugar - 2 teaspoons vanilla - Toasted sliced almonds - Hot chocolate sauce

Instructions

  1. Prepare the fish stock:
  2. Remove the fillets from the whole cowcod, leaving the frame, head, and bones.
  3. Place the fish frame in a pot and cover with water.
  4. Add salt to taste.
  5. Bring the pot to a boil, then reduce heat and simmer for 30 minutes.
  6. Make the soup base:
  7. Heat the olive oil in a large pot over medium heat.
  8. Add the onions, leeks, garlic, tomatoes, thyme, fennel seeds, saffron flowers, and orange peel.
  9. Cook for a few minutes, stirring occasionally.
  10. Strain the fish stock and add it to the pot.
  11. Bring the soup base to a simmer and cook for 45 minutes.
  12. Prepare the red garlic sauce:
  13. Mash the garlic with salt until it forms a smooth puree.
  14. Add the red pimento and pound until well combined.
  15. Add the egg yolks and pound until smooth.
  16. Stir in the breadcrumbs, hot pepper sauce, and cayenne pepper.
  17. Gradually whisk in the olive oil until the sauce is thick and creamy.
  18. Assemble the stew:
  19. Add the finfish to the simmering soup base.
  20. Cook for a few minutes, until the fish is cooked through.
  21. Add the spider crabs and mussels.
  22. Cook for a few more minutes, until the mussels are open.
  23. Make the rolls:
  24. Proof the yeast by combining it with warm water and sugar.
  25. In a large bowl, combine the flours, salt, and yeast mixture.
  26. Add the water and knead the dough for 1 minute.
  27. Let the dough rest for 4-5 minutes, then knead for another 4-5 minutes until it forms a ball.
  28. Place the dough in a greased bowl and let it rise for 3 hours.
  29. Punch down the dough and let it rise again for 1 1/2 hours.
  30. Divide the dough into 12 equal pieces and shape them into balls.
  31. Place the rolls on a floured linen towel and let them rise for 1 1/2 hours.
  32. Preheat the oven to 450 degrees F.
  33. Transfer the rolls to a cornmeal-sprinkled baking sheet and slash them with a razor.
  34. Bake the rolls for 20 minutes, spritzing with water three times at 2-minute intervals.
  35. Make the dessert:
  36. Pulverize the vanilla beans with 1/2 cup of sugar.
  37. Combine the vanilla bean mixture with the remaining sugar.
  38. Beat the egg yolks in a mixer until they form a ribbon.
  39. Gradually add the sugar mixture to the egg yolks, beating constantly.
  40. Slowly pour the hot milk into the mixture, beating until combined.
  41. Cook the custard over medium heat until it thickens.
  42. Pour the custard over ice and refrigerate until chilled.
  43. Fold the chilled custard into the whipped cream.
  44. Pour the mixture into an ice cream maker and freeze.
  45. Form the cookies by placing batter on a cookie sheet and rotating the pan to spread the batter.
  46. Bake the cookies at 375 degrees F until golden brown.
  47. Form the cookies into tulip shapes and fill them with ice cream, almonds, and chocolate sauce.

Other Ingredients - 1/4 cup raisins - Rum - Whipped cream - Glacé fruits - Almonds - Champagne - Orange - Crème fraîche - Raspberry sauce - Papaya - Kirsch - Strawberries - Blackberries - Raspberries

savory_choux_pastry.txt - Savory Choux Pastry

Objectives

  • Learn to make a savory choux pastry using cucumber and red onion juice
  • Understand the importance of proper cooking and egg incorporation for a smooth choux paste
  • Learn to pipe and fill choux pastry with savory fillings like salmon mousse and vegetable medley

Ingredients

  • 1 cup of milk
  • 1 peeled cucumber
  • 1/2 cup of cucumber juice
  • 1 1/2 tablespoons of red onion juice
  • 2 tablespoons of butter
  • 1 cup of all-purpose flour
  • 7 eggs
  • 1 teaspoon of fresh dill
  • 1/4 cup of finely diced red pepper
  • 1/4 cup of finely diced cucumber
  • 1/4 cup of diced mango
  • 1/4 cup of diced onion
  • 1/4 cup of diced summer squash
  • 1/4 cup of diced raw carrot
  • 1/4 cup of diced celery
  • 1/4 cup of diced tomato
  • 1 tablespoon of balsamic vinegar
  • 1 cup of mascarpone cheese
  • 1/2 pound of smoked salmon
  • 4 ounces of cream cheese
  • 1/2 teaspoon of Pernod
  • 1/2 teaspoon of black pepper

Instructions

  1. Combine 1/2 cup of milk with 1/2 cup of cucumber juice.
  2. Add 1 1/2 tablespoons of red onion juice and 2 tablespoons of butter to the milk mixture.
  3. Bring the mixture to a boil over medium heat.
  4. Add 1 cup of all-purpose flour to the boiling mixture, stirring vigorously until a smooth paste forms.
  5. Transfer the paste to a stand mixer.
  6. Add eggs one at a time, incorporating each egg fully before adding the next.
  7. Stir in 1 teaspoon of fresh dill until evenly distributed.
  8. Pipe choux pastry onto parchment-lined baking sheets.
  9. Bake at 400 degrees Fahrenheit for 10-15 minutes, then reduce heat to 350 degrees Fahrenheit and bake for an additional 15 minutes.
  10. Let the choux pastry cool completely before filling.
  11. For the vegetable medley filling, combine 1/4 cup each of finely diced red pepper, cucumber, mango, onion, summer squash, raw carrot, celery, and tomato.
  12. Season with salt, pepper, and 1 tablespoon of balsamic vinegar.
  13. Fold in 1 cup of mascarpone cheese.
  14. For the salmon mousse filling, combine 1/2 pound of smoked salmon and 4 ounces of cream cheese in a food processor.
  15. Process until a smooth paste forms.
  16. Add 1/2 teaspoon of Pernod and 1/2 teaspoon of black pepper to the salmon mousse and pulse until combined.
  17. To fill the choux pastry, use a small tip to puncture a hole in the bottom of the profiteroles and fill with salmon mousse.
  18. To fill the eclairs, slice them open lengthwise and fill with vegetable medley.
  19. Garnish the profiteroles with a dollop of salmon mousse and a sprig of fresh dill.
  20. Serve immediately.

seared_filet_mignon_steaks_in_texas_style_tomato_and_chile_sauce.txt - Seared Filet Mignon Steaks in Texas Style Tomato and Chile Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to make a flavorful tomatillo sauce with fresh chiles.
  • Master the technique of searing scallops for a crispy exterior and tender interior.
  • Create a delicious corn pudding side dish.

Ingredients

  • 2-3 serrano chiles
  • 4-6 tomatillos
  • 1/2 white onion
  • 2 garlic cloves
  • Water
  • Shiitake mushrooms
  • Cilantro
  • Fresh corn
  • Milk
  • Cornmeal
  • Butter
  • Chicken stock
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Sugar
  • Cream
  • Fresh tomato salsa
  • Cotija cheese
  • Peanut oil

Instructions

  1. Remove the stems from the serrano chiles and add them to a pot.
  2. Peel the tomatillos and add them to the pot.
  3. Coarsely chop the onion and add it to the pot.
  4. Add two garlic cloves to the pot.
  5. Add enough water to cover the ingredients.
  6. Bring the pot to a boil and cook for 10 minutes, or until the tomatillos are soft.
  7. Drain the liquid from the pot and add the tomatillos, onion, and garlic to a blender.
  8. Pulse the blender to create a textured sauce.
  9. Cut the shiitake mushrooms into medium-sized pieces.
  10. Chop the cilantro, including the stems.
  11. Grate the fresh corn on a cheese grater to create a puree.
  12. Bring milk to a boil.
  13. Slowly add cornmeal to the boiling milk while whisking constantly.
  14. Add the corn puree to the thickened milk mixture.
  15. Cook the corn pudding until thickened.
  16. Remove the corn pudding from heat and keep warm.
  17. Heat two tablespoons of butter in a pan over high heat.
  18. Add the mushrooms to the pan and stir slowly, allowing them to release their juices and caramelize.
  19. Add the tomatillo sauce to the pan and stir to dissolve the caramelized juices.
  20. Add 1/2 cup to 1 cup of chicken stock to thin the sauce.
  21. Season the sauce with salt, pepper, and sugar to taste.
  22. Set the sauce aside.
  23. Season the scallops with salt and pepper.
  24. Heat a skillet over high heat.
  25. Add a small amount of butter to the skillet and melt to coat.
  26. Sear the scallops in the hot skillet until they develop a crispy crust.
  27. Reduce heat and allow the scallops to cook through until firm and slightly springy.
  28. Heat the tomatillo sauce and add the cilantro.
  29. Bring the sauce to a boil.
  30. Stir two tablespoons of cream into the corn pudding.
  31. Plate the dish by placing a small amount of corn pudding in the center of a dinner plate.
  32. Spoon some of the tomatillo sauce around the corn pudding.
  33. Place three seared scallops on top of the corn pudding.
  34. Drizzle cold cream over the scallops and sauce.
  35. Garnish with fresh tomato salsa and a sprig of cilantro.

Objectives

  • Learn to make a flavorful red chile sauce using dried chiles.
  • Master the technique of searing filet mignon for a crispy crust and tender inside.
  • Create a delicious avocado relish and cotija cheese topping.

Ingredients

  • 1/2 white onion
  • 2 garlic cloves
  • 4-6 tomatoes
  • 4-6 pasilla chiles
  • Chicken stock
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Brown sugar
  • Cilantro
  • Avocado relish
  • Cotija cheese
  • Peanut oil

Instructions

  1. Chop the onion and place it in a skillet.
  2. Add the garlic cloves on top of the onion.
  3. Add the tomatoes to the skillet.
  4. Place the skillet under a hot broiler to blister and char the tomatoes and onions.
  5. While the tomatoes are broiling, toast the pasilla chiles in a medium-warm skillet until they puff up and release a strong chocolate, coffee, and chile aroma.
  6. Transfer the broiled tomatoes, onions, and garlic to a blender.
  7. Add the chicken stock to the skillet to deglaze and capture the caramelized juices from the tomatoes.
  8. Add the chicken stock to the blender.
  9. Remove the ends of the pasilla chiles and discard the seeds.
  10. Break the pasilla chiles into smaller pieces and add them to the blender.
  11. Puree the ingredients in the blender to create a smooth chile sauce.
  12. Season the filet mignon steaks with salt and pepper.
  13. Heat a skillet over high heat.
  14. Add a small amount of peanut oil to the skillet.
  15. Sear the filet mignon steaks in the hot skillet until they develop a crispy crust.
  16. Remove the steaks from the skillet and set aside.
  17. Add the chile sauce to the skillet and cook, picking up any remaining juices from the beef.
  18. Season the sauce with salt, pepper, and brown sugar to taste.
  19. Add cilantro to the sauce.
  20. Return the filet mignon steaks to the skillet and allow them to cook slowly in the sauce until they reach medium-rare.
  21. Plate the dish by placing a filet mignon steak in the center of a plate.
  22. Spoon the chile sauce over the steak.
  23. Top the steak with avocado relish.
  24. Sprinkle cotija cheese over the top.

shrimp_croustade_nantua.txt - Croûstades aux crevettes à la Nantua

Objectives

  • Learn to cook shrimp in a French mirepoix
  • Master the art of making shrimp butter
  • Create a delicious Nantua sauce for a sophisticated shrimp dish
  • Assemble and bake croustades for a stunning presentation
  • Understand the importance of using quality ingredients and French techniques

Ingredients

  • 2 pounds of shrimp
  • 1 1/2 cups diced onions, carrots, and celery (mirepoix)
  • 3-4 tablespoons of butter
  • 1/4 teaspoon of black pepper
  • 1/4 teaspoon of thyme
  • Salt to taste
  • 1/4 cup of Cognac
  • 1/2 cup of dry white French vermouth
  • 1 tomato
  • 1 bay leaf
  • Fresh parsley
  • 1 cup of shrimp stock
  • 2 tablespoons of butter
  • 2 tablespoons of flour
  • 1 egg yolk
  • A splash of cream
  • 2 cups of peeled shrimp
  • Melted butter for brushing croustades
  • 1 whole unsliced white bread
  • 2 tablespoons of shrimp butter
  • Chopped truffle or fresh parsley for garnish

Instructions

  1. Dice onions, carrots, and celery into small pieces to make a mirepoix.
  2. Sauté the mirepoix in butter until softened.
  3. Add frozen raw shrimp to the pan with butter, mirepoix, salt, pepper, and thyme.
  4. Cook the shrimp over moderate heat until the shells turn pink, about 2-3 minutes.
  5. Deglaze the pan with Cognac and ignite it to burn off the alcohol.
  6. Add dry white French vermouth and a squeezed tomato to the pan.
  7. Include a bay leaf, thyme, and fresh parsley.
  8. Cover the pan and simmer the shrimp for 5-7 minutes until cooked through.
  9. Let the shrimp cool in the liquid to absorb the flavors.
  10. Peel the shrimp, saving the shells for shrimp butter.
  11. To make shrimp butter (French method):
  12. Pound shrimp shells and butter together in a marble mortar with a wooden pestle for 20-30 minutes.
  13. Strain the mixture through a sieve to remove the shells.
  14. To make shrimp butter (modern method):
  15. Fill a blender with very hot water.
  16. Heat butter separately.
  17. Add shrimp shells and hot butter to the blender.
  18. Blend until smooth and strain through a sieve.
  19. To make Nantua sauce:
  20. Sauté butter and flour together until foamy and frothy for about 2 minutes.
  21. Strain the shrimp stock into the roux.
  22. Bring the sauce to a boil and thicken to a desired consistency.
  23. Temper an egg yolk with cream and a little hot sauce.
  24. Add the tempered egg yolk mixture to the sauce and whisk until smooth.
  25. To assemble croustades:
  26. Cut a piece of stale white bread into squares and remove the crusts.
  27. Scoop out the center of the bread, leaving a hollow shell.
  28. Brush the croustades with melted butter.
  29. Bake in a 450-degree oven for 5-6 minutes.
  30. To assemble the dish:
  31. Add the cooked shrimp to the Nantua sauce.
  32. Stir in 2 tablespoons of shrimp butter.
  33. Fill the croustades with the shrimp mixture.
  34. Garnish with chopped truffle or fresh parsley.
  35. Serve immediately and enjoy!

smoked_salmon_egg_torte.txt - Smoked Salmon Egg Torte

Objectives

  • Learn how to brine, smoke, and prepare salmon for a stunning presentation.
  • Master the art of making a light and flavorful egg torte.
  • Assemble a beautiful and delicious smoked salmon egg torte for a special occasion.

Ingredients

  • 24 oz Bodega Bay salmon
  • 1/2 cup water
  • 1/4 cup salt
  • 1/4 cup brown sugar
  • 1 bay leaf, crushed
  • 1 garlic clove, smashed
  • 1/4 cup vinegar
  • 1 tablespoon black peppercorns
  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • 1/2 teaspoon chervil
  • 1/2 teaspoon tarragon
  • 1/2 cup applewood chips, soaked in water
  • 20 eggs
  • 1/2 cup half-and-half
  • 1/4 cup chives, finely chopped
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • Salt and pepper to taste
  • Brioche bread, for the shell
  • Caviar, for garnish
  • Red onion, thinly sliced, for garnish
  • Crème fraîche, for garnish

Instructions

  1. Brine the salmon: Combine water, salt, brown sugar, bay leaf, garlic, vinegar, and peppercorns in a bowl. Stir until the salt and sugar dissolve.
  2. Place the salmon flesh-side down in the brine and refrigerate for 1 hour.
  3. Pat the salmon dry and brush with olive oil.
  4. Combine chervil and tarragon in a bowl and bruise with the back of a knife.
  5. Place the herbs on top of the salmon.
  6. Prepare the smoker: Add hot charcoal briquettes to the smoker.
  7. Add soaked applewood chips to the smoker, leaving some holes for air circulation.
  8. Smoke the salmon: Place the salmon skin-side down on the smoker and smoke for 20 minutes.
  9. Remove the salmon from the smoker and place on ice to stop the cooking process.
  10. Prepare the brioche shell: Cut and assemble pieces of brioche bread into a mold to create a crust.
  11. Toast the brioche shell under a broiler until golden brown.
  12. Whisk the eggs: Beat 20 eggs in a bowl with a vigorous back and forth motion until the yolks are well combined.
  13. Add half-and-half to the eggs and whisk until combined.
  14. Finely chop the chives.
  15. Melt butter in a pan over medium heat.
  16. Add the eggs to the pan and cook slowly, stirring constantly to prevent browning.
  17. Season with salt and pepper.
  18. Add the chives to the eggs towards the end of cooking.
  19. Remove the eggs from the heat and pour into the toasted brioche shell.
  20. Bake the egg torte in the oven for 5 minutes to set the eggs.
  21. Remove the egg torte from the oven and let cool slightly.
  22. Gently lift the egg torte out of the mold and place on a plate.
  23. Flake the smoked salmon and arrange it on top and around the egg torte.
  24. Sprinkle red onion slices around the egg torte.
  25. Garnish with a dollop of caviar, chives, and a drizzle of crème fraîche.
  26. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CAus5pAGK40

smoked_sirloin_farecki.txt - Smoked Sirloin with Farecki Grain and Red Wine Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn to smoke sirloin with alderwood chips for a subtle smoky flavor
  • Prepare a flavorful farecki grain dish with garlic, shallots, and chicken stock
  • Create a rich red wine sauce with veal stock, shallots, and thyme

Ingredients

  • 2.5-3 pounds sirloin (New York strip)
  • Alderwood chips
  • White truffle oil (or olive oil infused with herbs)
  • Farecki grain (or wheat berries)
  • Quinoa
  • Olive oil
  • Garlic (chopped)
  • Shallots (chopped)
  • Chicken stock
  • Roasted red peppers (peeled and seeded)
  • Harissa (hot pepper sauce)
  • Serrano chiles (dried)
  • Onion
  • Salt
  • Pepper
  • Chives (chopped)
  • Cabernet Sauvignon
  • Brown veal stock (or chicken bouillon)
  • Heavy cream
  • Fresh thyme (chopped)
  • Butter
  • Potato (Idaho baked)
  • Egg whites
  • 4-1-1 potatoes (4 parts potato, 1 part egg white, 1 part butter)
  • Thyme (fresh)
  • Chervil
  • Tarragon

Instructions

  1. Trim the fat from the sirloin, leaving a thin layer for flavor.
  2. Cut the sirloin in half to create two thinner pieces.
  3. Place alderwood chips in a wok or other heat-safe container.
  4. Smoke the sirloin for 15 minutes, covering the wok to create a smoky environment.
  5. Remove the sirloin from the smoke and rub with white truffle oil.
  6. Place the sirloin in a bag and refrigerate for 24 hours.
  7. Clean the farecki grain by removing any sticks or stones.
  8. Heat olive oil in a pan over medium heat.
  9. Add the farecki grain and stir to coat.
  10. Add chopped garlic and sauté until fragrant.
  11. Add chopped shallots and coat with olive oil.
  12. Pour in chicken stock and bring to a simmer.
  13. Cover the pan with a French cooking paper airplane to allow steam to escape.
  14. Cook the farecki grain for 40-45 minutes.
  15. While the farecki grain cooks, prepare the harissa sauce.
  16. Roast red peppers until the skin peels off easily.
  17. Remove the seeds from the roasted peppers.
  18. Combine roasted peppers, serrano chiles, garlic, onion, and harissa sauce in a blender.
  19. Blend until smooth and taste for spiciness.
  20. Season the farecki grain with harissa sauce, salt, and pepper.
  21. Stir in chopped chives.
  22. Set the farecki grain aside and keep warm.
  23. Prepare the shallot garnish by simmering chopped shallots in chicken stock until tender.
  24. Make 4-1-1 potatoes by combining cooked potatoes, egg whites, and butter in a food mill.
  25. Puree until smooth.
  26. Brush a baking sheet with olive oil.
  27. Place a cardboard stencil on the baking sheet.
  28. Spread the 4-1-1 potato mixture evenly over the stencil.
  29. Sprinkle with thyme.
  30. Bake in a 350-degree oven for 10 minutes, or until golden brown.
  31. While the 4-1-1 potatoes bake, prepare the sirloin for searing.
  32. Season the sirloin with salt and pepper.
  33. Heat olive oil in a pan over medium-high heat.
  34. Sear the sirloin on all four sides until browned.
  35. Chop shallots for the sauce and garnish.
  36. Deglaze the pan with a little red wine and scrape up any caramelized bits.
  37. Add cracked peppercorns and thyme to the pan.
  38. Pour in red wine and simmer until reduced.
  39. Add brown veal stock and reduce further.
  40. Set the sauce aside and keep warm.
  41. Place the sirloin in a preheated oven to finish roasting.
  42. Check the sirloin for doneness by feeling for resistance.
  43. Remove the sirloin from the oven and let it rest for 5-10 minutes.
  44. Strain the sauce through a fine-mesh sieve.
  45. Season the sauce with salt and pepper to taste.
  46. Add a tablespoon of whipped cream to the sauce and let it simmer until incorporated.
  47. Plate the dish by placing a quenelle of farecki grain on the plate.
  48. Top with a slice of sirloin.
  49. Drizzle with shallot sauce and garnish with whole shallots.
  50. Add 4-1-1 potato chips and garnish with fresh herbs, such as chervil, tarragon, or chives.
  51. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=paZ0ZsmMqcY

soft_shell_crabs_with_coleslaw_and_pasta.txt - Soft-Shell Crabs with Cole Slaw and Pasta

Objectives

  • Learn to clean and prepare soft-shell crabs
  • Make fresh pasta from scratch
  • Prepare a simple but flavorful coleslaw
  • Sauté soft-shell crabs with clarified butter
  • Assemble the dish with pasta, coleslaw, and a lemon butter sauce

Ingredients

  • Soft-shell Crabs (3)
  • Flour (for coating crabs)
  • Canola oil (for sautéing)
  • Clarified Butter (for sautéing and sauce)
  • Fresh pasta (recipe below)
  • Chicken stock (for cooking pasta)
  • Cold butter (for liaison)
  • Chives (for garnish)
  • Parsley (for garnish)
  • Lemon (for juice and zest)
  • Cole Slaw (recipe below)
  • Sugar
  • Water
  • Old Bay Seasoning
  • Freshly ground black pepper
  • Salt (sea salt)
  • Red bell pepper (julienned)
  • Yellow bell pepper (julienned)
  • Carrots (julienned)
  • Scallions (sliced)
  • Green cabbage
  • Fresh ginger (grated)
  • Saffron (steeped in hot water)
  • Semolina flour
  • All-purpose white flour
  • Eggs (3 yolks and 1 whole egg)

Instructions

  1. Clean the soft-shell crabs:
  2. Remove the brain, gills, and apron.
  3. Squeeze the center to remove the sand sac and tomalley.
  4. Make the fresh pasta:
  5. Combine 1 cup of semolina flour and 1 cup of all-purpose white flour in a bowl.
  6. Add 3 egg yolks and 1 whole egg.
  7. Season with salt.
  8. Mix until well combined.
  9. Add more flour if the dough is too wet, or more egg if the dough is too dry.
  10. Knead the dough until smooth and pliable.
  11. Add a pinch of saffron steeped in hot water for color.
  12. Wrap the dough in plastic wrap and let it rest for at least an hour.
  13. Pass the dough through a pasta machine, folding it over several times to ensure even color and texture.
  14. Dust the dough with flour to prevent sticking.
  15. Cut the pasta into thin ribbons using a knife or a pasta cutter.
  16. Let the pasta dry for a few minutes before cooking.
  17. Make the coleslaw dressing:
  18. Boil sugar and water together in a saucepan.
  19. Add Old Bay seasoning, freshly ground black pepper, and salt.
  20. Bring to a boil and then remove from heat.
  21. Let the dressing cool completely.
  22. Prepare the vegetables for the coleslaw:
  23. Blanch julienned red and yellow bell peppers in boiling salted water for 15 seconds.
  24. Immediately transfer to ice water to stop the cooking process.
  25. Blanch julienned carrots in boiling salted water for 15 seconds.
  26. Immediately transfer to ice water to stop the cooking process.
  27. Slice scallions thinly.
  28. Shred green cabbage.
  29. Assemble the coleslaw:
  30. Combine the blanched bell peppers, carrots, scallions, and shredded cabbage in a bowl.
  31. Pour the cooled dressing over the vegetables.
  32. Toss to coat.
  33. Refrigerate for at least an hour to allow the cabbage to wilt and the flavors to meld.
  34. Sauté the soft-shell crabs:
  35. Pat the cleaned crabs dry with paper towels.
  36. Coat the crabs in flour.
  37. Heat clarified butter and canola oil in a skillet over medium-high heat.
  38. Carefully add the crabs to the hot skillet, skin side down.
  39. Be careful as the crabs will steam and possibly pop.
  40. Sauté for about a minute per side, until golden brown.
  41. Cook the pasta:
  42. Bring chicken stock to a boil in a large pot.
  43. Add the pasta and cook until al dente, about 1-2 minutes.
  44. Drain the pasta and return it to the pot.
  45. Add a knob of cold butter and swirl to create a liaison (a silky sauce).
  46. Assemble the dish:
  47. Place the sautéed crabs on plates.
  48. Add a generous portion of pasta to each plate.
  49. Top with coleslaw.
  50. Drizzle with clarified butter and lemon juice.
  51. Garnish with chopped chives and parsley.
  52. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rLAlMrZj0xw

sole_poached_white_wine.txt - Filet de Sole Poché au Vin Blanc

Objectives

  • Learn to fillet a whole sole fish.
  • Prepare a classic French fish dish, Filet de Sole Poché au Vin Blanc.
  • Master the art of poaching fish in white wine.
  • Create a delicious white wine sauce with a velouté base.
  • Understand the importance of fresh ingredients and proper cooking techniques for a flavorful dish.

Ingredients

Fish - 2 1/2 pounds of sole fillets - Fish frame (optional) - 2/3 cup white wine or vermouth (for fish stock) - 1/2 teaspoon salt (for fish stock) - 1/2 carrot, chopped (for fish stock) - 1/2 onion, chopped (for fish stock) - 1 bay leaf (for fish stock) - Parsley stems (for fish stock) - 1 teaspoon chopped shallots or scallions (for baking dish) - 1 teaspoon butter (for baking dish) - Salt and white pepper (for seasoning fish fillets) - 1 teaspoon chopped shallots or scallions (for topping) - 1 teaspoon butter (for topping) - 1/2 cup dry white French vermouth (for poaching liquid) - Water (for poaching liquid)

Sauce - 3 tablespoons butter - 4 tablespoons flour - 1/4 cup cream (optional) - 1/4 cup grated Swiss cheese - Lemon juice (to taste)

Instructions

  1. Fillet the sole fish:
    • Cut along the line from the head to the tail to expose the backbone.
    • Use a flexible fish filleting knife to cut along the bone, separating the fillet from the skin.
    • Repeat on the other side of the fish.
    • Trim off any frilly edges and save them for fish stock.
    • Remove the skin from the fillets by wiggling a knife along the edge of a cutting board.
    • Score the skin side of the fillets with a knife to prevent curling.
    • Cut the fillets in half if desired.
  2. Prepare the fish stock (optional):
    • Chop the fish frame, skin, and trimmings.
    • Place the fish frame in a pan and cover with water.
    • Add white wine or vermouth, salt, chopped carrot, onion, bay leaf, and parsley stems.
    • Simmer for 20-30 minutes and strain.
  3. Prepare the baking dish:
    • Butter a shallow baking dish with about a teaspoon of butter.
    • Add chopped shallots or scallions to the bottom of the dish.
  4. Season the fish fillets:
    • Sprinkle salt and white pepper on both sides of the fillets.
  5. Arrange the fillets in the baking dish:
    • Lay the fillets flat or fold them in half, with the scored side facing inward.
    • Arrange the fillets in the dish, overlapping slightly.
  6. Add the remaining toppings:
    • Sprinkle another teaspoon of chopped shallots or scallions on top.
    • Add a teaspoon of butter.
  7. Add the poaching liquid:
    • Pour in enough dry white French vermouth and water to cover the fillets, just slightly above the top.
  8. Cover the dish:
    • Cover the dish with wax paper, folding it over twice.
  9. Preheat the oven to 350 degrees Fahrenheit.
  10. Heat the dish on the stovetop:
    • Place the dish on the stovetop over medium heat.
    • Heat until the liquid is just barely bubbling.
  11. Bake the fish:
    • Transfer the dish to the oven and bake on the bottom rung for 7-8 minutes.
    • The fish is done when it is opaque and white, and has a slight resistance when pressed.
  12. Drain the cooking liquid:
    • Remove the dish from the oven and drain the cooking liquid into a saucepan.
  13. Reduce the cooking liquid:
    • Boil the cooking liquid until it is reduced to about half a cup.
  14. Make the sauce:
    • Melt the butter in a saucepan.
    • Whisk in the flour and cook over moderate heat until foamy and frothy, about 2 minutes.
    • Gradually whisk in the reduced cooking liquid until the sauce reaches the desired thickness.
    • Stir in the cream (optional) and Swiss cheese.
    • Season with lemon juice to taste.
  15. Decorate the fish:
    • Pour the sauce over the fish fillets.
    • Sprinkle with grated Swiss cheese and a little bit of butter.
  16. Broil the fish:
    • Broil the fish for about 1 minute, until the cheese is melted and browned.
  17. Serve immediately:
    • Serve the fish hot, with a full-bodied dry white wine.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ouofqGBml3M

soupe_au_pistou.txt - Soupe au Pistou

Objectives

  • Learn to make a traditional Provençale vegetable soup
  • Prepare a soup base with potatoes, carrots, and leeks
  • Create a flavorful pistou topping for the soup

Ingredients

Soup Base - 2 cups diced potatoes - 2 cups diced carrots - 2 cups sliced leeks - 2 cups fresh white beans (or 1 can white beans) - 2 tablespoons salt - 3 quarts water

Green Vegetables - 1 1/2 cups diced green beans - 1 cup fresh green peas (optional) - 1 diced zucchini (optional) - 1 piece of stale white bread - 2 small handfuls of pasta or broken spaghetti - Pinch of saffron - Pepper to taste

Pistou - 4 cloves garlic - 1 tablespoon fresh basil (or good quality bottled basil) - 4 tablespoons tomato paste - 1/2 cup grated Parmesan cheese - 1/2 cup olive oil

Instructions

  1. Dice potatoes into 3/8-inch pieces.
  2. Bring 3 quarts of water to a rapid boil in a large pot.
  3. Add diced potatoes and 2 tablespoons of salt to the boiling water.
  4. Dice carrots into 3/8-inch pieces.
  5. Add diced carrots to the boiling water.
  6. Clean and slice leeks into 1/4-inch thick slices.
  7. Add sliced leeks to the boiling water.
  8. Add fresh white beans or 1 can of white beans (if using canned beans, add them later).
  9. Cook the soup base in a pressure cooker for 5 minutes or in an open pot for 30-40 minutes until the potatoes and onions are tender.
  10. Quickly reduce pressure in the pressure cooker by running cold water over it until the pressure releases with a sigh.
  11. While the soup base is cooking, prepare the cucumber soup.
  12. Chop 2-3 tablespoons of shallots or scallions.
  13. Peel and thinly slice 2 eight-inch cucumbers, setting aside 4 slices per person for decoration.
  14. Roughly chop the remaining cucumbers.
  15. Melt 2 tablespoons of butter in a saucepan.
  16. Add the chopped shallots or scallions to the melted butter and cook for a few minutes.
  17. Add the roughly chopped cucumbers to the saucepan.
  18. Add 1 teaspoon of wine vinegar to the saucepan.
  19. Pour in 1 quart of chicken stock or water (if using water, add a few more onions).
  20. Add 3 tablespoons of quick-cooking farina or cream of wheat to the saucepan.
  21. Add a pinch of salt and 1 tablespoon of dried dill weed to the saucepan.
  22. Simmer the cucumber soup for 20 minutes.
  23. Once the soup base has cooked, add the diced green beans, fresh green peas (if using), and diced zucchini (if using).
  24. Add a piece of stale white bread to the soup.
  25. Add 2 small handfuls of pasta or broken spaghetti to the soup.
  26. Add a pinch of saffron and pepper to taste.
  27. Taste the soup and adjust salt as needed.
  28. While the soup is simmering, prepare the pistou.
  29. Mince 4 cloves of garlic using a garlic press.
  30. Pound the minced garlic until it is nearly a purée.
  31. Add 1 tablespoon of fresh or bottled basil to the pounded garlic.
  32. Add 4 tablespoons of tomato paste to the garlic and basil mixture.
  33. Add 1/2 cup of grated Parmesan cheese to the mixture.
  34. Gradually beat in 1/2 cup of olive oil until the mixture is smooth.
  35. Once the green vegetables are half-cooked, add 3-4 tablespoons of canned beans (if using) to the soup.
  36. When the soup is ready to serve, add the pistou mixture to the soup tureen.
  37. Gradually stir the soup into the pistou mixture, beating with one hand and stirring with the other.
  38. Once most of the soup is mixed in, pour the remaining soup into the tureen.
  39. Garnish with fresh parsley (optional).
  40. Serve the soup immediately.
  41. Serve the cucumber soup hot or cold.
  42. Garnish the cucumber soup with cucumber slices, sour cream or fresh cream, and parsley.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6CnnDmSbz84

sourdough_starter.txt - Sourdough Starter

Objectives

  • Learn to make a sourdough starter with grapes, water, and flour.
  • Understand the process of fermentation and how to feed a starter.
  • Discover how to make a rustic loaf of bread and focaccia with the starter.

Ingredients

  • 1 pound of grapes
  • Cheesecloth
  • 1 cup of flour
  • 1 cup of water
  • Rustic Dough:
    • 1 cup bread flour
    • 1/2 cup sourdough starter
    • 1/4 teaspoon active dry yeast
    • 1/2 cup warm water
    • 1/4 cup milk
    • 1 tablespoon olive oil
    • 1 teaspoon salt
  • Focaccia:
    • Roasted vegetables (peppers, onions, tomatoes)
    • Goat cheese
    • Parmesan cheese
    • Fresh herbs (thyme, rosemary)
    • Poppy seeds
    • Sesame seeds
    • Olive bread:
      • 2 cups bread flour
      • 1/2 cup sourdough starter
      • 1/2 teaspoon fresh thyme
      • 1/4 cup wheat germ
      • 1/2 cup oil-cured Moroccan olives
      • 1/4 cup Kalamata olives
      • 1 cup warm water
      • 1 teaspoon salt

Instructions

  1. Tie up a pound of grapes in cheesecloth.
  2. Bash the grapes to release the juices.
  3. Mix 1 cup of flour with 1 cup of water to create a slurry.
  4. Submerge the grapes in the flour and water mixture.
  5. Cover the container and leave it at room temperature for a week.
  6. Observe the changes in the mixture throughout the week:
  7. Day 2: Slight separation with alcohol rising to the top.
  8. Day 4: Increased bubbling activity, cheese-like smell.
  9. Day 6: Grapes fully deflated, strong sour taste.
  10. Discard the grapes and squeeze out excess liquid.
  11. Feed the starter with 1/2 cup flour and 1/2 cup water.
  12. Cover and let sit in a warm place for 8-10 hours until active and bubbly.
  13. To make the rustic dough, combine all ingredients in a food processor and process for 1 minute until a ball forms.
  14. Let the dough rest for 5 minutes to absorb excess water.
  15. Reprocess the dough for a few seconds to finish kneading.
  16. Transfer the dough to a greased bowl, cover with plastic wrap, and let rise for 2 hours.
  17. Divide the dough in half.
  18. For the rustic loaf, transfer the dough to a piece of parchment paper dusted with flour and semolina.
  19. Cover with a linen cloth and let proof for 2 hours.
  20. Preheat oven to 500 degrees Fahrenheit.
  21. Lightly flour the top of the loaf with flour and semolina.
  22. Invert the loaf onto another piece of parchment paper.
  23. Bake the loaf directly on the parchment paper in the preheated oven.
  24. Spritz the oven with water to create a moist environment.
  25. Repeat the spritzing process every 10 minutes for the first 30 minutes of baking.
  26. After 30 minutes, remove the loaf from the oven and invert it, discarding the parchment paper.
  27. Continue baking for another 10 minutes.
  28. To check if the bread is done, smell the air for a baked bread aroma, observe the crust color, and knock the bottom of the loaf to listen for a hollow sound.
  29. Let the loaf cool completely before slicing.
  30. To make the focaccia, use a round cutter to cut out pieces of dough.
  31. Arrange roasted vegetables, herbs, and cheese on top of the focaccia.
  32. Bake the focaccia for 35-40 minutes.
  33. Serve the focaccia warm or let cool and slice in half for sandwiches.
  34. To make the olive bread, combine all ingredients in a food processor and process until a ball forms.
  35. Let the dough rest for 10 minutes.
  36. Process the dough for 20-30 seconds before adding the olives.
  37. Remove the dough from the bowl and knead by hand for a few minutes.
  38. Place the dough in a greased bowl, cover with plastic wrap, and let rise for 2-2.5 hours.
  39. Shape the dough into a boule by tucking the edges into the center.
  40. Place the shaped dough in a cloth-lined basket and cover with plastic wrap.
  41. Let the dough rise at room temperature for 2 hours.
  42. Refrigerate the dough overnight.
  43. The next day, turn the dough out onto a peel.
  44. Score the top of the loaf with a razor blade or sharp knife.
  45. Bake the loaf in a preheated oven at 500 degrees Fahrenheit for 45 minutes.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0C0CLTCC0NE

Objectives

spicy_shrimp_in_coconut_sauce.txt - Spicy Shrimp in Coconut Sauce

Objectives

  • Learn a traditional Indian recipe for spicy shrimp in coconut sauce.
  • Understand the importance of roasting spices for a deeper flavor.
  • Discover the unique characteristics of South Indian cuisine.

Ingredients

  • 2 tablespoons of coriander seeds
  • 1 teaspoon of black peppercorns
  • 1/4 teaspoon of fenugreek seeds
  • paprika (to taste)
  • cayenne pepper (to taste)
  • turmeric
  • 1/2 red pepper
  • 5 shallots
  • 1 inch of fresh ginger, chopped
  • 5 cloves of garlic
  • 2 tablespoons of water (for blending)
  • 8 cashew nuts, chopped
  • tamarind paste (soaked overnight)
  • 5 tablespoons of oil
  • 1 teaspoon of mustard seeds
  • curry leaves
  • 1 3/4 cups of water
  • 3/4 to 1 teaspoon of salt
  • 1 tablespoon of tamarind paste
  • 2 cups of Basmati rice
  • peanut oil or corn oil
  • 2 inch stick of cinnamon
  • 3 green cardamom pods
  • 1 shallot, sliced
  • 1 cup of chopped dill
  • 2 2/3 cups of chicken stock
  • 14 ounce can of coconut milk
  • 3-4 whole green chilies (for garnish)
  • 2 pounds of peeled and deveined shrimp

Instructions

  1. Heat a cast iron skillet over medium heat.
  2. Add 2 tablespoons of coriander seeds, 1 teaspoon of black peppercorns, and 1/4 teaspoon of fenugreek seeds to the skillet.
  3. Roast the spices until they begin to brown and release their aroma.
  4. Let the spices cool slightly and grind them into a fine powder using a coffee grinder.
  5. Combine the ground spices with paprika, cayenne pepper, and turmeric.
  6. Blend 1/2 red pepper, 5 shallots, 1 inch of chopped ginger, 5 cloves of garlic, and 2 tablespoons of water until smooth.
  7. Add 8 chopped cashew nuts and the spice mixture to the blender and blend until smooth.
  8. Strain the soaked tamarind paste through a sieve, pressing out the pulp.
  9. Heat 5 tablespoons of oil in a saucepan over medium-high heat.
  10. Add 1 teaspoon of mustard seeds to the hot oil and watch them pop.
  11. Add curry leaves to the oil and stir.
  12. Add the blended spice paste to the saucepan and sauté until it is lightly browned and aromatic.
  13. Add 1 3/4 cups of water, 3/4 to 1 teaspoon of salt, and 1 tablespoon of tamarind paste to the saucepan.
  14. Bring the sauce to a simmer and cook for 5 minutes.
  15. Strain the sauce through a coarse sieve to remove any remaining spice husks.
  16. Rinse 2 cups of Basmati rice several times until the water runs clear.
  17. Soak the rice in water for 30 minutes.
  18. Heat 2 tablespoons of oil in a pot over medium heat.
  19. Add a 2-inch stick of cinnamon, 3 green cardamom pods, and 1 sliced shallot to the hot oil.
  20. Sauté the spices until the shallot is browned.
  21. Add the soaked and drained rice to the pot.
  22. Reduce the heat to low and gently sauté the rice.
  23. Add 1 cup of chopped dill and 1 teaspoon of salt to the rice and continue to sauté.
  24. Add 2 2/3 cups of chicken stock to the rice and bring to a boil.
  25. Cover the pot with a piece of foil, followed by the lid, to create a tight seal.
  26. Transfer the pot to a 325° oven and bake for 25-30 minutes.
  27. While the rice is baking, heat the strained sauce in a saucepan over medium heat.
  28. Add 14 ounces of coconut milk to the sauce and stir until it is evenly combined.
  29. Add 3-4 whole green chilies to the sauce for garnish and bring to a boil.
  30. Add 2 pounds of peeled and deveined shrimp to the boiling sauce.
  31. Cook the shrimp until they are opaque and cooked through.
  32. Fluff the cooked rice with a fork.
  33. Serve the rice with the shrimp and sauce, garnished with 2 cooked chilies and a sprig of dill.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kPrLEC-umWE

spinach_timbale.txt - Spinach Timbale

Objectives

  • Learn to make a classic French spinach timbale
  • Master the technique of creating a savory custard
  • Utilize frozen spinach for a convenient and flavorful dish

Ingredients

  • 1 package frozen spinach
  • 2 tablespoons butter
  • 2 tablespoons chopped shallots
  • Salt to taste
  • Pinch of nutmeg
  • Freshly ground pepper to taste
  • 5 large eggs
  • 2/3 cup stale breadcrumbs
  • 1/2 cup grated Swiss cheese
  • 1 cup hot milk
  • 1/2 teaspoon salt
  • Additional pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Defrost the frozen spinach in a bowl of cold water.
  2. Drain the spinach thoroughly and squeeze out excess water.
  3. Chop the spinach finely.
  4. Melt butter in a saucepan over medium heat.
  5. Add chopped shallots and cook for a minute or two.
  6. Add chopped spinach to the saucepan and stir to combine.
  7. Season with salt, nutmeg, and pepper.
  8. Cook over low heat for 4-5 minutes until spinach is tender.
  9. In a separate bowl, whisk together eggs, breadcrumbs, Swiss cheese, and hot milk.
  10. Season with salt and pepper.
  11. Slowly stir in the cooked spinach to the egg mixture.
  12. Taste and adjust seasoning as needed.
  13. Butter a charlotte mold and line it with wax paper.
  14. Pour the spinach mixture into the mold, filling it to within a quarter inch of the top.
  15. Place the mold in a pan of water, ensuring the water level reaches a third to a half the way up the mold.
  16. Bake in a 350-degree oven for 30 minutes.
  17. To check for doneness, insert a knife into the center of the timbale. If it comes out clean, it is done.
  18. Unmold the timbale by inverting it onto a serving dish.
  19. Peel off the wax paper.
  20. Serve the timbale warm, with a sauce or as a side dish.

steak_cuts_and_cooking.txt - Steak Cuts and Cooking

Objectives

  • Learn about different beef cuts and where they come from on the carcass.
  • Understand how to identify and select high-quality steaks.
  • Learn two methods for cooking steak: a combination of sautéing and baking, and a classic French sauté.

Ingredients

  • 1 thick steak (1.5 inches or thicker)
  • 1 tablespoon olive oil
  • 1/2 teaspoon kosher or coarse salt
  • Italian seasoning or thyme (optional)
  • 1 tablespoon butter
  • Garlic cloves (optional)
  • Meat thermometer (optional)
  • 1/2 cup red wine or meat stock (for sauce)
  • 1 tablespoon butter (for sauce)
  • 1/4 cup chopped scallions or shallots (for sauce)
  • 1 teaspoon corn starch (for sauce)
  • 1/3 cup brandy (for flambéing)

Instructions

  1. Dry the steak thoroughly with paper towels.
  2. Heat olive oil in a flameproof pan over medium-high heat until almost smoking.
  3. Add the steak to the pan and brown on both sides for 2-3 minutes per side.
  4. Remove the pan from the heat and discard excess oil.
  5. Season the steak with salt, herbs, and a knob of butter.
  6. Add garlic cloves to the pan (optional).
  7. Preheat oven to 375 degrees Fahrenheit.
  8. Transfer the pan to the oven and bake for approximately 20 minutes.
  9. To check for doneness, insert a meat thermometer into the center of the steak.
  10. Alternatively, poke the steak with your finger: it should have slight resistance when it's medium-rare.
  11. Remove the steak from the oven and let it rest for 5-10 minutes before slicing.
  12. While the steak rests, make a sauce by deglazing the pan with red wine or meat stock.
  13. Simmer the sauce until it thickens, then stir in a knob of butter.
  14. Pour the sauce over the steak and serve.

strawberry_souffle.txt - Strawberry Souffle

Objectives

  • Learn to make a strawberry souffle using the Italian meringue method
  • Understand the importance of proper egg white beating and folding techniques
  • Master the art of creating a beautiful and delicious dessert

Ingredients

  • 4 egg whites
  • 1/4 teaspoon cream of tartar
  • Pinch of salt
  • 1/2 cup sugar
  • 3 tablespoons water
  • 1 1/3 tablespoons cornstarch
  • 2 cups strawberry puree (from 2 1-pound packages of frozen strawberries or 1 quart fresh strawberries)

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 425 degrees F (220 degrees C).
  2. Butter and sugar a 4-cup Charlotte mold or an 8-cup mold with a collar.
  3. Purée frozen or fresh strawberries through a food mill using the medium blade.
  4. In a bowl, beat egg whites with a hand beater until foamy.
  5. Add cream of tartar and a pinch of salt and continue beating until stiff peaks form.
  6. Make a sugar syrup by combining sugar and water in a saucepan and bringing to a boil, swirling the pan until the sugar dissolves.
  7. Boil syrup to the soft-ball stage (238 degrees F).
  8. Slowly beat the hot syrup into the egg whites until cool and thickened.
  9. Add cornstarch and beat until incorporated.
  10. Gently fold the strawberry purée into the meringue mixture.
  11. Pour the mixture into the prepared mold.
  12. Bake in the preheated oven for 35 minutes, reducing the temperature to 375 degrees F (190 degrees C) immediately after placing the soufflé in the oven.
  13. Test for doneness by inserting a skewer into the center; it should come out clean.
  14. Remove the collar and serve immediately with a raspberry sauce, if desired.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vEXtMBqLSM8

strawberry_tart.txt - Tarte de Fraises

Objectives

  • Learn to make a fresh strawberry tart using simple ingredients
  • Master the technique of creating a free-form pastry shell
  • Discover how to make a classic French pastry cream, crème pâtissière

Ingredients

Pastry Shell

  • 1 1/2 cups all-purpose flour
  • 1 stick (4 ounces) chilled butter
  • 3 tablespoons shortening
  • 1/4 teaspoon salt
  • 2 tablespoons sugar
  • 1/3 cup ice water

Apricot Glaze

  • 1 cup apricot jam
  • 2 tablespoons sugar

Pastry Cream (Crème Pâtissière)

  • 2 cups milk
  • 6 egg yolks
  • 1 cup granulated sugar
  • 1/2 cup all-purpose flour
  • 1 tablespoon vanilla extract
  • 1 1/2 tablespoons rum
  • 2 tablespoons butter

Assembly

  • Fresh strawberries
  • Lightly whipped cream (Crème Chantilly)

Instructions

  1. Prepare the Pastry Shell:
  2. Roll out the pastry dough into a long rectangle, about 1/8 to 3/4 inch thick.
  3. Place the dough on a buttered baking sheet.
  4. Fold up the edges of the dough to create a border.
  5. Use a ravioli wheel or other tool to even out the edges.
  6. Brush the border with cold water.
  7. Fold the side of the dough over itself to create a narrow edge.
  8. Use a fork to press the edges together and seal them.
  9. Prick the bottom of the pastry shell with a fork to prevent it from rising.
  10. Bake in a 425-degree oven for about 20 minutes, or until fully cooked.
  11. Make the Apricot Glaze:
  12. Sieve the apricot jam to remove any peel.
  13. Place the jam in a saucepan and heat over medium heat.
  14. Add 2 tablespoons of sugar for each cup of jam.
  15. Bring to a boil and cook until thickened and slightly clear, about 1-2 minutes.
  16. Allow the glaze to cool slightly.
  17. Waterproof the Pastry Shells:
  18. Brush the warm apricot glaze onto the inside of the baked pastry shells.
  19. This will prevent the shells from becoming soggy when filled with the strawberries.
  20. Make the Pastry Cream (Crème Pâtissière):
  21. Heat 2 cups of milk in a saucepan.
  22. In a separate bowl, beat 6 egg yolks with 1 cup of sugar until thick and pale yellow.
  23. Gradually whisk in 1/2 cup of all-purpose flour.
  24. Gradually whisk in the hot milk, being careful not to scramble the eggs.
  25. Pour the mixture back into the saucepan and cook over medium heat, stirring constantly.
  26. Bring to a boil and cook for 2-3 minutes, stirring constantly, until thickened and cooked through.
  27. Remove from heat and stir in 1 tablespoon of vanilla extract and 1 1/2 tablespoons of rum.
  28. Stir in 2 tablespoons of butter.
  29. Chill the pastry cream in the refrigerator.
  30. Assemble the Strawberry Tart:
  31. Spread a thin layer of chilled pastry cream in the bottom of the pastry shell.
  32. Arrange fresh strawberries on top of the pastry cream, filling the shell.
  33. Drizzle with apricot glaze.
  34. Serve immediately.

Tips: - You can use store-bought pastry dough if you prefer. - Use high-quality strawberries for the best flavor. - If you don't have apricot jam, you can use red currant jam. - Serve the strawberry tart with a dollop of lightly whipped cream (Crème Chantilly). - You can also add a splash of liqueur to the pastry cream, such as kirsch or Cointreau. - The strawberry tart can be made ahead of time and chilled in the refrigerator.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lDI5ZxDNtO8

stuffed_braised_bottom_round_of_beef.txt - Stuffed and Braised Bottom Round of Beef

Objectives

  • Learn to stuff and braise a bottom round of beef for a flavorful and impressive main course.
  • Discover the importance of proper browning and braising techniques for tenderizing tough cuts of meat.
  • Explore the art of pairing wines with different dishes, particularly with a focus on California wines.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole bottom round of beef (about 8 pounds)
  • 1/2 cup sautéed onions
  • 1/2 cup grated Swiss cheese
  • 1 cup fresh breadcrumbs
  • 2 eggs, beaten
  • 10 grinds of pepper
  • 3/4 teaspoon thyme
  • 1 teaspoon salt
  • 1/2 cup pork breakfast sausage
  • 1 cup carrots, lightly browned
  • 1 cup onions, lightly browned
  • 1/2 cup flour
  • 1 bottle red wine
  • 3 cups ripe red tomatoes, chopped
  • 1 herb bouquet
  • 4 cloves garlic, whole and unpeeled
  • 3 cups beef bouillon or homemade beef stock
  • Fat from the roast
  • 10-cup bowl
  • Raspberry jam, sieved
  • Yellow pound cake, cut into wedges
  • 1 cup Spanish sherry
  • 1/3 cup Spanish brandy
  • 9 egg yolks
  • 3/4 cup sugar
  • 2 1/4 cups hot milk
  • 1/3 cup heavy cream
  • 2 teaspoons pure vanilla extract
  • Kiwi fruit, sliced

Instructions

  1. Preheat oven to 325 degrees F (160 degrees C).
  2. Trim the fat from the bottom round of beef, leaving about an inch of meat on the outside.
  3. Cut a pocket in the beef from the top to almost the bottom.
  4. Remove the excess meat from the pocket and grind it into hamburger.
  5. Mix the ground beef with sautéed onions, Swiss cheese, breadcrumbs, beaten eggs, pepper, thyme, salt, and pork breakfast sausage.
  6. Taste the stuffing and adjust seasoning as needed.
  7. Stuff the beef with the mixture, pressing it in firmly to ensure it doesn't spill out.
  8. Truss the beef with butcher's twine.
  9. Place the beef on an oiled broiler pan.
  10. Oil the top of the beef to prevent cracking and seal in juices.
  11. Broil the beef for a few minutes, or until the top is nicely browned.
  12. While the beef is broiling, prepare the braising liquid.
  13. In a large pot, combine the lightly browned carrots and onions, flour, and red wine.
  14. Stir continuously over medium heat for about 5 minutes, or until the mixture is brown.
  15. Let the mixture cool slightly.
  16. Add the chopped tomatoes, herb bouquet, garlic, beef bouillon or stock, and the fat from the roast to the pot.
  17. Bring the liquid to a simmer.
  18. Place the beef in the pot, ensuring the liquid comes about halfway up the sides.
  19. Cover the pot and bake in the preheated oven for 2 1/2 hours, turning the beef every hour.
  20. While the beef is braising, prepare the trifle.
  21. In a 10-cup bowl, layer the raspberry jam, pound cake wedges, Spanish sherry, and Spanish brandy.
  22. Allow the cake to soak in the liquids while you prepare the custard.
  23. In a saucepan, whisk together the egg yolks and sugar until thickened.
  24. Gradually add the hot milk, whisking continuously to prevent scrambling the yolks.
  25. Cook the custard over low heat, stirring constantly, until thickened.
  26. Remove the custard from the heat and stir in the heavy cream and vanilla extract.
  27. Let the custard cool to tepid.
  28. Line a mold with kiwi fruit slices.
  29. Pour the cooled custard over the kiwi fruit.
  30. Cover the mold and refrigerate for several hours or overnight.
  31. Serve the braised beef with the chanterelles and the trifle.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XUUNFMVnLz8

stuffed_braised_veal_breast.txt - Stuffed Braised Whole Breast of Prime Veal

Objectives

  • Learn to prepare a stuffed braised whole breast of prime veal.
  • Understand how to trim and bone the veal breast.
  • Learn how to make a flavorful stuffing for the veal.

Ingredients

  • 1 whole breast of prime veal (approx. 13 lbs)
  • 2 cups of onions, chopped
  • 2 tablespoons of garlic, minced
  • Olive oil
  • 1 lb ground veal
  • 1 lb ground pork
  • Pistachios, whole
  • 1/2 cup bread crumbs
  • Pecorino cheese, grated
  • Marjoram, fresh
  • Thyme, fresh
  • Sage, fresh
  • Parsley, fresh (Italian)
  • 6 oz mortadella, diced
  • 3 oz provolone cheese, diced
  • Peas, cooked
  • Black pepper
  • Kosher salt
  • Marsala wine (approx. 3 cups)
  • Plum tomatoes, fresh or canned
  • Bay leaves
  • Browned chicken stock
  • Polenta (cornmeal mush)

Instructions

  1. Trim the excess fat from the veal breast, leaving some surface fat for basting.
  2. Cut off the first three ribs from the veal breast.
  3. Bone the veal breast by cutting a pocket along each rib, stopping about an inch from the end.
  4. Cut around the cartilage at the end of each rib.
  5. In a separate pan, sauté the onions and garlic in olive oil until softened.
  6. Combine the ground veal, ground pork, pistachios, bread crumbs, pecorino cheese, chopped herbs, mortadella, provolone cheese, and peas.
  7. Season the stuffing with salt, pepper, and a little olive oil.
  8. Stuff the veal breast with the prepared mixture, pressing it down firmly.
  9. Tie the veal breast together with butcher's twine.
  10. Season the outside of the veal breast generously with salt and pepper.
  11. Preheat oven to 400°F.
  12. Place the veal breast in a roasting pan and cook for 30 minutes, or until the top is nicely browned.
  13. Add the Marsala wine to the roasting pan and bring to a simmer.
  14. Add the plum tomatoes, herbs, bay leaves, and browned chicken stock to the roasting pan.
  15. Cover the roasting pan tightly with foil and place in the oven.
  16. Braise the veal breast for 4 hours.
  17. Remove the veal breast from the oven and let it cool slightly.
  18. Wrap the veal breast in foil and refrigerate overnight.
  19. To serve, reheat the veal breast in a 400°F oven.
  20. Ladle the braising sauce over the veal breast and garnish with fresh herbs.
  21. Serve with polenta.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=d6CIWfV96Cs

stuffed_turkey_leg.txt - Stuffed Turkey Leg

Objectives

  • Learn to bone a turkey leg and create a stuffing
  • Understand how to make a smooth, creamy mousse for the stuffing
  • Learn to cook and serve a stuffed turkey leg with grits and asparagus

Ingredients

  • 1 whole turkey
  • 1 tablespoon of olive oil
  • 1 teaspoon of salt
  • 1/2 teaspoon of black pepper
  • 1/2 cup of shiitake mushrooms, stems removed
  • 2 cloves of garlic, diced
  • 1 shallot, diced
  • 1/2 cup of heavy cream
  • 1 turkey tenderloin
  • 1/4 cup of Surry ham, diced
  • 1 tablespoon of chives, diced
  • 1 cup of stone-ground grits
  • 4 cups of chicken stock
  • 1 tablespoon of butter
  • 1 bunch of asparagus
  • 1/2 cup of veal stock
  • 1 sprig of rosemary

Instructions

  1. Remove the turkey legs from the carcass by making an incision along the natural break.
  2. Bend the leg down until the bone comes out and cut along the bone.
  3. Remove the breastbone by cutting along the center of the breast.
  4. Pull the flesh away from the bone with one hand and run the knife along the bone for a clean cut.
  5. Remove the wing joint by cutting straight down.
  6. Remove the tenderloin by pulling it apart and following the natural line with a sharp knife.
  7. Scrape away any small pieces of gristle from the tenderloin.
  8. Bone out one of the turkey legs by cutting along the natural line down the bone on both sides.
  9. Scrape the flesh away from the bone using the tip of the knife to expose the joint.
  10. Cut around the joint, keeping the knife pointing at the joint to avoid damaging the rest of the bird.
  11. Cut around the knuckle, removing the gristle.
  12. Rotate the leg in your hand as you scrape down the bone.
  13. Break the leg bone above the joint.
  14. Make a cut parallel to the cutting board on the thick portion of the leg to make it easier to stuff.
  15. Clean the cutting board before proceeding to the stuffing.
  16. Cut off the stems of the shiitake mushrooms and slice the caps.
  17. Heat olive oil in a cast-iron pan until smoking.
  18. Add the sliced shiitake mushrooms to the hot pan and stir constantly to prevent them from stewing.
  19. Dice the garlic and shallot.
  20. Add the garlic and shallot to the pan and stir constantly to prevent them from burning.
  21. Season with salt and freshly ground black pepper.
  22. Add a small amount of chicken stock to stop the cooking and add richness to the mushrooms.
  23. Let the mushroom mixture cool.
  24. Puree the tenderloin until smooth.
  25. Add an equal amount of heavy cream to the meat, by volume.
  26. Puree the mixture in spurts to prevent it from turning into butter.
  27. Scrape the sides of the bowl and puree again.
  28. Transfer the mousse to a bowl that has been sitting in ice water to keep it cold.
  29. Dice the Surry ham.
  30. Add the cooled mushroom mixture to the mousse.
  31. Add the diced ham to the mixture.
  32. Dice the chives.
  33. Add the chives to the mixture.
  34. Taste a small amount of the farce to adjust seasoning, especially salt.
  35. Season the boned turkey leg with salt and pepper.
  36. Stuff the turkey leg with the farce mixture, pushing it down to get as much in as possible.
  37. Wrap the turkey leg in pork caul fat or crepinette.
  38. Tie the turkey leg with butcher's twine to hold the stuffing in place.
  39. Heat a pan over medium heat and add a small amount of oil to prevent burning.
  40. Brown the turkey leg on one side.
  41. Rotate the leg to give it color on all sides.
  42. Place the turkey leg in a hot oven (500-550 degrees F) and rotate it once or twice for even cooking.
  43. Cook for about 25 minutes.
  44. Prepare the side dishes: grits and asparagus.
  45. Cook the asparagus in salted water until it loses its crunch.
  46. Reheat the asparagus in a skillet with butter before serving.
  47. Cook the stone-ground grits in chicken stock for 25 minutes.
  48. Use four times the amount of liquid to grits.
  49. Season the grits with salt and add butter.
  50. Let the grits rest for 10-15 minutes before serving.
  51. Let the turkey leg rest for 15 minutes to allow the temperatures to equalize and the juices to redistribute.
  52. Untie the turkey leg and carve it into slices.
  53. Warm the asparagus in a pan with butter.
  54. Add a touch of salt to the asparagus.
  55. Plate the turkey leg, grits, and asparagus.
  56. Drizzle the rosemary sauce over the turkey leg.
  57. Garnish as desired.
  58. Serve immediately.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OtNF65YwmDA

sunday_night_pasta_with_balsamic_vinegar.txt - Sunday Night Pasta with Balsamic Vinegar

Objectives

  • Learn a quick and easy pasta recipe perfect for a busy Sunday night.
  • Understand how to cook garlic slowly to bring out its sweetness.
  • Discover the difference between true balsamic vinegar and industrial balsamic vinegar.

Ingredients

  • 10 cloves garlic
  • 3 tablespoons olive oil
  • 1 pound dried pasta (rough texture)
  • 4-5 ripe tomatoes
  • 3 tablespoons chopped chives
  • 3 tablespoons chopped mint
  • 3/4 cup packed basil leaves
  • 6 quarts water
  • 1 1/2 - 2 tablespoons salt
  • 1/2 cup pasta water
  • 1/4 cup balsamic vinegar (true balsamic)
  • Shaved Parmesan Reggiano cheese (to taste)
  • Salt and pepper to taste

Instructions

  1. Dice 10 cloves of garlic into large pieces.
  2. Heat a large pan over very low heat.
  3. Add 3 tablespoons of olive oil to the pan.
  4. Add the diced garlic to the pan and cook for 10-15 minutes, or until softened and slightly blond.
  5. While the garlic cooks, prepare the remaining ingredients.
  6. Cut tomatoes in half and remove the seeds.
  7. Dice the tomatoes into half-inch pieces.
  8. Chop the chives, mint, and basil leaves.
  9. Bring 6 quarts of water to a boil.
  10. Taste the boiling water and add 1 1/2 - 2 tablespoons of salt, or until the water tastes salty enough.
  11. Add the pasta to the boiling water and stir to prevent sticking.
  12. Cook the pasta until al dente, stirring occasionally.
  13. Heat the garlic and olive oil mixture over medium heat.
  14. Add 1/2 cup of pasta water to the pan and bring to a simmer.
  15. Add the herbs to the pan and warm through.
  16. Drain the pasta and add it to the pan with the herbs and garlic.
  17. Add the diced tomatoes to the pan and toss to combine.
  18. Add shaved Parmesan cheese to the pan and toss to combine.
  19. Season the pasta with salt and pepper to taste.
  20. Serve immediately.
  21. Garnish with additional shaved Parmesan cheese, diced tomatoes, and basil leaves if desired.
  22. Drizzle a spoonful of balsamic vinegar over the pasta before serving.

tamale_mole_verde.txt - Mole Verde and Tamales

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a traditional Mexican Mole Verde.
  • Understand the importance of roasting ingredients for flavor.
  • Learn two methods for making tamales: with corn husks and banana leaves.

Ingredients

Mole Verde:

  • 10-12 Tomatillos (soaked in cold water for 1 hour)
  • 1 Poblano Chile
  • 3 Garlic cloves
  • 1 Onion (coarsely chopped)
  • 3 Tablespoons of Parsley (Italian)
  • 3 Tablespoons of Epazote
  • 1 Teaspoon of Salt
  • 1/2 Cup of Water
  • 1 Tablespoon of Masa Harina
  • 1 Tablespoon of Lard (or oil)
  • 1 Teaspoon of Sugar (optional)

Tamales (Corn Husk):

  • 2 Cups of Chicken Stock
  • 2 Cups of Masa Harina
  • 1 Pound of Lard
  • 2 Tablespoons of Salt
  • 1 Cup of Mole Verde
  • 1 Cup of Queso Fresco (fresh cheese)
  • Corn husks (soaked in hot water for 30 minutes)

Tamales (Banana Leaf):

  • 2 Cups of Chicken Stock
  • 2 Cups of Masa Harina
  • 1 Pound of Lard
  • 2 Tablespoons of Salt
  • Banana leaves (soaked in hot water for 30 minutes)

Filling:

  • 1 Onion
  • 2 Garlic cloves
  • 1 Poblano Chile
  • 1 Cup of Fresh Corn (taken off the cob)
  • Cilantro
  • 1/2 Cup of Pork
  • Red Chile Sauce (made with water, peppercorns, and garlic)

Instructions

  1. Roast the tomatillos and poblano chile on a hot griddle for 10 minutes (tomatillos) and 8 minutes (chile), turning them frequently to ensure even cooking.
  2. While the tomatillos and chile are roasting, prepare the other ingredients for the mole verde: peel the garlic cloves, coarsely chop the onion, measure out the parsley, epazote, salt, and water.
  3. In a blender, combine the roasted tomatillos, poblano chile, garlic cloves, onion, parsley, epazote, salt, water, and masa harina. Blend until smooth.
  4. Heat a pan over medium heat and add 1 tablespoon of lard or oil.
  5. Pour the mole verde mixture into the pan and cook, stirring occasionally. Add a teaspoon of sugar to balance the tartness of the tomatillos, if desired.
  6. While the mole verde is cooking, prepare the tamale dough: combine 2 cups of chicken stock, 2 cups of masa harina, 1 pound of lard, and 2 tablespoons of salt in a large bowl.
  7. Beat the tamale dough with an electric mixer until it is light and fluffy.
  8. Divide the tamale dough in half. Mix one half with the mole verde.
  9. For the corn husk tamales, soak the corn husks in hot water for 30 minutes.
  10. For the banana leaf tamales, soak the banana leaves in hot water for 30 minutes.
  11. To assemble the corn husk tamales, place a spoonful of the mole verde tamale dough in the center of a corn husk. Fold the husk over the dough, creating a package.
  12. To assemble the banana leaf tamales, place a larger amount of the plain tamale dough in the center of a banana leaf. Fold the leaf over the dough, creating a package.
  13. Place the tamales in a steamer basket or a pot with a rack.
  14. Steam the tamales for 45 minutes.
  15. To serve, remove the tamales from the steamer and let them cool slightly.
  16. Garnish the tamales with mole verde sauce and a sprinkle of corn filling.

Video: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gu8e94ZKohQ

bacheofe.txt - Bacheofe

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a traditional Alsatian Tarte Flambee
  • Understand the importance of using thin pastry and ingredients
  • Discover the history and origins of the dish

Ingredients

  • Puff pastry (7 ounces)
  • Cottage cheese (1/2 cup)
  • Crème fraiche (1/2 cup)
  • Flour (1 tablespoon)
  • Salt (to taste)
  • Pepper (to taste)
  • Oil (2 tablespoons)
  • Bacon (thinly sliced)
  • Onion (thinly sliced)

Instructions

  1. Roll out the puff pastry very thin.
  2. Cut the pastry into four pieces or leave as one large piece.
  3. Lightly oil a baking pan and prick the pastry with a fork.
  4. Refrigerate the pastry.
  5. In a bowl, combine cottage cheese, crème fraiche, flour, salt, pepper, and oil.
  6. Cut the bacon very thin.
  7. Cut the onions very thin.
  8. Sauté the bacon in a pan until lightly browned, then add the onions and cook until softened.
  9. Spread the cream mixture over the pastry, leaving a small border.
  10. Top with the bacon and onion mixture.
  11. Bake in a preheated oven until the pastry is golden brown and the filling is set.
  12. Serve warm.

Objectives

  • Learn how to make a traditional Alsatian Bacheofe
  • Understand the importance of using a variety of meats and marinating them
  • Discover the history and origins of the dish

Ingredients

  • Beef chuck (1 piece)
  • Pork butts (1 piece)
  • Lamb shoulder (1 piece)
  • Pork feet (1 piece)
  • Pork tail (1 piece)
  • Onion (1 large)
  • Garlic (1 clove)
  • Bouquet garni (thyme, parsley, bay leaf)
  • Salt (to taste)
  • Pepper (to taste)
  • White wine (enough to cover the meat)
  • Potatoes (cut thin)
  • Flour (for sealing the pot)
  • Water (for sealing the pot)

Instructions

  1. Cut the beef, pork, and lamb into large pieces.
  2. Cut the onion into slices.
  3. Cut the garlic in half and remove the germ.
  4. Combine the meat, onion, garlic, bouquet garni, salt, pepper, and white wine in a bowl.
  5. Marinate the meat in the refrigerator overnight.
  6. Cut the potatoes into thin slices.
  7. Wash the potatoes thoroughly.
  8. Slice the onions thinly, removing the core.
  9. Layer half of the potatoes in the bottom of a large Dutch oven.
  10. Season with salt and pepper.
  11. Add the marinated meat on top of the potatoes.
  12. Cover the meat with the remaining potatoes and onions.
  13. Season with salt and pepper.
  14. Strain the marinade over the ingredients.
  15. Add a little more white wine if needed.
  16. Seal the pot with a paste made from flour and water.
  17. Cover the pot tightly with a lid.
  18. Bake in a preheated oven for 2 1/2 hours.
  19. Serve hot, garnished with parsley.
